O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh ye children, dear ones, I have completed this book which is the follow-up to the knowledge of medicine, putting into practice what was written within it, and have finished the end through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is twisted and distorted in our region and is strange throughout all its parts, it has lost the science and understanding, and there remains only what is left of fire, namely small descriptions in books of the ancients who had moved their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arose errors and foolishnesses, and the intentions were shut, and the knowledge was separated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will live and thrive according to the order of this treatment in accordance with the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I have come together the forms of cauterization tools and other instruments of work with the adjustment of declaration and preparation for them, just as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of this that there are no good masters of hands to be found in our time, the art of medicine has been extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is fitting for one who enters into this that he should study anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the measure of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and knowledge of bones and nerves and joints and the number of joints, and the movement and stillness of veins, and their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this Hippocrates says that the bone with no nails is much, and the one with the scar is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	So we say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not familiar with what is being said, should beware lest he falls into error and hurts men; thus I have often sought out those who intervene in this knowledge and abandon it, for lack of understanding and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a mad doctor who cut an abscess on the shoulder of a woman, and cut the arteries in the neck; because from that much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another doctor who treated a large stone from an old man, and he carried away a part of the bladder with it; and died within three days in his own home.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have seen that they called it a cure, and saw the state of the patient and the size of the wound, and knew well whether the person would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And then I saw another treatment where they cut the cure of our land who had broken his leg, and with the break got an injury; and the physicians ignorant of how to treat it stretched the break on the wound with stitches tightly sewn, and did not leave the wound at all, and thus ended up as I described; and he commanded that he should not be freed from it; and stayed in this state until his leg was completely numb and his foot came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to free his leg; and when I saw it dislocated he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all corruption is already confirmed in the member, and cannot be cured; and the corruption does not cease to go down into the member until the member is entirely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there are other treatments that will collapse the abscess, enslave it, and then inflame it through the evil of its power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humour, does not require that it be touched with iron unless it is in its place, for one can remove all what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that work of hands is divided into two divisions: this is to say, whether there is danger in one or more situations; and I will show you in each of these chapters where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason you must guard yourselves, so that the fools may not speak ill of you. If you take up your arms in comfort, and gently yet firmly, and use the better way so that through God's grace you come to salvation and are praised; and leave off fearful diseases from weakness of health; and put away the things that make you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you can come from this world to the other world of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Gauls wrote in some of their warnings: "Do not take care for a bad disease, lest you be called a fool doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this book according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cautery and acid cautery, and they are arranged from head to toe; and the forms of dressings, and iron instruments for cautery, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and ventouses, wounds, extractions of arrows, and similar things. And the chapters are ordered and described in the forms of discharges.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things. And it is ordered to have the shoulder joint just as it was before, and described in the forms of discharges.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we have remembered the work, it is necessary that I tell you about the quality of aid and the harm of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and the harm are the longest words and subtle science and hidden answers. And the wise men speak about them and agree on them. And they forgive me for my lengthy words because I am long-winded.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire cautery helps universally for every complexion whatever the matter is, whether it is cold with matter or dry with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the cold and dry complexion with matter combined, some said there was no difference and said that fire cautery is great help; but the others said that fire cautery is of little value to diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated for hot diseases by heat or dryness, but rather this one who says the contrary that fire cautery helps greatly in hot and dry disease that comes into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you purchase the body of man and its moisture is at the hot complexion, you find the body frozen.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this phrase.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it no other way by experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And no path should be entered by fire except for him who has experienced it, and who knows through long use the art of cautery, and the diversity of human conditions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and remedies and space to take treatment; for other conditions we have little fear, themselves in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all physicians agree and concur on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that cautery is made from fire so much as it is a part of the remedies, and has more beneficial effect than burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire cautery, it is simple, and fire comes only to the member that is burned, and not to any other member unless its name is spoken.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Medicines that burn come from one member to another when they are removed, and bring disease into the healthy member; and by chance, the fire does not occur on the sick person due to its high heat and the goodness of its substance, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this is what I have found by experience and through long study and service, and it was known beforehand; and for that reason I excuse myself from the length of the word, because it does not please me to reveal to you the secret which is gained with fire, and the quality of the work, how it debouts the diseases of the body, as the philosopher said by demonstrating; so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And you must know, son, when they are agreed on what times the cauterizations should be done, and they pray to God.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is convenient in all times, because the evil sicknesses are drawn out from below with the aid of cauterization; and even if the cauterizations cause pains and hardships that no one can bear until greater evils come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think ever, dear son, how they say the physicians; for a disease cured by cauterization has no return, and he says so thus; but it is not quite as they claim, because cauterizations are not just medicine that moves the complexion, and dries out the humors that cause pain, but rather more of a medicine because of its rapid value, and through the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes once according to the constitution of the patient and their natural state and virtue; and they are assembled in him the excesses through the acquisition of food and such things, if you do not administer cauterization to them when they have little excess and moisture, as cauterization for pain and such things, because this does not return with much pain; but it happens seldom.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the rear of medicine, and it's seen; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine, but their opinions are false, and cauterization is the rear of medicine because when we administer various kinds of cures in any disease and they do not work, then we must give them cauterization, and it is valuable.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And so let it be understood that fire cautery is the hindrance of medicine, not according to the intentions of mad men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more effective than with iron, and they claimed this because of the quality of gold and its high substance; but they did not say it was thus because of fire alone, for I have tried both and found that it is so in some men; cautery with gold is more effective than iron.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And beware, for when you heat an instrument of gold, you know not whether it is spoiled by the color of gold and cooling down afterwards; and if it is heated too much, they say it must be done at the fire; and so there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we shall use fire cautery which we have used before, in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	For which reason we have ordered this chapter on the head, because the vein is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	to apply olive oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful in moist and cold places on the head, because of "soda" which is caused by many diseases, such as a fall out from an excess of humors that pour into the head and ears, and the throat, and because of many dreams and pain of teeth and pain of the gullet, and themselves all kinds of diseases that come from cold so like paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by medicine solute, manifesting the head in three or four ways, according to what virtues and humors and accustomed habit of the patient can bear; and then reapply the head to the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit, cross his legs between your hands, and place his hands on a soft surface; after putting the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and when it comes to those two middle fingers, if it bleeds from the needle, then put the cautery called "olivare", because this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put on the left side of his signet ring with ink, and do so in descending and extracting your hand little by little, turning it around; then lift your hand slowly, and reapply the cauterization as long as you see the bone so small; if you don't see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone like I told you to; after take a bit of silk, apply it in oil and soft cotton inside, and place on the wound, and let him rest for three days; after put on a moist cloth in butter; and let it stay until he has lost the oozing; after cure the wound of inflammation which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until he is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And when they said the old ones, that as long as the wound stays open longer, it will purge more; and therefore he takes medicine.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of these said that you must cool the cautery so much of the bone is burned, and then put back what has been burned by the bone, and cure.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say another thing, you must cool the cautery so much that it is applied above, and push so hard as you lower down to bone, as large as the size of a green thread which women put in their wounds for that reason the humors go out quickly; and after you have cooled the wound long time, then cure and bleed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in all respects, for fire which is used by some men gives them no peace; and I think it would be better to leave [the method] alone; because the bones are weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have shown in other members; and so too when the joints of the sick person are weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more safe and soothing for me; that's why I prefer one over the other.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When pain of the head is chronic and lasts for a long time, if the patient uses the medicine called "cochie", and purgatives of the head, oils, and plasters; and if they do the cautery that we have previously mentioned, it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Before doing so if the patient's head is of strong nature and not too cold; then cut with that same cautery as we previously mentioned.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After applying cautery to each corner of the head where the bone is, as we previously mentioned, and apply the cautery that they call "vasselz"; and it's the one that you put ventouses on; and align your hand so that you don't see anything around the bone: the patient feels much more intense pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about that later; and it is fitting that the cauterize of the corners be more subtle than those of the earliness of the chief, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	burning of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is sudden pain in one part of the head, and the disease spreads to the oil (i.e. the scalp), and the chills are purged with medicinal herbs, and other treatments have been done as I have said in the division of diseases, but they do not help: then it must be done cautery according to two kinds, namely by the use of hot medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery by hot medicine is done as follows: you take an ounce of fat, remove the scab and apply it on top of the two joints, and then make a cut on the temple in such a way that you can put the fat back under the skin; and when you have done so, tie it tight and leave it for 12 hours; and then untie it and treat with hot fat the same amount as before, leaving the wound for 2 or 3 days; then cover it with a cloth soaked in lard until it is healed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of wounds until it is healed; and if you see, then do what I have written about any burning medicine that I have prescribed or ordered to treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of what kind it is that has this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a clover or has little bird poop, and in its middle there is a small appearance; and put on the painful place, take hold with your hand and twist the iron gently until the moisure of the blood that is drawn is cooled; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is away from it, and bleed abundantly with blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Instruct the patient to apply cotton in awe of silk, and put a cloth on the shoulder for three days; then, put cotton soaked in butter, and cure the wound until it is healed. And if you want to cauterize this swelling with the cautery called "cultellare" at its entire tip, be careful not to cover the artery in that swelling which is not old.
de emigraine	of a lump or swelling
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure the swelling as we have said in our division of diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery previously described by medicine and iron did not bring relief, then it is necessary to heat up the "cultellare" cautery until it is white; and so apply oil on the shoulder with a line of half an inch long, and hold your hand once, and strain yourself so as not to cover the artery, and do not let it grow in close proximity to the bone. Be careful that the mouth does not move while eating, and the nerves have no sensation but numbness and spasms, and be aware of the risk of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is a great fear of its cutting, for those who are not skilled and experienced; and let the swelling remain for a time. But I will tell you how to keep the wound when the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If the fire cautery does not work well on the disease, and the patient suffers greatly, cauterize the area near the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter of cutting out an artery, with the cautery having two cuts; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	from the pain in the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear comes from coldness, and you have tried medicines that dissolve and other treatments we have said regarding cutting, and the pains do not cease, then apply this cautery called "pins," for it is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pricking all around the diseased ear, or around both sides where the pain holds, and you move a small distance from the root of the ear towards the bone once you have marked the point with a needle; and apply X points all around each ear; after cure it until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	From the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cautery should not be done with those that move due to fever, just as we have said in the divisions of the disease; and do not do cautery on swellings that come from oozing and pus of wounds.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this resemblance of torture that is quiet from fever and discharge and swelling of the head and gargareme, and so it seems worth doing cautery to the patient: one in the root of the ear, and another just in front of the temple, and the third in the jointing of the two lips; and put the cautery on the side that is healthy, and do direct cautery on the forehead of the ear above a little beneath the cornual part of the head, and another in the temple as long as our finger; and let the cautery stay up until the discharge of the heat be dried; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the appearance of the cutlery that we have placed before you, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the cuts be a little thicker; after care, let him do so as I said, until he is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it in this way, and he does not benefit from it, and the patient has no fever, then do IV cauteries: II on the II corners of the head, and I on the head itself, and I on the "vasselz" (which we have said to be like), and one cautery on the skin of the stomach; and treat him in this way as we have said before.
de litargie	Of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness it is necessary to give the patient large and pounded pills for the brain; after, let him take a head made of the patient, and place upon the occipital bone the plaster of senna which is written in the way of treating plasters; and this is the manner of cautery: if he does so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy thus, then good is; and if not so, the three cauteries of the forehead in the lower part around the neck will be done, with two spaces between each cautery one of which is large. And the cure will be as the others, and if you see anything to add, and the patient suffers, then one cautery in the middle will be done; and for those who are skilled, two others above on the two horns, and the cure until they are healthy; and let the cauteries which are called "olivare" be done, as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary to cleanse the head with years and what we have said before; after receiving the head from the sick person, then do cautery around the head and on each horn, and I in front and III above the spine of the neck; and if you have more need, and the body is moist and the patient suffers, and the disease is severe, then do four cauteries above the spine of the back; and let it be done until he gets a good cure, and lift your hand; after the cure, as long as he becomes healthy, and let the cauteries which are called "olivare" that we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The physicians should use cauterization with fire only on those who are spongy, and it is recommended to first sterilize the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and suffers greatly from pain from medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer, then make gargarism and mastication sterilizing the brain frequently with bones meat; after putting the head in a space, and making cauterization according to what we have said before, and cauterizing on the neck, and on each horn; and if the patient is fierce and suffers greatly, make cauterizations as I told the one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and so make cauterizations with olive oil according to the way I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, then if he makes me cautery subtle according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy there are fluxes or moistures corrupted and big phlegm, then do the cautery on body parts as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the fluxes decline to melancholy, and the body of the sick person is moistened, then he should drink something by which his brain may be cleansed, according to what it is in front of him in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After returning the head of the sick person; after doing the piece of linen well made, in the shape of a circle, if you put it on the head; and the patient lies crossways, and are kept tightly from all parts; after presenting the linen, and using mus of barme of ancient goat fat; and the heat is tempered in fire, so that it may be poured on him when he can suffer; after voiding the circle by inside the head, and letting it cool down; and doing this to each sick person once a week with another good government, until they are sane.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see this being cauterized when doing multiple punctures to the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization increases the inflammation of the brain; and then put on a moist cloth in butter and beef fat.
de l’awe des eulz	Of the blood of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When blood comes first to the eyes according to the signs I've said in division, then start and do as follows: make the patient drink something purifying the head, and ward off all moisture, and let him sweat or take baths multiple times.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After the command to see his head, and make cauterize it around the scalp, and make two cauterizations on both temples when there is bleeding in both eyes together, or in one if there is; and strike all over the cautery at all veins and arteries under the wound, and so cauterize long according to the length of the temple; and ward off the complication of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, so pinch with great force as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and by incision, how to caution when you extract them; and never once did a cautery or hatterel done below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	with the force of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or when you cut at the arteries that appear on the face outside; and one sees that it's from superfluous cold humors, then do the cautery as I said in the beginning, descending under the eyes: I cut the forehead, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries below the two bones; and if there is need more, so cautery with a small amount of cauterizing over the eyebrow at all.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	out of the eyes through the eyelids
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you give medicine according to what we have said in the division, and he does not profit from it, then give him three bitter medicines; after the king, his head, and cauterize with a cautery olive oil; and do two cauteries of cautery which are called "clavilis" on the two sores, one below the eyebrows.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the oil paper is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	If you see such a thing do the fire cautery on the two swellings just as long as the swellings are; and do not put out the hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	a single hair that pricks at its root.
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	There is never the case that the hairs of the swellings are converted to being tender, and pricking at their root, and then one does cautery according to two manners: namely by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then put the patient in a bed; after that, on paper of the eyes, draw a figure like as the fuelle of myrtle, and like the beginning of the sign of the hairs; then put cotton wet with oil and musk and perruches upon the cautery of which is this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cautering on the figure that you have drawn a little bit, a little more each time, so the color of the hairs is at the right place; and the signs of the good health of the work are that you see the paper pulled in, and the hairs raised to the tip of the oil; then let go your hand, and leave thus for III days, then put cotton wet in butter until the cautery is removed; after the cure of ointment until he is cured.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	If the hairs grow after this, and the paper is softened then reapply the cautery on the same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are fallen off, apply the cautery until the paper rises to its natural place, and is even, and does not prick the hair.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medicine cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a parchment shape like the leaves of myrtle; then take French soap and live charcoal each one .2; crush them together well; and apply quickly, if it does not cool down, then place on the forehead in the same shape as the leaf of myrtle, and put on the paper of the eyes; and if the patient is affected only by the oil, do it with the left hand, and also with the right; and underneath the oil, put cotton wool soaked in olive oil on the arm of your healthy hand, and show your two fingers above the medicine, and press it into the flesh every time the patient feels the stinging of the medicine, for he feels it just as if by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the doctor says so.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the swelling has passed, lift the limb away, and if you see that the swelling is lifted just as it was lifted by constraint of fire or by incision; and if so, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not so, then put again the medicine on the limb or if it has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes are fixed; then put on cotton soaked in butter until the wounds are closed, after applying a cure called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary that you take care of your work by great caution, so that the medicine does not touch your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes moldy after that, and they prick at it in oil, then resume the medicine on that person who has become soft with pure paper, just as you did before; until the cure is complete, and this is the form of a gentle poultice.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to their condition; do not be replied with the straight path to him who has the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cauterization.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula in the manner we have said in our division of diseases, and your treatments do not bring benefit; then it is necessary to cauterize him according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head on a clean cloth; and bind the meniscus with his head between your hands in such a way that he does not move nor does his head change place; after putting moist cotton wool or persillade juice on oil, heat the cautery so that it is shaped like an arrowhead, assembled so that they are bound together; if you see, so it will be marked from one to the other, and if you see, so it will be as if a tent; but however, this which is shaped as a value is suitable for your service.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the abscess so that it bursts open and takes out the pus and dries it; if it is closed again, then sew, and take fire at the bow of the arrow; after putting on the heated cautery in the shape, hold your hand to the cautery at the part where it has no nerve below the oil, lest your hands go mad; and put the cautery into the fat of the oil, so that it becomes corrupted.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just before the bone, it would be better.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If that is not the case, you must begin again once more. And if it is needed again, then put on coton soaked in butter and apply the dry dressing of ointment until it is healed. If forty days pass without healing, then put on medicine to dissolve the corrosive so that the bone may be uncovered; and have the king as prescribed according to what he came to his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a manner of cautery for a fistula that none of the ancients have said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And understand that the fistula and cut it; afterwards put in the wound a canthar (or camphan) subtle of which this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	Instruct the patient to take half a pint of plaster; and hold your hand firmly in place, so that the patient does not move at all, until the plaster is cooled and stops bleeding; it is best to put cotton wool soaked in vinegar or oil on the wound: the plaster will act as a fistula, and the clean one will be restored through marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, it is best to apply poultices on the wound, and return the fistula to its proper place in the body according to what is necessary in his own person.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are fissures on the lips called "poil", and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fissures as we have said in division, and the cure is not effective, then take a small cautery knife of the kitchen utensil form.
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it immediately in those fissures until the juice flows out, then apply a poultice of ceruse to make him whole.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess from the throat.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the uvula, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has putrefied and dried up and become a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not heal: then it is good that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; after removing the dead tissue from the fistula, hold your hand until the iron needle enters the root, or into the bone; and do so once or twice, after the treatment as we have said in cures, until he is whole; and if it heals thus, that's good; but if not, then it is best to discover the root and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in your book.
dou movement des dens	A joint moves out of its place
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines, but it doesn't work, then place the head of the patient on a clean cloth; after burn the cautery which will come out afterwards in this manner that you put a metal rod on the tooth; and put hot cauterization inside it tightly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after lift your hand and resume the cautery according to your will; after fill the patient's mouth with vinegar and salt, and boil it for an hour and a rich fire.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the teeth that were moving are fixed, and the gums softened are held back, and the moistures are corrupted and dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the toothache comes from coldness, or there is coldness in the eye, and medicines do not help, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two ways: and cauterization with butter and fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter if it is done so that you take butter from the cheek, and press it onto a iron spoon or linen; after taking cotton and covering up the point of a cloth, and let the pus in butter boil, and put on the painful tooth quickly and hold until it cools; and do this many times until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and see if mole and cotton in butter freeze, and put on the tooth, and put iron hot enough so that the fire comes to the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Instruct the patient to put on a fire cautery made from iron or linen, and one that is large enough so that the heat does not come to the mouth of the sick person; after cooling down the cautery, it will form in its place afterwards, and you should put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools off. Do this often, because the pain will be gone on the same day or the next day itself.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is fitting that the sick person fills his mouth with good butter in the haste of applying the cautery, and then raises his face; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery on his head whatever you like, and according to your skill; and this is the form of the iron (or linen):
des scrophules	Of swellings
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swellings are of pus and cold moistures, and do not yield to digestion by medicine, then apply the cautery to the hair, because this comes after; and take away the openings for the pus to come out from the other side; and put the cautery hot on the abscess once, or until it is ready, so long as it comes to a boil of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply cautery according to its size, and let it be so for three days; and cover with moistened cotton wool in butter until the dressing falls off; after cure take away the limbs and bandages until he is sane.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the wound:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistors conquer on the channels of the pormon, and myself when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the sick be voided first by soluble medicines; after that, make cautery to the root of the throat, and keep in mind that you do not come near the throat again, and burn with fire but a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the first cautery to the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and the cauteries which are called "clavicle", since we have the form before, cure the patient as we have said until he is healed.
de la toust	of the throat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all diseases of pormon are caused by cold moistors, and the patient has no fever or drying up, and the disease is ancient, make two cauteries on the testicles in the joints; and another cautery on the flesh between the two mammary glands; and make the cauteries which are called "clavicle" as we have said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, do cautery by pricking at the whole cautery called "points" because of which the shape is as before in the disease of the ears; and let the points be just at thirty-three or near.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the treatment according to what has been said, and let the cauterizations be three in number according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because they are lighter for that reason, for you do three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After sovining the patient above his back and on his costeit; after relieving the wound which is inside the titlet as due to your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, take the cautery which has two pointed ends here in this form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	And cauterize the wound so that it goes all along his back side, and the flesh comes out with the joint together four cauteres; and because of this, a cautery is made with the cautery having three points, for the figures of cauterization are these cauteres; they are like nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and that's the form of the cautery having three points:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is joined back onto this nerve because there are eight cauteres.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Instruct the patient to put on the cauterization tool, a sharp bronze rod with a cord, after which he should rest and do not allow the limbs to be exposed for a long time until they are well recovered.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if a dislocation occurs because of the fall, then do a cauterization on the thick bone of the shoulder joint with a sharp cauterization tool or many cauterizations with pointed instruments.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed and there are bones swollen with moisture, and healing of the patient.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When colds come to the stomach and many moistures until they are extracted from his body and there are multiple purging in him, and he does not benefit from the usual remedies, then it is necessary for the patient to lie on his back and stretch out his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Instruct the cauterist to make 3 cauteries I under the nail of the finger by the quantity of two fingers' width all over the cautery knife, and 2 cauteries on either side as long as the figure of the cautery is at three angles, and has a space between them so they are not joined together when they rot; and make the cautery such that it pricks the 2 parts of the flesh, and be the figure of the cautery according to this form next to it.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see a great cautery applied to the belly according to this form; and if one has fear of this cautery, apply it by pricking and point to the belly at that very spot, according to the quantity you have seen before, then apply the cautery all over what is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment we had before, so long as it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As for the liver, pain comes from cold and moisture and great swelling, so long as it is put into its natural condition through the surplus; and the sick are cured of this according to what we have said in divisions, and they do not profit from it if the patient should be covered up with his own heat; sign of three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, excluding the hypochondriacs, to the left at the cost of the gallbladder comes; and there is space between each cautery the swelling of a doth (dough); and the cauteries should be long in the body, and not press too hard with the hand all along the cautery; and let them burn only the moist parts of the kiss; and let the patient stand straight above his feet; and if he cannot, so let him sit, and extend his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If your will is, then cauterize these cauteries with the cutlery, if you are subtle and wise in this art, and beware that you do not burn all the flesh, because you would dry out all the body; and lest it come to boiling, for the flesh is very subtle near the end, and the knowledge of how to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you see if it is on the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is on the flesh, he feels the patient some pain but not very strong; and if it is in the membrane, he feels a very painful feeling.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure requires the application of poultices, it is best that the patient lies on his back; and then apply the hot poultice to where the abscess is, and then heat the cauterized part which is similar in shape.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Instruct the fire cautery so that the hairs are burned, and it comes just before syphilis, so that the pruritus is completely free; after the cure according to the cure of ulcers, until the patient is healed; and it is not suitable to use any fires from this cautery except those handled by someone who has studied long in the art of medicine, and whose hands have cured these diseases some time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And then he can work with great courage; and it seems to me that it is worth leaving.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the cauterization of pleurisy.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleurisy one must cauterize with the roots of Aristole, and in this manner: take a long root of Aristole, as large as you can find, dry it, and so large and so long as your thumbs; and in oil, take hold of it over the fire, and cauterize with a cautery between the lung and the neck, and two more on either side of the jaw; one above the fifth rib, and the other below the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two along each side of the lower ribs, so that the cautery is between the shoulder blades; and do not press too hard with your hand, but make it as astringent as an odorant.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said an old man that no one uses cautery of fire like the shave, and the scalding and puts it between the ribs, until it comes to that place; and the pain goes away as we have said in the chapter on the spleen.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear for the sick now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.
