When you cure the disease of the mouse as we have said in our treatment divisions, and it does not benefit at all, then they assert three kinds of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	One of which is that you perform three cauteries or four, linking according to the length of the mouse, as we have shown in the figure of the cautery of the spleen; and do not hurry at all with the cautery, and let the sick person lie on his back; and another kind of cautery is that you scald the cautery which has two nerves, just as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the wound where the mouse is, or the swellings come towards the left side, and lift the wounds according to the size of the body, according to the length of the limbs, and the cauteries are accordingly according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After the ones have been burned for two nerves, flame them so that the keys are perceived from the other side, and then apply fire to the cautery, and in this way it will be four times. And if you see, cauterize all the cautery at three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment, as long as he has gotten infected by rotting for a long time, and this is what is meant by "the other cure" that was said before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not effective for dropsy, except when done in the way that is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit them, then it is fitting that you make four cauteries inside the belly, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one near the kidneys, and two at the back below the spine, and one towards the groin; and so that the cauteries be well close to the spot of the wound.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After letting the fire cautery burn for long times, and not stopping the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing would be hastened, and both the pain and the disease would be united with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is like the claw that we have shown; and on the back it is olive oil, according to what has been put in front.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in the person who is dropical, and are full of pus like citrine, it is necessary to cautery on the back of the foot between the auricle and the ankle; and hold your hand with the cautery as if turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply into it, for just as fire burns wood, so also does cautery burn the flesh.
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After doing the same for both legs, cut two cauteries on each leg at the point of the scabbard; and let one cautery be longer, one under the knee in front, and the other behind, within the leg; and leave the cauteries to dry long enough so that they may harden.
de la menoison	of the belly
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the sickness of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so that the virtues retentive and digestive, which are in the stomach and intestine, are bloated and cannot be cured by any other means; and you see the patient suffering greatly, if you do the following cautery on the stomach, according to what he has spoken about it before, or the fire cautery; and four cauteries around the navel, with subtle clavicle cauteries, and two cauteries on the groin.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	If you see the moistors abunding and the patient suffering, let it be cauterized on the point, and cauterize on each vein, and make two cauterizations on the stomach of the belly, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are found in the fundament, or one or more of them, and are old and have large cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, it does not profit if you cut: Three cauterizations on the spine behind the back, namely that which is entirely opposite to the left almighty date point by point in a triangle, and one cauterization below; and if you think its stomach is chilled, and its flesh is not cooked, and swelling of the face is seen, then make one cauterization on the stomach as we have said before, and another one above the liver, and another one on the mousehole all over the cauterizing nail; and let it remain for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment the limb should be healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of flesh which is called "theul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the flesh, if it shrinks like a knife that cuts, and then puts everything on fire at the place where the flesh was cut; and leaves your hand until the cautery comes to the beginning of the vein, so it won't bleed; do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh left, cauterize each part as we have said; after the treatment with ointments, let them be healthy. And if you cauterize a great cautery on the cartilage, it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of badly healed wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot suffer from size or opening what we will tell in his own words, if it comes to that illness which cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When any person comes to have an ulcer, and is wrinkled and infected with putrid matter and moistened corruption, if you prove the entire wound with subtle inquiry, and watch that you know how much depth it has.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After having the cautery which seems like a razor, and pouring it into the ulcer according to how much it had entered, repeat the cautery until the flesh and corruption are burned off, once, or twice, or three times, depending on the quantity of what needs to be done; and beware of setting fire to the nerve that is exposed, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the ulcer is in the intestine and on the belly, beware of these things, and do not burn it with fire unless you are using charcoal, and think it is not flesh; after treatment make the patient well, and if the ulcers are ulcerated, and the materials are long-standing, then know that the ulcers are entirely healed; and if the materials do not heal, know that the ulcers are treacherous, and the bones are corrupted at the font; and thus as we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of the kidneys comes from a blow and great swelling, and does not take hold in women, then it is necessary that you make cautery on both sides of the kidney, using the cauterized clavicle as we have said before; if they cause us three cauterizations in line, and the pain gets greater aid.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and inflamed from a blow and moisture, so that patients retain their urine, then make cauterization in the posterior part of the bladder, where the hair follicles begin, both on the right and left side; each side should be cauterized as long as possible with one movement, just like we have done with one finger; and make the clavicle cauterization according to the shape said before.
de la marris	In the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrix is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are late to come in; and when they arrive, if it hurts much: then it is suitable to make III cauteries around the belly, as we have said about fire cautery of the bladder, and II cauteries away from the back; and let them be clavicular, as we have said.
de la hainche	From the venison
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist viscous fluids descend to the groin of the venison, and because of this they stop moving, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that there are many leucocytes in the departure from the joint, so it is suitable to cauterize the patient on the groove of the venison with I cautery similar to a circle, and sign in front of the joint as if it turns, so that the groin is within the circle; and do cauteries like those which have been done for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this fire cautery is not present, let the patient do three fire cauteries of olive oil, and make the cauteries as deep as all the others; and let the healer be there until he is safe.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we said about division, and the healer's remedy is useless, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the sick man of heavy humors, or fetid stones, or other hard stones resembling them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the method of the cautery is two manners: that is to know the assembly of hot medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is done in many ways, from which some are like this: that you cauterize under the hair of the hamstring three times; and I make a deep and great wound, and have space between each cautery the size of two doves, and it is olive oil; sometimes one does cautery at the midpoint above the chief of the hamstring, because there are four in this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, that the cauterizing at the cautery of the ring which we have before said in the dislocation of the hamstring; but make it in a way that the rings contain all the hamstring, and all the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way to do it in sciatique, when the pain stays in the hamstring and does not reach either the thigh or the knee.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	In case of pain in the calf and leg, if it comes just above the knee, cut off two hairs on top of the patient's skin where they say the pain is located, and four doves are made on the ankle four; either use a cutting cautery or apply an ointment with an increased thickness of heat; and if the patient feels that the pain extends up to two feet or near the knee, cauterize at the place where he feels the pain three points or four.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it happens that they do more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the calf, make a cutting cautery or circular one, and be careful in all your cauterizations not to burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not make the patient suffer more pain and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen others who have done fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they let them grow long until the leg was completely removed, and also the toes, and it became clear and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a belly solution which caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in both lower and upper parts, do fire cautery on one and the other, as is this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sages said in the fire cautery of the girdle, "Thus is the manner, make this kind of iron and it will be as big as a ship’s keel, or one eighth that size, and so place them alternately, one between the other, at intervals equal to the space of an apple; and let the interstices be twice that, and also like walnuts, and have an iron girdle well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to heat it so that it is completely red and feels like hot needles, and then place it on the diseased haunch of the animal, and turn up the healthy side; and once the cautery has been applied once, let it remain for three days; and then apply a plaster made of butter, and leave the wound uncovered for a long time; after the treatment with poultice until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the fear of its sting, and since few people know how to use it; and all see are good cauteries which he can tolerate, and for what he is concerned.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns if you make an instrument with a cross-shaped section in which the edges descend along the edge of the door, and is made of iron or wood about one inch long, and two inches high, and between each one the quantity of the growth of a cow; and are overlapped and above, and joined together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After meeting on the hedge of the hawthorn tree in a patient lying on their cost side, and pressing your hand firmly on the hedge of the hawthorn; after girding between the two circles of hot ashes which are heated over one pug, and letting it remain for an hour or so, and suffering the patient from the heat and inflammation.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For in mordication, it is also like fire; and when the mordications are past, lift your hand with the instrument and remove the hot ash, and let it remain for three days, and apply butter as long as the blackened flesh of the wound is cleaned up; and let it remain for three days until rot sets in; and that would be the rear part aid after the treatment of ointments until the patient is sane.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to just the thigh or just the leg, then make an instrument that you have seen before in the groin area even more; and this is the manner of applying hot treatment, and I have written it out in treating of medical remedies.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take equal parts of alum and sulfur, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small opening to prevent the point of an arrow from entering; and put in that pot another pot full of lead, and put on alum and sulfur and hot water above, until it has two layers of powder when you have taken it firmly to your hand; and let it be so until the hot, icy, or cold mixture comes out of the pot with lead, then take all that hot water, and pour it onto sulfur and onto alum as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And when it is very wet and is managed in the movement of overworks of medicine and cauteries of other members, because it makes all kinds of work with fire, and has other medicines that are cauterized well in such a way as to cut off the hair like this, and anacard, myrrh, and gum with soap, these all combined together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Galen tells us of a remedy that one hundred men were cured of the pain in the hamstring and sciatic vein, and he highly praises it, and says that no other cure was needed, and they became well only once when this cure was done, and he instructs that they should bathe as he does after.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in some way that you take fresh and dry green gall, and crush it much with a little fat, and put it on the hamstring and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain is, and bind it; and then let it be for three hours, and by the amount of time that the patient feels less irritation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath so that his body is a little moist, and let him lie down in bed, and the pain will go away altogether and he will be healthy.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cauterization of such medicine unless after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dyscophorus says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with horsehair, if it provides aid, and must be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linseed oil and anoint it with beeswax, and apply it to the crevice that is between the big toe and the other one which is called the fissure.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dry horsehair, and applying it to a fire until it is carbonized, and anointing with linen, and leaving him so that he stains; and redo again in this manner, and do not cease doing so until you think by sense that it comes just to the hunch, and that the pain is ceased; and these kinds of cauterization are called "cautere of horsehair".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain from the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or by percussion, or by too great evacuation, or by appearance of spread-out cold matter, none of these things is worth cautery, except for those who come from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the sick person should be given voided pills or other appearances, on their back, where the pain resides, three lines signed with encaustic, and in each line a cautery or more as required by virtue and quantity of what the patient can endure; and it must be done the cautery according to the "poins" cautery; and if you see, do III cauteries or IV at the clavicle middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness comes to small children many times, and the signs of its beginning are such that they have a swollen vein when they rise up, and fear; and you will find in the lower spine on the back and in its appearance which comes upon other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see such a thing and you treat it, if you cauterize with the cauterization of the cell according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the cauterization is red in each part of the spine increasing.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that, if you cauterize between the spine with the cauterization on two points or three, and they are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the treatment the patient as long as it is sane according to what we have said, and guard so that you do not administer cauterization in the groin where there is a lump of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the joints' pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints comes from moistures that are swollen in each member of the body, and when the pain comes to the foot, they call it "podagre" precisely, and when it is due to cold causes and medicines cannot cure it, so if you cure with cautery in this manner: make a poultice of cautery around the joint on the foot, and use olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is an injury where you press on the face of the foot, make cauterization all over the whole cauterized area which we claim is called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the groin and other joints, and this happens many times, if you make cauterization on each groin three cauteries or four of each part, all over the olive oil cauterized area; and if you need more, do more, but don't hold your hand too close to fire than until the spices of the kiss are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to just below the joints and on the back, instruct the patient to apply the fire cautery that we have discussed in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, so that pain goes up and down two fingers; and if there is no pain in the joints, then give pain above each finger and above the palm of the hand; and if pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good treatment to the patient with medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	But if you give good treatment and purge the swelling, it will bring healing through the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the split of the fistula
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a splinter comes into an angery (inflammation), and the swellings descend to the joints, and it is new, so it is necessary that you cure his eyes first; let him not touch himself that day; and he should use things that lighten his stomach, so that his fever subsides from his belly; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to press his elbow until the swelling is repaired, and bring it to your fingers, and sign with a mark, such as is like the half of a circle above the body; then take out the cautery in the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is white and it feels cold.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the stools to their place; and the attendants hold fast to their hands so they do not return again; and work well on the patient, and put over them a sheet and a servant above the knees, and another above the thigh which holds up the hands; then apply the cautery to the sign at the tip of every finger, and your left hand and your right hand until you touch the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, so it recurs again in another place until you reach the bone; and be subtle in watching that the bowel does not escape while you are doing the cautery; lest you burn it; and that the patients do not die, or from any other malady.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you are not near the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	Instruct the cautery on children to be subtle according to their measure and great men also great according to their measure; after three days of cure let them cool with butter until the scab is removed; after the cure of other ointments, until they are healed, and apply to the patient for forty days on his back so that the wound is well covered; and it is necessary that his nourishment be long and fatigued, so that the boil does not emerge when he gets up to go to bed in chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to rise, dress him a well-made bandage, and apply it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he may work little and avoid excessive consumption of beer and eating, and drinking too high; and when you follow this teaching, he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after the treatment of cutting with cautery on his body.
de la routure dou ventre	of the surgical incision on the abdomen.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When other surgical incisions occur in the belly and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, then apply fire cautery according to its quantity, and burn off one-third of the affected area; after the treatment as we have said; and no one of the ancients said that it should be cauterized with fire at three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but mark first the center of the incision and draw a line above its width, and another below it; then tie your hand tightly around all the cauterized flesh.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and less painful.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, whether from falling or hurting, and the pain lasts for a long time, and medicine cures are not effective, then it is fitting that he be cautered with the cautery called "poins", and the cauterizations be done according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and virtue and its location of twists and torsions and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the pain is relieved by the first cauterization, it is good; but if not, you must repeat another cauterization on that same part, because it is customary to make the wound heal in the member that is nearest to it, so that you should perform the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of slowness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The problem is not cured with fire by great means, and itself the disease that comes from the rotting of pus and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You can see the cautery, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in division, and do not cut or stay, and you doubt that the corruption will spread all over the sick one, then make cauterization on the head: I cover the head with new, and another towards the front up to the ends of the eyebrows; two on the two horns, and one behind the neck; and hold your hand until the cautery comes alive just at the bone, and so long that the bark peels off so that the vapors of the large humors can come out; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the malleability is everywhere spread; and it manifests clearly, so it should be that you cauterize with these cauteries which we have said earlier or on the head, and two cauteries in some nails, and six cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one grant on the shoulder, and another on the other; and two on each of the shoulders, and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the leg, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and in the fossae of the hands; and be careful not to burn those that are on the lower ribs, so you don't burn them; and never do a cauterization on the bone of the finger, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when you do more cauterization, the more aid you provide, and the patient benefits; and know that patients feel no pain from cauterization as long as they are healthy, because their body is already totally corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the fire cautery should be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in various ways of using the iron tools.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment let the patient be fed with fine flour mixed with honey and other treatments until he is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When an inflammation arises in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it does not heal, then make fire cauteries on the member according to its size and smallness; let the cautery be put inside the wound where the pain lies; then treat the limbs with ointments until he heals.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes one makes cautery by hand and by foot and on the back, to deaden the nerve that numbs the member, and so if there is an inflammation; and see well not anyone gets in between unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the movements of the bones.
de albaras	Of fires
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the malady known as "albaras" is old and medicine does not help, then cut with cautery one spot at a time, according to the size of the swell that has formed, until the blister is opened and its color changes; then give the cure some flour mixed with vetches and lentils with oil from roses and leaves of plantain, and salt from gall and salt from alondre, each one a part; and mix all together, bind it with a cloth, and apply to the patient until they are cured.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of canker by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When canker comes at the beginning and you stop looking at it, then cut with cautery around the circle that seems to encircle the entire circumference of the sore.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all the wise men said that you should do cautery at the middle of a boil; and all agree on this not seeming good, because I fear it will cause ulcers and corruption, and I have never wanted to try it before, and there is no more reliable thing than cutting into the center, with the "circule" cautery, just as we have said in many other cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of an inflammation that cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have an illness called "adubelati", and it delays dying or because of the abundance it makes, or because the age of the patient is old (that is, very aged) and they are poor in blood, or because of time, then you see it hastening to die: therefore cauterize inside with many small cauterizations after that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	She will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her pierced with the cauterization at all, if she has heated the cauterization because of this there is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that sickness called "adubelati" so that the cauterization may pierce the liver, and so arrange the cauterization that the patient feels pain in that manner that the course of the putrefaction is masked.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until he is completely cured.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cauterization with fire by iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease that is called "corrodens", and it's nothing else than a swelling of a limb, because it eats the limbs just as the fire eats dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in the one who can suffer fire cautery together with fire, then take small and large cauterires according to what is suitable for the patient or the disease; after that cautery all parts so that you eradicate the whole corruption, and nothing remains.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and put on the patient's cautery so that they suffer breaking with oil until the scalds of fire are broken, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of pain generated from a natural source.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that a healthy child is not born, it's good; and if this is the case, then recommence cautery on the one who remains corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy is never cured with water medicine in its place, but all methods of fire cautery are more effective, and I have already said the remedy for water medicine in division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of pearls that come to the stones
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times a stone has to be borne with because of it, and is called 'clos' according to our intention, and is a great thing that causes bruising of the pit.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And there are two kinds of fire cauterizations for this disease.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	I.e., fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat the hair like a hot needle, and it's done with good iron to the measure that it can penetrate all parts, and has subtle edges. After that, put the hot thing on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches its root; and let it be so for three days until it starts to rot out; then make a poultice of fresh marrows crushed with fat, and place the poultice on the whole nail, and the wart will come out and will be desicated from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the shoulder with ointment, applying heat to it until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are cut into pieces from the body, and it happens many times in hands and feet, then it is advisable to treat them with fire water; and thus: take a nail or iron bar, or a needle of flint, and place the nail and the thorn, which is called cauterizing warts; and put the nail on so that it pricks all over, then pour some hot water onto it, and keep your hand firmly in place, and press your hand down gently until the edge of the nail reaches the root of the thorn, and the hot water can penetrate deep enough to reach the root; and let the patient suffer a little from the heat of the water for one hour; then leave it so, and it will seep out all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So instructions after another until you search all those who are inside the body, then treat the limbs that enclose the heart.
li cure dou trembler	treat the limbs that shake
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some are shaking from cold, of fever quarter or of another kind, so it is fitting that you make four cauteries above the spine on the back, four below each spine; one over the elbow and one over the stomach with olive oil cautery; let them shake, and hasten their recovery from the disease of the cold.
des pustules puans	of unpurulent boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	never appear on the body unless it's through bad baths or purulent boils that come from large, corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is convenient when they first appear that one makes a cautery on each of the boils: a subtle cautery with a stick of myrrh, so that the point is gripped by fire, or with an arborvitae root long, or with a cautery lenticular.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time do the cauterized with this method grow in size or increase in front, but are shattered by the superfluous parts that come from them, and are healed. But it is convenient to do so after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the arteries are cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great hemorrhages from the artery that is cut in the wound, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery on the member, and similar things; and it is a very painful thing to stink.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Instruct the patient so that when this happens to anyone, hasten and put your two fingers on the wound of the vein, and strain them very much until the pain subsides under your two; for a good deal of it will cease after this. Then apply olive oil cautery in small and large sizes as they are all red; then take one or the other according to the size of the wound and let the liver be exposed, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your two fingers, and keep it there until the pain does not remain any longer.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the fire escapes when you lift your two fingers over the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take hastily another cautery which is at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until it is completely stopped; and beware that you do not burn the nerve which is near, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when the blood does not flow from the artery, you cannot stop bleeding yourself if the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: or through cautery, or extraction since it has not been treated, or with a strong tie of thread, or with medicines placed on it which have power to stop the blood; and in order for this to happen.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer a restoration of the tight bond by covering or laying things tightly on it, or other similar things, unless they profit from it.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone, and they have no medicine or remedy present, he must place his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out so that it is restored over the wound and over the vein; and he should not move him, but let him feel cold from time to time, until he becomes very cold, so that they may congeal and thicken, and become restored.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments of wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	As we have said in the first chapter, all diseases where it is necessary to cautery with fire or with medicine, and the causes, ointments, and treatments, and forms of the cauteries; and I have placed this chapter on wounds next to that on the head, and I will go through this same path to find the one that works more easily, as we used before.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than with the first of the cauteries, and therefore you must be more cautious.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to venture into madness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come in for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who have suffered so greatly with their illness that they die quickly because of the force of their disease and the great size of its evil, and for this one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these, there is one who interprets his meaning, and says: "Wait, I am healed"; and the sickness is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting for you to only consider those who come to you with this condition, but rather put greater consideration in your honor than in your greed, and do not be too weak but rather wise about what you are certain of, and from what you have gained; and use prophecy and indication in the treatment of your sick patients so that salvation may be converted; and this will help you to gain a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three most dear sons, Our Lord grants you good understanding and right judgment, and if it pleases Him to inspire you with the holy spirit of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I instruct you to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
dou chief plein d’aigue	fill him with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	He knows that this illness comes very often in children when they give birth, and because he tightens the child's head too hard; and at times it is due to a return of the cause which one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness occur in adults, and all those I have seen died from it; therefore it seems to me that one should be cautious with the work in these procedures.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw that the child had a broken bone due to water, and the head swelled every day so much that it could no longer be borne; and he thought that moisture was the cause of his death, and this moisture is assembled below the bone under the skin, between the vein and the bone; and the abscess is small, which you must cut open in the head a large incision; and if it is as long as two fingers, so that the moisture flows out, and look at this shape of the spoon:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more deep, and the abscess is larger, then do two incisions in the manner of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and you see the commissures of the cheek on both sides, and the fluid spills out when you press your hand into it, but this does not return: then it is fitting to make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After tying the incisions with strips and powder, and putting vinegar and oil in them, and leaving it so for five days; then release, and treat the wound by applying poultices and bandages, and let the head drain out more, and then give the patient dried meat of a bit of moisture until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at or open the big opening of the abscess, and the assembly of the water; for sometimes it comes out before, sometimes behind, sometimes in the right hand, and sometimes in the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore let you cut to the size of the abscess that is opened, and the filling of the water, and cut it according to what you have the power to do; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and take care to stop the bleeding, so that the patient dies from the deterioration of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of stone
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When such a disease occurs which is called "cataract" in the eyes or in the worst case, and the disease is old, and the medicine cure does not help, then the last cure is that of cautery with what you cut open the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary to cover the eyes when you treat the patient, so that they make a gesture of their head; after that, press the leaf on them with an iron cloth until the arteries appear, then pull out the patient's neck from all the cloths; then observe where the vein flows, and the leaves are behind the ears, and they will soon recover; then sign the leaves inwards, then cut one and the other of a good spatula with two parts, until the vein comes to just above the bone, and so be done with the wide gesture of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, pour out the spatula under the artery and cut up above, cutting in the same way as it should be to pass through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if he stops not without continuous bleeding.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Et se li artere n'apert au sentir, 
de emigrainne	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient dislocation comes about, and a cough is good, because of the moisture from tears and the heat in the temples and old sore place and similar things, and he is treated with various remedies for medicine, but none of it benefits him, so we remove the arteries from the temples and the cauterized areas, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the sick person makes their hair back behind his temples, and listens to the artery opening in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and it does not come back quickly like in some men who are too cold; and if it has returned, he strains the neck of the sick man with some cloth, then rubs him with a rough cloth, and raises him with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then takes up the spatula of that form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Instruct the patient to scorch the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then grasp it from above with pins, and depart well the threads that are attached to each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn a pin on the point of the needle, and strike from that side according to the quantity of the two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	If it is not struck, do not strike without pain in any part at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And grasp the vein of six fingers, just at three; and if the artery is great, it is fitting to bind it with two leathers of a strong double silk thread, so that no discharge comes from before the sound of the wound, and blood flows continuously from the vein; then strike the superfluous part between the two leathers in that same hour, and then, if you see, if the cautery is applied with the cutlery cautery just to the bone until the fingers are struck, that is the correct work, if the patient does not have fever and it is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is aid to finish the moistors; for this is greater aid on the moistors.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is necessary to draw the arteries; for this let him fill his veins with new cotton and put on well-made tourniquets; and when you release them, cure him of dry medicines that make char, and tourniquets, until he be healed; and if you do not have a touch of the artery before you work, you hasten to cover by cautery, or you apply the vinegar leather around your hand so it is not stung; and if you don't have this, put on the leather of his vein as soon as it freezes, and raise the leather with cold water until it freezes more; and bind him as much as it seems fit; and what is softened and easier to draw from the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery with two halves, but the tourniquets be well-spaced to ward off its heat for longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the symptoms are too subdued, it holds less of its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have two incisions one in each artery, one has to be big with a large knife, and then when you've applied salve on both sides, and you heat the iron over them so that it comes near the bone, and cut the vein in two; and they should be separated by the two joints because there is no healing from this cautery at all; and that's the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing into the veins above the forehead bone, and there is no relief from medicine that's applied, and you see the face of the patient becoming red, and feel the pain in the front, as if of fever; and when the hair of the scalp is wet and moist so that the hairs fall out, and the scalp is scorched by the heat of the tears, then it may be necessary to do this cure.
