Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	Et the name they called it was "cure contuse", and you should make the patient look at his hair on his forehead, then cut three incisions in a straight line according to the length of the front; and so one of the incisions is like two fingers covering the front from underneath, and the others are two inches apart above the eyebrows; and beware not to cut the arteries that are two fingers' breadth apart above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from continuing the work on both mandibles; and make each wound three times as wide as a thumb over it; and take a piece of sponge and a lot of cloth with it to absorb the blood, then apply the spatula well in two parts like this:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision at the temple to the second incision; scrape all the wound that is between the two incisions up to the level of the bone, then make another part from the middle incision starting from the other side, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you prick in the first cut with the instrument called "cultellary", and it is very sharp from one side and soft on the other, not sharp, and this is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the cutting side towards the raw flesh at the wound, and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it comes to the second cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut off the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous just as far as the opening of the wound, and then do it again in the second cut just as far as the other end; and then extract the blood equally, and press out the fluid from the wound; then put a tunic of clean linen in each cut, and place soft cloths moistened in wine and oil and salt on top, and keep away that which brings abscesses; and on the third day remove the bandage, and administer a great quantity of diluted water and tede, then apply the ointment basilicon with olive oil, and other cures for wounds, until he is cured.
dou reume des eulz	Let your eyes steady
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any vein is inflamed, accustomed to this condition, and you see the eyes dimmed and reddened, and the sight fails, and the eyelids burn; and the hair falls out, and pain sets in at the root of the head, and the patient cries out; then recognize by these accidents that those materials and that inflammation do not come but from many veins, and the mother cure knows it, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to press his forehead, then make a deep cut on both sides of the forehead.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the left temple to the right temple, making incisions just until the bone; and keep your hand away from the area between the temples that moves with pain; when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with an sponge; then apply a cloth of linen and then cotton wool between the two lips of the wound; tie off with damp strips of linen soaked in wine and oil; be careful not to let pus form; when it is cured, suitably rub the bone until it starts to produce pus, then treat with exfoliating remedies that make it itch.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make it paste; and administer this to the wounds to bring a cure for all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear's discharge
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that comes out of the ear is one of four things: food, meat, stone from the mine, or similar substances like iron; or seeds, such as jujubes, fennel, or similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When he coughs into the ear anything that does not stick to the ear or grow in the ear, if you put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a small amount of violet oil or sesame oil; and administer an extraction. Then make it eject the condisi (perhaps meaning 'congeal' or something similar to mucus), and stop the nose when the ejecting comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool into the ear; and hold the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often comes fever by this cure; and if it does not come, extract with subtle pinchers, for thus is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it falls with the pinchers, it is good; if not, extract at the navel with subtle sewing of small stitches; and if it does not fall by this, make a cauldron of resin and pour cold water over the head or ear hole, so that the venom cannot enter through the cauldron with wax until it stops; then pull off the form, for often comes fever just as we have said; and if it does not come in that manner, take out the gall because you will get to know of it when you extract the eyes, and put on some instrument pointed for this purpose, and put a little cotton inside; then press the gall onto the bone or whatever thing it is, and pull off the form.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And instruct the patient to let her not jump out from all these things we have said, if you rush to cut off the ear so that the abscess opens and spasm; and the manner of cutting is such that you first heal the patient's head, and remove the blood according to its strength, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fat or where it hangs down; and the incision shall be like a crescent moon, until you reach the bone, then cut according to your power, and suck hard into your mouth; and the cure shall continue until she is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that has lodged and swells up, instruct the administration of removal; and if it will not come out, administer an application of poultice on subtle form according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that flesh.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make this cut when you think the grain is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many cuts; then take it out with fine pins and to a receiver, as we said, so that the extraction is light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water then, since you throw into the ear it is convenient that the patient uses a condition of powder first and fills the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And if it's also on the same ear or in the water.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if she falls through this, then it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	if that does not happen, then repeatedly make incisions according to the length of your hand should keep and light, and shave one spot over the ear, and let fall from other parts; and put on fear from another piece above the piece in the ear; and do not cease to do this until the water has all been lost, and so she falls all lost; and if you see, then take a joint, and put one of the pins into the ear, and the other pin is pierced by fire until the greater joint be hot; then repeat another piece of joints until the water has all gone off, as we said in the bone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the ear, if it is of small size, like a grain and similar thing, cure as we said in division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, do the extraction with pincers; and this is the lighter thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ear, tie off your ears when you cure as we said in division and treating dilations; but if the cure does not help, it is best to look at the ear under the sun: if there are no worms present, take the tweezers that are fine, and if none can be seen, take the wire for this is the form.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow under and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And take the more subtle snare in the ear according to the quantity of suffering the patient has, and then form it all around the wire; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	Instruct the patient to let it stay put so that it does not cause more harm as I have said in the operation; and if they do not come out as I have said, place a cotton thread inside as I have done before; and if they do not force themselves like we did, administer enemas as the ancients have proven in the removal of worms, and you will find them or treat with enemas; and distill your oil and medicines into the ear with this instrument, because it is thus that you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if it is of silver or lead, cut through at the small openings, and above it make a distillation; and to press into the distillation with an instrument well-made for this, and if you see the razor and swoop it inside the point of arrival cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the tube, and let the cotton be in the ear; then pour into the razor all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or just comes out of the ear; and feel how it hurts the patient inside, and so warm the distillations as much as you do when they are done in the ear; and guard that it does not get too cold, for the medicine would be poor.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the falling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any holes in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by the falling of a wound, or of a bone within the ear, and these falls come often enough into full depth in the ear, if one does not see them; and sometimes the hole appears after some time, and the person sees well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore when it comes to full depth, if one cannot see it, it is due to some sort of illness affecting multiple dispositions, and in that case, you must put the ear of the sick person towards the sun: and look inside: if you see the inflammation appearing, then the wound has been there for a long time of this sort, because of which the shape is
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be cautious and careful in front of and behind all flesh, if you do not strike the ear; if the opilation is of the char or bone of the ear, if you have fine points and lightly strike it, until that char is completely bare.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opilation is deep in the ear, take a fine razor and lightly shave it there, then put the bone of the ear into it.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the opilation that the patient feels great pain in the ear, cut lightly, and keep from greaving the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to its size and the pertus, and the moistened mummy of Egypt.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do anything on that day until the wound is sewn, or take a tent and the moistened rosewater mummy, and powdered with vitriol ash; and if you see the ear swollen, cover it so you treat the tent and move another tent, moistened in resin made from olive oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure him until he is well.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If it is bleeding from the nose, plunge an sponge and wring it out in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies for the removal of blood that are used to treat hemorrhages.
de la char des papieres	from the ash of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the ulcer that occurs when paper gets wet and dry again, so it's advisable to stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and cut off its roots with a spatula, then apply vitriol on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	If the ulcer doesn't heal, then gently cauterize the lenticular part with fire cautery, and cauterize afterwards the incision is valuable; and many times it heals again, when nothing remains of its roots; and when those roots are cauterized by fire, they do not return.
de la gresle	of the itch
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often happen some things on the eyes that seem like itch in their shape and hardness, and because of these the disease is called "grandine", and it is a collection of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is thus: take care if the grandine moves from one side to another, and this is a light thing to know; do then as follows: cut it down into large pieces, then scrape off each piece lightly, then pick it up with tweezers, and strike it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot pick it up by piercing the paper just one little bit, and do not cause harm to the patient; and if the opening is large, if the assembly has a seam, then treat until it is healthy; and if it is small, do nothing to force it, for the stitches restore it at once and put flesh on.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the blood is pouring down into the ear towards the upper part, so that the paper is inverted, and there is a small amount of blood at one place, take it up by pinches, and press it on both sides, and if the paper is separated from the incision, nothing will hurt; and when the blood is pressed, wash off the salt water oil, and cure the patient until he is cured.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	It is a grease that is woven in threads of paper above, and it happens more often to children than to anyone else, and it causes great pain to their eyes, and they come to have diarrhea in the mornings, and cannot see into the light of the sun because the tears are pouring out onto their eyes; and for this reason they lie on their faces until morning, and sleep upon them, and their eyebrows are moist with the grease that comes out of the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the elbow with your two hands and feel the exirnach within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way of the work is that the patient puts his head on your healthy one; and then take a linen strip, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exirnach contained in each part; then put it there; press with your two hands from one side and the other, so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; then make an incision at the midpoint of the moist place to the spatumile, cutting a wide slit not greater than the wound you made on the vein; and sew the skin as far as you see the exirnach; and in other positions, the exirnach comes out through the slit, following the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract it from the body then tie it with a piece of cloth, charmed between your two hands in front; and turn your hand to right and left so that it is spread out; and keep away from the wound what you are tying, lest you become affected by the whole spectrum until you reach the oil, lest you be wounded.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the dressing does not adhere at the beginning of the wound, draw it slightly closer to it so that it appears; then cut as we have said; then tie up with cloth easily and water, and put on the patient, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such men who break the thread and put it on to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the physician until he is cured.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it happens to an abscessed part of the body that is hot, the doctor should apply poultices soothing the place until it becomes sound.
des poilz des papieres	from paper hair.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hair grows unevenly or is inflamed, and affects the eyes, they cause various kinds of illnesses, such as excessive tearing and skin softening and a bluish discoloration of the paper, which is due to the destruction of the eye; and there are four ways to treat this: either by applying fire treatment together with cautery, or by using a cooling medicine according to what is in front of him in the cautery book, or by doing it through incision and suturing, or by tying, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the patient's head on your healthy one; then turn the paper with oil in your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; but if not, prick an arrow at all the hair above; and either cut along the margin of the paper where the hairs are growing, or pull the hair up above to the entire paper, and turn it to the razor; then make a cut in the part below the paper, under the hair, from the great laceration to the small one; prick and take out the thread, and place under the paper a small cloth of cotton and silk; and then sign on the paper a figure like that of mirto's resin, if you see so many hairs lifted by the paper as it is drawn.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Et if to the cloth which has need of binding be applied a great quantity of paper according to what the paper is softened; then make on the entire spectrum above the two lines that you have signed, and begin with a large scar just in front of small; and let one of the cuts close to the natural hair in the growth of a root, then pour the vinegar on one of the two angles where the blood has flowed, then scorch all; then sew the two edges together with a single thread of fine linen, and drain the blood, and dry the remaining filth above the two marks at any point, so that you see this done; if not, so do not have care, then let the sewing and the threads just in front of three days or four. Then treat the wound with dried bandages and binding, for the paper relieves itself immediately after the wound and the assembly of it, but the sewing is weak (as the ancients said), and this is evil; and if to another manner: and it is that you sew the paper with a figure which is equal to the fuel of myrtle, just as we have told, at three times according to the form that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off those who overstep according to equal forces, following the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you have no strength to hold the tongs, and they are not equal, then take a needle or have one thread, and pierce the mark on the figure; and pierce another thread of the larger sleeve, and the second thread of the smaller, and assemble them equally between your fingers; then tighten your hand equally, and tighten all the skin where you have marked, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, until he is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar ointment assuaging; and sometimes happens that the hair of the skin becomes converted: so it is fitting that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and another is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the backache is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the fat into inside according to what I said, and then do II caines by art, and II subtle ligatures as long as the paper and the widening of the thumb space are; and cut as II knees of II parts where you hold the strings; then assemble both one and the other subtly on that which is covered by the paper of oil, and strain the II caines from the II parts form; and let it be so some days, and the strained flesh will die and turn black and turn into a porridge, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if you cut with force, then the cure until he is healed; and when the wound is covered with a splint, and the skin returns to its original size, and there will be no more pain from the hair; that's the form of both caines that you make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Instruct the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Instruct the patient to treat the head of the shoulder if it is dislocated due to moisture and cannot stay in place. If the hair does not come out with the dislocation, then you will have to pull out the thread from under all that which you have ordered, until the thread sees force enough to break through above and that you see it by the vision of oil; then you will pull out the thread and the oil, and close the eye for two or three days, so that the hair grows in its place and comes out the char above; and if the hairs are short, accompany one long hair from the neck with nature, and lift it up with that which you leave, until it is stretched and then put back.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the rottenness of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	How this disease which is called "aleacratic" comes on, or the rotting (of oil) comes into it, if in there are two kinds: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And often by sudden injury, or from cutting, or cautery, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of it is that you split that wound, and serve the edges with it, and put in linen tents, and tie as long as they are healing; and it is not fitting to use anything in treating wounds that dries up and constricts.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	But if you do that, the disease returns worse than before; but with works that soften, like fenugreek; and rose of water or ale and linseed seeds are cooked, and the ointments of diaquilon melted in any oil, and a tent is wrapped around it, and this is the cure.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you guard yourself from it so that it does not become soldered in the same form as before; and these injuries which we have said do not burn but only appear like this disease, returning according to the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is below what truly is called "axacratic", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the direction of the work is in such a way that you prick an arrow, having two strands, and the thread in the flesh, and you pierce as far as the second joint on the arm, so that the thread comes out in two joints of the flesh; then put the thread above all at the arrow's point, and cut off with one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper figure returns as it should, that's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two slits on either side of the paper; and so that the joints of the two slits correspond to the angles of the incision you cut, and so that when they are assembled, the figure will be as it is with a letter that has no 'g' in its name "I griesche"; then remove that thread, according to the length below of the cost, from what is shown on the paper; then join the two parts cut off, and sew with threads of linen; then give him the cure of what we have said about mollifying medicines and stitches, until he is cured.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	Et if the sickness comes from cutting or sewing or cautery, so it is fitting that you cut a straight incision under the hairs of the paper-thin skin; and according to what has been said before; then sew between the two fingers of a cloth, as I have said; and one must make the work according to the shape of the sickness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters make an instrument out of any poor material so that it can return the figure to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what they need from surgery and instruments; and more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Suddenly from the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	So then when this suturing has come to be on the hands in a certain manner, where the paper above is soaked with white oil and cannot move or do its natural work, if it so happens that you put the point of a rasp over the paper, and lift it up; and draw along carefully, so that you copy what is true to the fine style of the stylus, which should not be too rough nor too sharp, so that the patient can endure neither being too rough nor having the oil stain them; and thus your incision, from which you scrape off that assembled part, do lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and is all healed, without ever making it in hot oil salty, or taking it away with cool water, and vinegar; then put between the paper and oil a cloth of linen, and put on the oil lard moistened with wool; and after three days use the coliere and such quick remedies until they are healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the oil of the wood
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two kinds of wood: one is hard and smooth like a nerve, and another that is not hard but is similar to frozen fat; when you touch it with iron and cook it in pan grease, it does not burn; and both kinds begin to resemble the great vein, and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye and all light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your hand, then closes their eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then cuts the wood as thin slices of double-edged stitch, and places it above; then takes a needle, and inserts a hair from an ox, or a horse, or a cow, and a strong thread; and doubles the point of the needle a little and pokes into the wood, and drives the entire needle into the wood, and ties the wood with a thread and places it above; then scrapes all over the skin of the wood as the color of the nail is followed to the hair on the head, then cuts off the remaining part at the root of the vein until the tip of the subtle scale and small forces, and leaves nature to the vein itself, so that by the incision there will be no blood coming from the eyes accustomed; and sometimes the wood is only cut for the oneness of the vein, and with a thread, as we have said; then scrapes all over the softness of the thread of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to let the spatumile not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the prunelle should be perceived; and after the incision, ghee in oil a small amount of broken silk, and make a collar of litargire, and leave it till the next day; then the cure will do what he thinks is necessary to heal it.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot push the needle, and the unguent does not enter, this cure has often treated a false appearance of an ingrown nail with medicines; and they give birth as I have said in division, and if you see it covered, apply oil to the patient, and take out the spatumile gently with slight touch according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the ingrown nail with subtlety, and if you see that it has not diminished at all and the region is pressing, then distill from your mouth into oil the collier made of litargire and red silk and let it cool; then reapply the oil the next day; then continue the other work according to this same operation, until all the swelling has gone.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against you in the oil, as the pus, then take the milk, and first cure the pus so that it becomes clean, then resume the work as before, until it is clean.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh is dark with pus at night in the oil because it causes great harm, then remove a little pus and not too much, lest blood comes; then distill in the oil a red liquid which is made from ligation.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of flesh that grows above the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men do not get any red flesh and cover the eyelid and restrain it with paper towels and torches as if it were a rosebush; and wounds are made so that the patient puts their head on a healthy one, then they cut the eyes, and all of that char has suitable wounds to it, and support them with force; then cut the first flesh, and go cutting every time until you get to the razor just to the end, and be careful not to strike the oil at the work; and make an incision as we have said in the incision of the ulcers and with small forces as if it were a wound that is not painful, so that the form after this chapter shows; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is cut out, then use the oil of silk or distill red liquid and similar corrosive medicines, and put cotton in the oil with linen wool, if it becomes clean; and if it does nothing, and the patient grows no chills, and you doubt about pus, then leave the oil and cure the pus with soothing things; then go back to your work until it is clean, and so do the same for all that char is cut out in the oil by this form.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in order that you may alleviate the cure of each weak person according to their natural way and by accident, through iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	But these veins are red that are covered on the flesh, and they tolerate the eye's work and weaken the flesh every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	So it is evident that on the first day you should look at the flesh, in what manner it is, whether it is thick or thin, and there is no other disease than the swelling; therefore take care to do it thus: command the patient to put his head on a clean cloth, then suspend those veins to the bone according to his wisdom, and cut them with subtle double cuts according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them do two operations one by one at a time according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then one by one apply gentle forces to those veins, and suck out the blood hour after another, until you see remove the forceful veins from the oil; and guard that you do not touch the oil with the points of the lancets, and perform this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your operation so that you only cope those veins; and when you have done this, if you distill vinegar into the oil green and red to corrupt what remains in the belly.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to suck out all that in one hour, then apply a plaster on the oil with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it remain for some days until the pains are eased, and secure yourself about the abscess hot; then resume according to this manner as before until you are healed.
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the abscess of the skin.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire or arissati named "abscess" of the skin: when you cure it by cautery and medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not cured, there is an infection in it that you must cut open at the abscess site, because if it is there, it will die, and remove all the moisture that is in it, until the bone becomes uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered and you see corruption and blackening, if it is in that form; and it is called "aspere chief" (hard head), and make iron into its shape, and point it like a knife so as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put the iron on top of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press with one finger until you feel that this corruption has returned; and do not do this again, then restore to the use of excitative remedies.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bowel is soldered, and it closes, and the bowel's flesh is soldered, and remains so for forty days, and it does not heal again, and there are no other accidents, then you know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other cure but to return the fistula to the perforated duct according to this form: and then you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it heals uncovered, as before this form, and so the nails of iron are set at three angles, and the bowel is softened till the head just like you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put it on the marrow bone of the ribs, and withdraw your hand from the oil as much as possible, then turn to the whole forest until it pierces the bone and feels the patient by that which he comes in if he holds his hand above his navel; and afterwards restore the left arm with dry medicines, just as I have taught you, and when the bowel closes and hardens the ribs, then let the material go into the navel; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open all over and do not come to be opened at the nose, nor softened in any way, it is advisable to leave the patient. Then apply salve, then put vinegar or wine on the wound with iron for treatment, then make a poultice of ice and aloe and incense and sarcoccolle, and then strain the poultice and apply it on gauze and cloth; and so the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and double each one in four, and then put one over another according to the quantity they have need. Then strain by a strong thread from above, and repeat the application with iron for treatment; then remove the iron and leave the poultice strained every day and night, and if it is tied with cloth, so much the better that you tie it tightly; then untie the cloth after a day and a night, and if the eye looks restored, that's good. But if not, then repeat the poultice and cloths and the thread and iron until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The fall of a torn thread (or veil)
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a tear in the veil comes to an opening and brings forth papers like grains of resin, it is a terrible sight; therefore, if you cover your eyes, the wound is such that you should insert a needle into the root of the part above the lower joint, then insert another needle where the double thread is at the shoulder; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut off the double thread and tie one part of the vein on top, and tighten it well, then pull out the needle and put some wet linen oil on it many times, until the threads cling together with the wound, then treat the linen oil in a way that comforts the thing, so that the wound is healed; and at no time does the wound heal unless it is tied by one part of a circular piece of cloth around each part.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes have great appearance, then pierce at the space within them that comes from the oil and run the moisture away and descend the eyes, and enter soon afterward; then take them out until they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the oil-bowl
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness called "alcunnati" is nothing but the oil-bowl assembled in the oil, resembling water flowing down, but it's not water; and the way its appearance looks like this: you seat the patient on a stool prepared straight, then take hold of his head with two hands, and press so long until you see the bowl coming up to your eyes; then let it be fixed, don't pull down and won't break the light, and observe how the patient behaves as he used to; and if they don't come out below, know that it's water, and if the appearance of the bowl is prepared like we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you put the patient in your hands, then take the fine spatula and make above the corneal conjunctiva where it is pointed by the continuation of the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown; until the bow does not come out; and when it comes out, distill oil warm with honey melted or fenugreek boiled and honey in it, then be cured with another cure until she is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oil.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	As we have similar properties in the oil in division, and what is needed to pierce it; if done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you put the patient between your hands crossed, lit by fire from the sun, and tie the good oil very tight; then place the paper of the oil on your left hand if his eyes are left-handed, or on your right hand if they are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if his eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or on your left hand, if his eyes are right-handed; then put the tip of the instrument between the crown by the size of a nail on that bloody border of the oil near the small nerve, and press the "almagda" virtuously, and turn your hand until it pierces into the bloody border of the oil, and feel when "almagda" comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the "almagda"'s path be to the end of the space between the prune's pit to the end of the black spot; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the corneal conjunctiva, then put the instrument just above where the astringent is, and press out from one side after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the wound now has come to pass, then sees the patient before him and the instrument on his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little, and if the wound is coming back through the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is fastened and does not come up, gently pull in a little at a time by turning your hand a bit at a time; and then remove from the oil a small piece of cloth, and wipe away.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put on the oil a cloth or linen soaked in oil and rose water, and tie with good oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	For this, and for those of our time, put on a common broth with abundance of water.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the pus cannot enter into the oil due to its hardness, because there are many men whose nails are too hard, then you must take up the instrument called "alberit", for this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Instruct the patient to prick the conjunctiva alone, and do not go too deep in the piercing, but do it subtly, then pour alum on him, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, the doctor will come to the patient, who will be sleeping on his back in the dark room; and you must keep all movements, and give light food, and do not move his head or right arm or left arm, and he must be tied according to his disposition every third day; then release him from this same dark house, and examine his eyes, and make him see some things, and then put the bandage on again after seven days; and it is not necessary to do that in the wound of the cure now or after the incision, but it is necessary to alleviate that, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	The head of the shoulder comes apart, when you release the oil before the seventh day, and the advice of one who sooths an abscess; and when it is appeased, hold back your sight and put on his face to cover each day, for if he stays in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he goes back and forth to the house little by little, and converts himself into those cases; and knows that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Irach, who told us that in some far-off land he had heard of a powerful potion made by someone called Almagda, with which it succeeds to cure water, but I never saw it or heard of it in our land, nor do I know it from any ancient books; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the shapes of alum, because those who do not know them see them in their own way; and they resemble pure linen:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head of the ash (alum) of this same subtlety, and the bottom in three angles of fire.
de la char sor le neis	of charcoal on the nails.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never do the nails of charcoal come out differently, because some resemble scorpions by weight; and if there are such, where they have charcoal hardened in various colors, and if they have soft charcoal with a white bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore in those soft nails that are not hardened, it is necessary to sit the patient between your hands facing towards the sun; and work his nose, and pour some powder on the nail, and draw out the hairs; for you must do what you can support until the subtle patina dries well on one side, so that you know if the nail is completely peeled.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	Et s'il en reste aucune chose qu'on ne puisse couper, si on lève à tout I des estrumens subtillement légèrement, si qu'il n'y demeure rien; et se sans te sormente, ou aposteme caus, si lou secort si com il convient; et se c'est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterise tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chairs, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the pus overflows and moistors come into just at the palace, such that it is seen to be in a good state; and if moistors do not penetrate as it should, then it is known that there is a nail left in the bone above, because the swellings do not come out to cut: then it is necessary that you put in a thread of linen a little bit thick, and no less than an inch or so, and tie it around the head of the child with great care, and draw it through as far as the mouth; and this is done often by children at school, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it; then take hold of the chief that comes out by the thread in one hand, and the other chief that comes out by the mouth in the other hand, and check one after another while holding your nose as we are.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make it so that you know how to cure the flesh, then take care of your children, clean the wound, and anoint the flesh in Egyptian oil, and put it under its head as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corroded all what remains from the flesh; and then put on a poultice made from pounded onions some days until it is cured, and if he needs dry medicines, use them; and that’s the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, because they distill oil and medicines in it:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or lead, resembling a lamp over, like an onion skin, and lead it accordingly; if you see it, make a sealed onion skin, and the instruments should also be prepared for purging the head; and hold one hand on the head to keep it while you heat the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	Of the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the hair is cut off and cooked.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	She knows when a solution of continuity comes to one of these overgrown cartilages, little profit is gained, whatever it may be in others.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.
