It is therefore necessary to consider this when it happens to one alone, if you examine whether the wound is fresh and bleeding from its whole surface; and then add two stitches to a suture, then treat him until he is healed; and if the lips are split on both sides, it is necessary that you burn all the parts of his lip until they heal, then reassemble the two lips to a suture, bind them, and apply powder of bleeding of dragon, burning incense; and cover the powder with an emplastrum of strong or other soft plaster, and let him be treated until he peels off by himself, then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is that you assemble the seam: or with needles, as we have said in sewing over the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With one's own hands, an abscess of the lips comes in, resembling grains of sand, small and larger ones; therefore you must turn back the lips, and cut each one apart, taking them with tweezers and striking each part; then apply lead after the vitriol incision breaks, until the wound is stopped bleeding; and then clean and treat the abscess with a poultice and cure with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;
des sordens	of sounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	There are no times when the roots are gathered at the top of the teeth, between the gums in the mouth, rough and ugly scars; and there is never a tooth black and yellow and rotten, until corruption comes to the gum, and it becomes putrid. So it is fitting that you sit the patient between your hands, and keep his teeth apart, so long as you notice anything; and thus do black, green, yellow, and other discolorations, until they are gone. And if one finds what is at the first cause, that's good. But if not, then it repeats itself on the second day and third day, until you have reaped everything; and observe that teeth need various forms of tools to clean them, according to what the work shows, because the rasps which we use to remove teeth have other forms than those that are used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is fitting when you cure the patient's tooth pain that you do not delay in applying the treatment as long as you can, because this should not be left undone; for it is a very high substance just since then and therefore we have no excuse for delaying the remedy.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to take a treatment, it is fitting that you be certain about the tooth being inflamed.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Most times the pain of the patient is, and consider that it may be in the good tooth; and treat with the healthy tooth. And beware not to depart from the pain by this means, until the evil things have been removed, for we have never had success with these sages; and when you are certain about the inflamed tooth, it is fitting that you burn into the tooth at all its extent with a hot instrument to ward off the gum disease in all directions; then pull out the teeth with your two fingers or pincers, carefully at first and gradually, until they are well cleaned; and afterwards fix them firmly; and place the injured tooth between your hands, and have it in your mouth so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the removal of the tooth, instruct the patient to pull it out directly into the broken pieces and if it doesn't fall, take any remaining fragments and push them into each piece lightly, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are fractured and muddled, it is advisable to fill them with draperies, either in or where they are broken; and if one strains them carefully with pincers, so that they do not break when straining; and it is much prudent to cover over the gum with a dressing to soothe the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and leave a part remaining, and inform the patient that this will cause greater pains from the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to do as the ignorant doctors do, who in their haste and boldness break the cartilage every time, and bring no cure for this illness; but sometimes it comes by the decay of the roots that remain, or by breaking the cartilage, just as we have often wished; and when the tooth is weak, wash the leaf with wine or absinthe and salt; and if there is bleeding, which frequently happens, use the leaf of vitriol to break it; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of ulcers, when first come, are of long points and thick handles, which do not double up when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And are thick members that do not bend when pulled, and are made of good iron well-made, and have teeth to hold in place.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root is left in the tooth, it is advisable to put some moist cotton wool soaked in butter on top of it once a day or twice.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the joints are softened, for that is when the needles which are called "algefry" are put in, because the head seems like a sore; and they are made just like a file and this is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out from all these tightings, so it is advisable that you uncover the skin entirely around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", namely plane, because this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it may be strong and thick if it does not break immediately, and if the root jumps up from this, it is good; but if not, help with all the instruments, because then the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it is aided by this instrument that has two openings, because this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front in the line of the teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large pincers, because this is its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And so let this instrument be used that it cannot break, and know that much of the bones are instruments; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise masters subtle in their own hands take possession of their own instrument, according to what his works and the diseases show, for there are many diseases from these instruments and the ancient ones do not teach them because of the diversity of those and if it breaks point on the stone or other bones, so I seek the instruments that are necessary, which I have told you, and aid with gestures, because thus is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And so let them be large and well-held to hold the bone, that they may not break, but can hold and remove; and then restore to the patient according to the suitable medicines, if he has rot in the bone, and it is small, then take out this entire instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not as their natural body form, and the shape is ugly, and especially in young women, so it is good that you know whether the teeth are new after the tooth, and are not in their right place, and cannot be placed or settled: then draw; and if they have an arrow with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a little beak, and is of iron well-made in form.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the knife cuts and cuts day by day in order to make the teeth hard, and because you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears as if it can be placed, then take a piece of linseed like this form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the linseed to make needles; and in linseed, the tooth cuts day by day gently so that it does not move until it breaks; then the surface becomes smooth afterwards, and if the teeth are too pointed, and they bite the tongue, so you must place the sharpness as long as it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth loosen, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot bite on them because they are loose, and you cure them with restraining medicines, which do not work; if some must be restrained with an iron thread, for silver threads rot and spoil, but gold does not move at all; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are loose, take out the thread and pass it double through both the healthy teeth, then place the pins between the healthy teeth, up to one or more than one, until you have secured them firmly in a straight line with the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume covering where you began, and pull your hand gently and carefully, so that it does not move at all; and be sure to let loose a little around the root of the tooth if it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Instruct the patient to cut the hair with a stringed instrument and tie them together, and put them between the healthy teeth, and place them so that they do not bleed from the tongue; and then leave it tight as long as it can stay, if it comes loose, or the strings will come out, then tighten with another string; if it stays and serves, like this for all of its duration, and this is the form of teeth and their alignment on both healthy teeth and on two diseased teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth comes loose, put it back in its place, fresh and new, as we have said; and do not let anyone touch it who is not wise and experienced, because at no time is the shape of a tooth made from a piece of cow bone, and then put it back on the affected area, and tighten it as we have said, and leave it to stay there for such a long duration.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is no ligament that comes from under the tongue or naturally; it occurs thus: either when born, or by accident of a burn, and the wounds are such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and have their head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve of the tongue along its length, until the tongue is freed from its place, and if there is hardness or anything else, and it is due to a sudden wound, then inject the lancet and cut along the length of that ligament; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, lest you cut into the artery that is underneath; and when you have done this, lift the head with hot water and vinegar, or with ashes, or with cold water, then put a cloth under the tongue, so that the patient can swallow each night, until the wound heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if it comes to bleeding, put vinegar on the wounded place. And if they do not come out, cauterize with cauterization, which is good for this; then give another remedy until they are healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see the pus come out in a color that is black or brown and hard, since the patient does not feel it and it should not be touched at all, because it is a chancre; and if he inclines to a blister and there is moisture, take the poultice, and make one from a spatula, finely removing one side and the other; and if they do not come out at his own place, put vinegar on him so that he becomes stained, then return to his own place until you treat all of it; and lift the wound with ease and from pain, and give another remedy until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Wounds of the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	There is no occasion for mouth wounds that are called "godath", and properly call them by their name; and when you treat them, as we have said in division, if they are not healed, be careful: if it's an abscess of small sense and flesh color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron either, for the loss of blood; but leave it as long as it is dead, and then you will cut it, or it would burst by itself; and if it is white in color, returning, and the root is subtle, have a prepared instrument to cover it, but first of all check whether the abscess has settled and calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his joints be strong, and he opens his mouth and the squire presses the instrument between his hands, and pushes the tongue under all the equipment, for this is the form; and it should be made either of silver or with subtle tin like our scalers:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue to all this equipment, and see the abscess, if take a lancet and punch into the apple, and pull out as much as you can; and pull out any cloth from around it, then cut with the instrument, for this is the form that resembles forces; and look at how the head is curved, and one side the other, and are very good, and are made of iron in this or of a handle:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use the tongs, for it is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be cut from one side and the other side; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after incision gargelize the patient with hot and cold water, and hot and cool, and if blood comes out, then gargelize the patient with hot water, or cooked pomace of green pears, or myrtle buds, and similar things, until they are stopped from bleeding; then cure as long as they are cured; and once an abscess is born in the throat other than at the two almonds, cut them as before when they adhere.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was near the throat, namely the small one; and had closely tied the entire neck so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor eat or drink, and she died if she stayed thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses are high so that they have been forced up twice by the two openings in the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Therefore I cut into it at once, and stuck one needle in the wound, then applied fire, and with a great portion of bowstring; then stuck another needle in the other opening in the neck, and closed the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that, I put the needle in these abscesses, and cut off a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus I opened the throat conduit of the woman, and now she begins to drink water and wine, and did not cease cutting at this abscess for many days; and the abscess swelled again, and filled with what I had emptied it with, until it became very large; therefore I applied pressure and cauterized inside the throat: thus remained still for a while; and then departed from these parts, and so that God may be praised after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eyelid falls down and it is swollen and prolonged, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is too large and rounded, it is called an "eyelid".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cut like we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and you see that the swelling of the abscess is reduced, and it is subtle, so it is best to copy it; and the one which is rounded and cannot be prolonged; and if it is red or dark from blood or black color, it is best to open the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its color and length, that you put the patient on a bench in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned before; then prick the eyelid from above, and take away from below, and cut at both the places where I have said for the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to let no more than the superfluity that is outside the natural term; for if you do more than this, it grieves your voice, and your speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the second almond incision, and treat so long as she becomes healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of the cutting, so it is fitting that you use an engine at the cautery of the fearful senses.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterization is moist water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient places his head on your healthy one, and then presses his tongue against the instrument that we have said in the cautery chapter, with live hot cheese, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and takes hold of this instrument’s tip, which is like this:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more safe than the cautery, whether it is cured by incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamine and yarrow and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in an i pot, and put aisil in, and make boil; and the pot should be sealed well with strong earth, and the instrument head according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And if it is of silver or lead, and if one of the chopped bones is poured into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is numbed; after this repeat often until the eye dries, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of the swellings hot, because many things happen; and do not do this only when the swellings are hot.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If the fire cautery is not present, then take a knife and put it into his head an arrow of ice, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot; for the arrow of ice does not make much vapor to press on the mouth, and this is a good cure together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Sometimes it is said to be brought to the throat with an arrow of fish or with nothing at all; therefore it is fitting that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue on the sun until you can see what thing it is; and if whatever does not please you and returns to the throat, it is fitting that you make the patient vomit so that the meat may be cooked in the stomach; by chance if it burns with vomiting; or if the maledicte swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cork, or a radish root, or a dry bread crumb; and tie to the sponge a thread, and then transfix it; and when it comes to rest, it will be cool again, and then pull forth; and if it does not come forth as we have said, take an instrument from the depths according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Et so that the curved instruments enter more easily into the throat if they can, and lift the head up high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest it will come out to life, or push the bone inside; for he must press with such force as his malady allows, for this is how he knows whether the thing is raw or not; if it is pushed down, or he pushes all over the instrument evenly, until it is done.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	there is no medicine for the throat, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when it does not help at all, then look at the throat of the sick person to the sun, and then press the tongue onto the instrument which I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound without any sign of infection, even if it has just a small incision or subtle tacks.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	But if that does not work, take a handful of horsehair, and put it in the throat of the patient, then drink or swallow some hot iron.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is weakened by water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take the whole glass of cold water, and open your mouth, and swallow in that direction, moving it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the wound feels the water, spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she does not spit as we have said, then submerge the patient in asafetida, at the instrument which I have mentioned for the fumigation of the wound; do this many times, because it will bring up the dung.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of the fumigation is that you take out a pot or where there are charcoal sticks, and it has a cover closed in the middle, and in that hole are the keys of the instrument; then you put your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the stick into his mouth, and closes the mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes out just at that point; and now the pain will come, and if it does not come, you continue the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat foul things and sour ones, and do not drink any water; and thus the sickness will be overcome by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument that is used to treat the abscess, it is when you can see it, similar to curved tongs for nails to enter into the neck; and has a resemblance to the beak of the swan, and has roughness of lime, so that what takes hold of it cannot let go; and thus there is this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The practitioners of the art of surgery
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Much of the likeness of an abscess is, according to what is remembered in this book, and is different in perforation and size; and it is in two manners, one being like the other, and because of moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those who are within or in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the limbs, and the abscesses in the lean horse are different from those that come to the joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses where you should not pierce, as long as the bowel is dead according to its completion; and if of those it is necessary to pierce when they are certain, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	When the abscess comes from between the joints, and you let it be until it has putrefied, by chance if there are corruption in the ligament and nerve of the joint, because this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is between the main limb and if you delay the perforation until it has putrefied, if it harms the main limb; or if it is near the foundation, if one pierces there so that it dies; and it is not fitting to pierce an abscess when you think the digestion is complete, lest that which is near the foundation will rot and penetrate to the marrow, and make a fistula; and cannot be cured in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is fitting that you know the location of the perforation of the abscess according to the completion, and it is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the dullness and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is fitting that you make a hole in a more dependent place, near the abscess, where the swelling is present; and if the perforation is deep into the body, when the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints, nerves, and arteries, and are equal everywhere, except at one spot without any discharge.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who are bent, by chance of the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the groin, if you value, keep the perforation until it is confirmed to be completed in digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce in front of it, the flesh will stretch and swell with venom from it, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance, its lips and palate become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if the abscess is pierced according to its size on the body, according to how much it requires of the limbs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	It is fitting to pierce small abscesses, small punctures; and large abscesses, large punctures, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess; and if it has such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the lock, and cover; when it becomes like the fold (of cloth), it is worn out, so it is fitting to do as we do with the buttons: and there are those who are cut into three angles, and those whose incision is like the stalk of myrtle, like abscesses of gangrene; and there are those where one makes a rounded shape, and other shapes and sizes, and resembling a copier.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who has no head, like an abscess with a superficial surface, it is necessary to cut through it thoroughly; and when the abscess is large, and it has grown a great bowel, and you cut through it, so that you do not take out all the bowel in this hour, but only one part; then stop the abscess just after tomorrow, then take out nothing underneath; do this repeatedly, grain by grain, until the bowel is whole; meanwhile, if the patient has weak virtue, or a woman carrying it, or a small child, or an old man decrepit with age.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Because he may expect to survive only once with the outcome of the bowel, and perhaps he will die, and you should not be disappointed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then dismiss this chapter with great care, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound is formed, and examine whether the wounds from the abscess are small; and if it's a plain cut, apply linen or old cotton patches; and if it's a large abscess, and there is much pus, then it is necessary to put in each a patch so that one falls against another; and if you have pierced the abscess with part of the skin, and you tie it inside, then fill it with old cloth or rough linen rags with moisture, and tie it up on the third day; then apply the ointment, and cure of wound care until he is sane.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	If the blood comes out of the wound, apply cold and clean water, and take off the dressing, and put on new ones many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply a gentle and soothing treatment and the powders that I have instructed in this book to you, and if it is winter time, and the powder on the wound or on the abscess is very irritating, then consider putting on tannin strips and dressing them with wet linen soaked in wine and oil hot; and if it's a scab, and the powder is burning, consider applying moist strips of linen soaked in water and oil, or in wine and oil hot, once a day, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and clean it, if it needs to be done, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what you must investigate universally in the treatment of abscesses: or you have told me how to prepare before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sorrows
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the swelling of the head often appears small abscesses, and are like those in cloth, just as the liver of a young goat, and there is much similarity among them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fatty ones and those that are moist like pus; and there are others of similar size as those in the flesh, and those that are hard and stone-like to cut, and there is no doubt about it if they cause a change in the arteries.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the swellings of the groin are that you should prove all the instruments that are called "intermittent", because the shape comes after it, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they make a cut under long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, they scrape off nothing on the skin that contains that moisture, because it comes back when you leave anything there; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; if not, in water and oil, and apply the wound, leaving it until the next day; those who stay by night will be cured.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resume the cotton, as before, the next day, and the treatment, until you know that it will not stay by night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable to its condition, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses are stuck fast, make a cut according to this shape, under long; and scrape off all your hair, and scratch all parts, and apply all your treatment for treating the wound where it is; and if the arteries cause opposition, do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do also of the abscess if it is a stone, and as I told you when cutting and curing as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut above the painful abscess if it is a stone and moist, for if it is light in weight, there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are some of these abscesses or wounds that have no moisture, and such as I cut out from the head of an old woman; and found the abscess just like a hard, rough, and white stone that cannot break; and if any had been cauterized, they would be treated just as well as one from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come from wounds or the head, whether it is from children's heads or ear roots, cut open so that the bowels will come out, and cure as necessary.
des scrophules	Des scrophules translates to "The scrofulas".
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often the abscess occurs on the neck, and under the armpits, and sometimes in other parts of the body, and are very large, and join one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly inside its side, just like the lump and abscess on the cheek, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malignant and do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then, where you see a good disposition in the elbow joint, and is similar to the color of the flesh, and mute in every part, and not inflamed at the neck, or in the artery, nor in the vein, and is not deep; it is fitting that you copy it from above, and scrape off each part, and make both cheeks red like one another, if you need to, as we have said in abscesses of the cheek; and pull it out slow, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or vein, nor should you use sharp instruments, lest the hand gets blistered, and does not see too far ahead, that you do not cover what is not needed.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you prick the vein or artery, and do not allow it to close, put vinegar on the wound or some powder that will stop the bleeding, and bind up the wound; and let it be until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begin to pour.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when it has stopped bleeding, return to your work, until you complete it; then look at the patient's stool to see if there are small scrofulas, and cut them off and lance them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the scrofula, do not think that you should cut only that vein, but tie it with a double thread strong, and let it fall off without any pain; then apply the wound with Egyptian linen bandage, then the cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you cut the scrofula entirely, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound and sew now, so that there is no lingering of superfluity due to the great size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if it is fitting that you listen to the root of the thing, and treat the wound, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, perforate where the swelling is; and perforate as we have said, depending on it, then insert tentatives with ointment and similar things, so that what remains from corruption is corrupted; and when the wound is well cleansed, if ointment is applied to the site until it is made whole.
de squinance	of squandamence
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old people spoke and told about the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen in our land who did it, and that is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	To those who have ulcerated, it is necessary that the swelling of the throat, which is called "epiglote", be avoided; and do not make assistance for this, because all the veins and the part of the tongue are swollen in those who have a sharp ulcer in the mouth, or in the throat, or on both.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the tongue, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglote, that we cut it beneath the three circles or four small cuts through and between the two circles, or according to the size of the cut on the syphac, not on the cartilage; for this cutting is suitable for the section of the epiglote, so that there is no scar, and the vessels are long in coming.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Instruct the patient that if the master is fearful, he must stretch the skin of the throat up to its tip, then cut it as long as the vein comes out at the channel; and pull off the scabs of blood, if you see any thing, and then strike the sac, just as we have said; and it will be shown by section of the vein that has been broken by the animal that is broken, and by the fault of the voice; and let the wound cover one piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is past, because of which we doubt strangulation, gather both lips of the wound of the vein together, and remove the skin to the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow until it is safe.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	If not this is done until the throat is completely closed, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the disease worsens.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Instruct the patient to hold the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and for this the ancients commanded to leave the wound covered until the disease passes, and it has passed after three days or four years; and then they ordered to sew up the wound and cure, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took out her sword and pinned it in her throat, and cut off part of the neck flesh; and I was summoned to cure her, and found her dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had come out of it, and I realized that she had not pierced her own vein or inserted any foreign object only in her throat, but it came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I have failed to translate the text.
de la grosse gorge	From the big throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This hernia is called "thrust of the throat" and it's a large protrusion in the color of jet, and it's often found in women, and there are two kinds: natural and acquired; where the natural has no swelling.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the acquired kind is in two manners: because one is like fat flesh, and the other like an abscess coming from an artery; and it's feared, and should not be treated with fire for those who are small, and prove and search around the inside; if you find it as fat as I don't, and there's no cause to fear, then cut it just like we cut flesh, and pull out all its covering, if there's none; and search well, and cure as it needs, until it's perfectly healthy.
des nous	Our
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many kinds of cuts in us, and I will tell you all the types, and it is fitting that I say all the differences between them and a separation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that separation is then and fever remaining, as long as the boiling has not been completed, and it is done by allowing to putrefy; therefore rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the cut there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which are its own sacs, according to the color of the body, and begin in the same way as a jelly, and become large; and are similar in appearance, or color, or moisture, and much of the color are so like what I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of this malady, that you ask and investigate first everything in the instrument called "intromissoire", according to its form or chapter which comes next.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way of inquiring about the abscesses inside us is that you prick or squeeze the moistest part you find in the abscess, and turn your thumbs a little at a time, until you see that the instrument has pierced the heart, then cut it according to the size of the abscess; then remove the intromissoire, and be careful not to push.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the mortar is cut through, as it has color then, if you prick as I have said for other abscesses; and if after that the intromissoire does not come with moisture, see that it is fat, so if it bleeds then in a cross, and take hold of it with pincers, and scorch it lightly from each part, and watch the coat where you find that you draw it clean with the nose; and if you cannot draw it clean, then draw it by pieces as it does not stay anything.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it stays still, it will return by many times; and if it remains for a little while, do not be upset, so apply the wound to some corrosive powders sharp, hold the wound, and put on soothing things with hot poultices, and treat other cures until he is healed; and if the swelling is great, cut off two fingers of the wound, and cure that who causes inflammation of the char.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is swollen against you or against another, and if you hurry to apply the treatment with the lead of vitriol broken, let it remain for two days or three, until the wound has passed, and rests on the cooling of the blood; then return to cover that which is remaining in the other place.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the interstitial humors, and they come in three kinds: large and small, and also have three quarters called "albaret", and one called "breb"; and they are also in three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle the nodules of fistulas; and are like the needles with which one cuts the sutures, and made of citrine, iron, or silver, and move well those who are yellow, and are more advantageous for encircling the corvids of fistula; and come in three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the broadness of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of ulcers are much like one another, as you see here: great, small, and little; and so are the ulcers with two feet in three ways likewise; and those with three feet, and are also in three ways; and those with two feet, and ulcers alone of one foot, and are in three ways; and all this is necessary for their treatment.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these cuts is thus made sharp, and of such kinds that there are those who cut only from one side, where the flesh is burned because they do not pierce the vein or nerve; and such incisions have bleeding returning in handkerchiefs, so that the patient does not lose them when opening abscesses; and there are three kinds: great, small, and medium, as you see; and do not use only one kind of force more than for joints, such as legs, arms, and breasts, and tendons, and similar places; and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling scabbard of fistulae, according to this form, in which the wound bleeds.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And put it on no occasion in the place where the veins are healthy, and the arteries, and on no occasion do they return to this great form:

puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound with charcoal, then assemble the two lips of the wound to the skin, and let the treatment continue until it is healed; and if the breast grows downward, and becomes swollen as in women, so that one forms over the other, so that both are bound together at the end of each, according to this form, from line b up to line g; then scrape the leather between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about costume and powder, and what is necessary for treatment, until it is healed; and if it does not heal, or the incision has not been completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the decomposition of blood, then you should fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive ointment; and let it be treated until the remaining tissue and fat are reached, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	There are abscesses at the joints.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from under the joints are hard swellings or knots with fever.

de la routure de l’artere	Of the cautery of fire
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin is sewn over it when it's on top, if many abscesses come up and it happens with a vein that has flown away and an abscess; and if one observes so when it's for the artery, then there are long signs in through it by its passage; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel strangulation; and when it's for the vein, you see more swollen; and it is foolish to cover up this abscess, and itself when it is beneath the shoulders and near the neck and other joints, and there are great swellings.

It is therefore necessary to abandon the iron cautery, and he who has a head should do so as well; and in one who has swelling of an artery, cut through the skin on top of it; then sew up the belly with stitches, and carefully remove the artery from the skin, until it is uncovered; then suck blood from above to above the stitch, and make the artery double the thickness by tying it with two threads, according as I have taught you in the extraction of two arteries that are in the temples; then take care not to leave any space between the two stitches until they heal; then apply a treatment that follows the bowing back, until the stitch comes out; and if the abscess is large enough for the vein, it is necessary that you tie the abscess with one thread of two parts as two fingers of the thumb; and if you doubt that the threads will not come out, suck an artery from above to above all the abscess on the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four fingers; then cut the abscess until it is completely emptied, then cut the empty part with a knife and leave the one that is tied; then put on a moist bandage made of linen and wine, and apply treatments of tentacles and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the joints
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Then comes an abscess in the artery and vein, when it is putrid, or because of excessive work, and similar things.
