And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows where there are joints, and it's an abscess, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and is associated with many deaths, and when one pulls out, they feel pain, and it's not easy to relieve from flesh, but under the skin; and one suffers well from all parts, and doesn't move forward or backward, nor above or below, and he who has joints cannot be covered with iron: by chance it may contract; and that who is in the head or forehead, makes a membrane on the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have tongs and cut it at its root; and if it's large, if you suspend it with an onion and scorch it, then scrape and oste the wound to the bone, and sew the skin back together until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging down.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never has it occurred in the abdomen or any other part, and it's a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, with subtle roots and large nodules; there are small ones as well as large ones; I saw one man who had two bellies that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and they didn't have the slightest difference, and were white, with a thin root, and were split open, and were rotting away due to moisture.

Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess enchanted, and I came to treat this chancre after.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is swollen.

If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or a cut on the sac, and is located on the abdomen and has some boils, like in other cases, or because of blood that cuts through veins or arteries according to what is in front, or because of ventosicity; and if this is by the wound of the syphac and by the issue of the boil, then it resembles the color of the body, and is a light thing with pain, and opens from diverse issues.

Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is fitting that you leave the cure.

dou chancre	A chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in dividing the symptoms of a chancre, and how to treat it with medicines, and how not to use iron cure; and that a chancre spreads to the mares, and great caution must be taken in the treatment; and they say that when chancres are on him where one can prick them like a chancre that is at the breast, or in the crotch, or similar places, and it should all be removed as soon as it starts; and when they are large and old, do not dare to approach them, because I have never seen anyone cured of such, nor has anyone else ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment of ulcers when they are on him where one can remove them is that you do not purify the patient with black bile once; then make him healthy if he has manifest repletion, then do what we have said to make the ulcer; then apply your poultices or chancre, and cut off all parts, and leave nothing but bone; let the wound heal completely, and hope well that the patient will recover at your hands or on any thing; and if the bleeding comes from the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it so that it is not dried out.
de ydropisie	From dropsy (water sickness)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have discussed in the division the symptoms of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each symptom, and the medicine treatment for them, and the cure that can be done by iron: if it's only exposed; and one should not touch iron to these two similarities: this means tympanites and hypostasis, because they are a mortal thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy with medicines, which is called "exposure" of medicines, and the cure does not profit, look at if the patient is weak or has another disease than dropsy, as fever, belly pain, and similar things. Do not touch iron because there is doubt; and if you see that the patient has great strength and only has dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then do this: lift the patient upright above your hands, and let the ministers press the abdomen towards the lowest part of the belly, then take the spadon with thorns in such form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let them cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Cutting a point and making sure it does not enter too deeply so that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot be pulled out; then check if the drop of blood is coming towards the intestines: if it's suitable to cut in the right direction under the third bone of the arm below the elbow; and if the blood drop is due to liver disease, cut to the left side of the third bone of the arm; and if it's due to gallstones, cut to the right; but do not let the patient stay on that part where weakness occurs to others; then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, tie off, and apply pressure to the main artery between the skin and the vein just as when draining blood from a wound until the amount of an angle or less comes out; then pierce the vein so that the bandage comes up to the elbow; and that's the sign of the water, then pull it out, and use this instrument in the shape of which
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is like a chain of silver finely, and it is made from iron or from the arth (a type of metal), and in the part below, there are small breaks; and on one side, three breaks; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the joint is cut as if it were like a pen, and this is the form of the incision that the scribes make with the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head above is the alemele, so when the instrument comes to the water, draw it up now into the instrument; empty then one-third or one-half, for if you empty more than it should, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit with the arrow, or he will drop his hands, or approach death; but empty as much as is suitable according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the signs of the virtue on the patient mean, and his feet; then take the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now by the pressure that blocks the break above the wound, which I have said, so you must pierce according to this manner; then resume the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and take a small quantity of water from the vessel; do not do this one day, and beware not to fool around until he does not stay but for a little bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt about the patient and give them much water, if the cure uses dirt or sharp stone, and follows much sweating or bathing and sun exposure, and drinks beer; and the cure of drying medicines until they are healthy, and cauterizes on the stomach and liver and spleen after drawing out the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of a stoppage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	There is no child born without a hernia in the penis, or if there is one it is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If you want to do this at the same time as it pierces, then you must insert it very subtly for every inch of the length.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Instruct the patient to put on a bandage from the knee up to the groin, and tie it so that it is tight but not too tight, like three fingers or four for three days; and when he wants to urinate, stop the wound, make urine, and then remove it. And in case it does not come out at all, because the urine that comes out now will not close, do not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the cut is on the foot, it will be cured with a bandage from the knee up to the groin, just as we have said, if it spreads.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the cut on their own leg are troubled, because no one is born with a cut on the head of the penis, since they cannot urinate until they lift up their penis to the top; and they cannot menstruate for this reason, because the matter cannot come out at just that place, and it's a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to sit on his backside, with his elbows bent and his head resting on an armrest, holding a rod like the head of a stick about the length of a pinhead, so that the injured area is surrounded by a piece of cloth as it should be; and beware of bleeding which often occurs, and if it happens, bind up what is bleeding, and cure the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of swellings on the rod (or staff).
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often swellings come on the rod, and it is an ugly appearance; and some are bad, while others are not bad. If you must pierce them at once with a subtle instrument, cut and lance them all, then apply wet cotton cloth in Egyptian ointment; then cure with sharp ointment until they heal.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the skin is infected and of a foul colour and smell, it is advisable to apply cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you cut it, and if the skin is infected with pus in some places and also outside, it is advisable to remove the pus that is inside first; and when it is closed up, if it is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	But when you treat the whole thing together, it is not certain that the infected vein will be removed completely, and blackness and corruption may come to the vein and its contents; therefore, cut off everything that is black and rotten, then cover with a poultice made of honey and flour made from pomace of grapes and dates, and the cure should do other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if they are discolored due to blood, then apply lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is useful in two dispositions: namely, when they are discolored due to blood, and when corrupted; and if the head of the rod is corrupted and retracted, then it would be appropriate to pour out or lead out from the rod a channel of pus, and let the patient pass. When the hair grows long at the top of the rod which has not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or abscess, then it would be appropriate that you scorch with the instrument cheek, until the ligaments are loosened, and the rod of the verge is freed from all parts; and if this causes a painful swelling, then it would be appropriate to scorch with a spatula upon the top of the rod and skin; then carefully place between two, and put a subtle linen cloth soaked in cold water beneath, so that it does not strike directly.
de la circoncision	About circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a hindrance to continued healing like other wounds; all things allow us to do this work of our own will, and properly in children, since it is necessary that we make the better and more gentle work, and for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not say about circumcision in their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I wanted the greatest part of the masters and physicians who performed circumcision on infants, with forceps, and all a new novelty; they did not use it because there are two souls, and by chance some were killed above and kept that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	For the recovery of the flesh, and it is a double pain, and after purification which is not certain about the tip of the limb; and by chance escape the iron, and the wound becomes infected, and many times there are such purifications that they do not have need of them, and I wanted to know.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Through the purification which is done with force, to all the length of the limb I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut exactly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, the cuts are equally distributed all along the joint; but if the thread is not tightly tied around the skin; and if the manner of the first operation is such that you make it seem like you're doing nothing to the child, who hears it, then you only tie the thread around the staff so tightly; and do it in all ways possible; then put your hand straight over the staff, and lift the forces between your hands or beneath your feet so that the child does not see anything, nor any instruments; then take your hand to the staff and blow on it, and pull it up until the joint of the staff is exposed; then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled there; then tie a double thread to the new skin; then tie below one above another; and hold them tightly with two fingers as in the second binding to the pouchet and to the dough, and tie between the two, then pull tight the wound from top to bottom; and take off the head of the staff; then let the blood flow a little by little, because it is the most tender part; and put powder on and on with the powdered glass, mixed with rosewater, warm and simmered until soft, confectioned with good olive oil, and fresh, and leave it to dry until the next day, and cure with another cure until it is safe.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the force for cleansing is thus this: the two shoulders are joined and so are the joints, and the shoulders are as wide as the arm.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of cleansing is when the curvatures fit inside the incision; therefore it is necessary to extend your angle, so that the abscess opens; and strike equally, and if you cannot hold onto your angle, then take your nails, and then strike.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they persist for three days, and what is beneath the vein is swollen, then let it be left until the abscesses on its surface are smoothed out, and it is lightly scorched; strike equally as you can move, and take care of the part of the vein, so that it will not harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the joint of such sudden injuries, where we have treated powders, and if it is cut too deeply outside measure, and it goes up high, so that it does not harm, cure it then, as we have said, until it is sound.
dou retenement de l’urine	and retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by the concretion of stones, or blood clotting, or bowels, or gallstones, or similar things that we have described in the division; and if the urine does not flow, and you see it is blocked, then there is a stone lodged near the neck of the bladder, so it is wise to bend the patient’s knees; and they are placed on their back, and his belly is stretched out from above the back, and he should be restrained as much as possible until he can. And thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the stone above, because the urine flows; and if not, as we have said, then the patient feels great pain, so it is wise to administer extraction on all the instruments called "siringue", such as: with a silver thin leg, like a bird's feather; and with a cane from half a palm of palm wood and slender at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
des maladies de la vessie	of urinary diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorchers or blood comes into the bladder, or when pus is assembled there, and you see water and medicine dripping out, do this to all the instrument called "clepsydre", and it's in the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three perforations: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the leather straps because the medicine is applied so well to the tip of the instrument, if possible, to extract moisture, and push when necessary. When you see your medicines dripping into the bladder, put the head of the stopper in the moisture, and pull out what's inside; if you pull out the moisture from the stopper, then push it back strongly into the stopper; if the moisture enters the stopper again, and comes into the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the subtle form of the cystoscope which we call cystitis:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	Et est d'argent ou d'aurot, and is the key more high; and below it to the vein where they tie it; then take a sheep's gut vessel and put in the moisture that you see clotting in the vessel, then tie between the two breasts forming a good double thread, and heat it over the fire; then pour the head into the clister in the vein, then strain your hand on the vessel until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the vein; and if you don't have the vessel, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce round about it; then push the strong thread into those punctures, then assemble the circle as we assemble the skin, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie in the instrument; and do so as you have done with the vessel, pressing on your hand until the moisture comes to the vein.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division how to cut stones and extract medicines; and I have said the difference between stone that freezes with rain, and all the signs; and when to cut which stones, and how to operate on the bladder, and the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone frozen in the bladder often happens in children, and it's a sign that the water bursts from the bladder like water bursting from subtlety; and they have open wounds, and they prick the patient's penis, and they pierce them many times, and then enure; and for many of these falls, and are lighter to heal until they are four years old, and are much grieved in old age, and are in between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with lye, because it removes all the filth that is inside the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	But it is never advisable to inquire about cutting into stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and push them down and outwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and does not sometimes come up into their chest; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and let his legs be down below his knees, so that the bladder is completely turned downwards; then take it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, immediately hasten now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out through the toucher to the bottom, if your right hand has an oily index finger, since the patient is sick or on his left side, since the patient is young and accomplished; and pour it into his fundament, and take the stone, and when you feel it with your thumb, immediately squeeze it against the neck of the bladder; then press it towards the place where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands him to extend his right hand across the chest, and with his left hand to press the skin under the chest where they make the incision; then he pours the spatumile into the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they make it between the chest and the foundation, not at the middle but on the side of the left nipple; and it should be straight above the bone, and two fingers' breadth away from the foundation, and it should be cut to a width as needed, except that it is too narrow; for in case the pressure pushes against one of your fingers on the foundation, it will jump out during the work; and notice if there is part of the stone that has angles, and margins: if it is difficult to extract; and if there is some part below, like a glint, and rounded, from which comes a light, easy to pierce.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For the celestial bodies then, if they are at an angle and margin, make the incision larger; and if it does not bleed, so that you can constrict the nails as tightly as a file on the forehead to prevent constriction of the stone so that it doesn’t escape; or pour down into the subtle instrument bent towards the head; and if you cannot do so, then enlarge the puncture of the pierced part, and if there are no incisions, then strain with vinegar; and if there is more than one stone, then pour first the largest one onto the neck of the bladder, then cut upwards, then take out, and the smaller ones after if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then cut a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine comes out afterwards because of the wound that the flesh cannot close; but try your best to treat, or to cut open the nails, until you have cut it by pieces; and when you have completed your work, then apply the poultice of incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and cover with a damp cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to calm the abscess; then revive the patient on their back, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, pour out much oil and water into the wound, then treat with resin binding and powdered resin until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come to the wound and cause corrosion and free blood in the bladder, and are retained because of urine, which is known in this way that without urinating with urine: put then oil in the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains there, the bladder will be corrupted, and damaged; then lift the wound with water and ash and silk, and assist him in all ways as you know, until he is healed; and it is fitting that every medicine you give him, you bind his two knees together, and assemble those medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it is set up in a canal of the urethra, and it cannot come out with urine: if the treatment of this which I said is also done to you, then we excuse ourselves from the operation for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tried this way before.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Prepare the iron according to this shape and fix three points on one side of it.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and place it around the vein below the stone, so that it does not come after in the bladder; then push the iron into the vein lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the iron slowly on the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; when this happens at once, then press your hand over what is remaining of the stone that is inside the vein.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it breaks at once and comes out with the urine, and cures the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that forbids it, then tie the thread around the stone and the other side above, then make the vein straight to the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and release the thread, and clean the wound with the ice that is in the cut; and cure until he is cured.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stone is in women, and if it has happened once, the patient will be afflicted, and he is forbidden by three things: one is that by chance the woman may be a virgin; and the second is that no one can find a woman who knows how to shave herself, especially when she is at her period.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman who knows how to do this with her hands; and the fourth way is that the stone in a woman is more embedded than in a man, because it can cause a deeper wound, and great fear comes of it. And if need arises for this, it is fitting that you take hold of a midwife who is well-known, and at first look carefully, and if you do not find her, then choose a clever fake; and present him with a tale well-versed in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and he commands her to do what you ask from his inquiry about the stone; and observe very much whether she is a virgin: then it is fitting that you throw your coin into the foundation and search for the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain her thus under her coin, and he demands that she pour out her coin or with the patient, and wants and presses his left hand on the bladder form.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	Instruct the patient to let it be still from great to great until the entry of the bladder up to below; then strike above the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone, where you will find something like an arrow on that side; and do not move your thumb either above or below the stone, and tie it with a thread first; then pour the hot liquor into the wound, if you feel the stone so close to the pain as far as the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small and large, sharp and rough, long and rounded, and those that have marks.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the appearances so as to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it does not bring back to life, he should apply vitriol powder broken into the wound, and hold onto it for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the stone comes out, and you have the tools that I told you in the extraction of stones for your aid in your work. And if it does not bring back to life, and it's from cutting the artery that was cut off, then apply powder on the wound and the stain of lint and bandages, and do not resume it again, and let the stone alone, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the wound is pacified, and the pus stops, it returns to its place until the stone is broken.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia in the groin.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The rhamose aquouse is nothing but an assembly of moist or white siphon, which lies under the skin, near the joints, where it contains the blood; and they call it "siphon", and sometimes it is not properly in the skin, if one thinks it's another wound; and this (the membrane of the joint) we have said to be the skin of the joint between the white siphon which we have mentioned; and such things happen by chance or no.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rhamose (wound) is so weak that it comes to the joints, and spreads out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes if it happens to strike the joints and this moisture is many colored: or there's a decline in color to yellow, or without red, or black, or white, and that occurs more; and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, because if it's white as we've said, then the abscesses return, as long as the figure of an ox, and not opening the joints, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there's moisture in its own skin, then the abscesses return with a part of the flesh, and because of that one thinks it's another ox; and if the moisture is between the joint and white, you feel pain well; therefore, when you see how to know the color of the moisture, make sure to inspect the entire interior quadrangle, for this shape is what's in front.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to those who come after the intrusive injury, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat with iron, it is fitting that the patient should be judged according to our power and the replenishment of his body; then set his spine on one thing which is high, and put a great number of drapery on him; then sit above his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod onto one of the two ribs of the shoulder; then take the speculum, and scrape the skin of the shoulder from its midpoint up until it reaches the joint, and make a straight cut through the skin so that you reach white flesh, and shave it finely according to our power; then pierce the shoulder plain with water until it is full-sized, and extract all the water, and then put on your dressings, and set the shoulder again; and do not touch the heart of the shoulder, but only the shoulder itself, cut through it piece by piece in the same manner as you cut through the costal bone, so that if you do not cut well, he will return to being full of blood; and if his blood swells beyond your work, tie him up with a bandage when you have completed the work on the shoulder.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find the corrupted blood of another disease, so it is fitting to tie the straps that are suspended above, in doubting the worsening of the disease; then strike the point at all the suspension, and extract the blood, and treat as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if an inflammation has assembled into two parts in assembly, such that they are two branches; if you strike the other part as you have done the first equally, then clean the wound, and put a moist linen in the wound in rose oil; and put on another wet linen in wine and oil, and put over the two points, and put double drapery above, and tie it up on all the line that follows this shape:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take the two drapes and treat them with wool fluff according to this resemblance and assemble them by sewing in the neck of the braies, and one of the pins presses against the foundation just at the back, and the other on the side of the nail; and another pair of heads above the two horns, and it is all assembled the tightened belt in the bow of the braie; and sometimes this branch is treated with cautery instead of iron according to its size, and you take a subtle caulder knife, and strike the skin of the points, and scorch so as we have said, until the white matter that contains the inflammation is uncovered; then take the cautery in this form, and pierce those syphac with nails, and scorch with this subtle cautery hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	Instruct the patient in all ways that you can, as long as you mark it well; and keep in mind that fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more safe; and beware of the corruption of blood, and be mindful of the wounds of cutting; and if no other thing troubles you, or an abscess, or wounds, or another thing, then cure what troubles you, according to what has been said beforehand.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and will not wait for this work due to its horror, you must perform perforation, as I told you, since when you are certain of it by the significations we have said, that water is laid down like a bandage, you should place the patient on a raised bed; then pierce the abscess in the lower part of all the affected area, and make the perforation deep into the long body part; and let the wounds be wide enough so that all the blood flows out; then put cotton over the wound, tie it, and leave for the remaining blood to flow out, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the bandage does not allow the blood to escape from the mouth of the wound, you must pour a quill or the instrument used to treat waterborne diseases, which is as we previously said; and enlarge the wound, and know that the blood returns, and is assembled after six months or sooner, and when it is assembled, as before, so will pass the patient's days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the throat
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this branch there is fear of more deaths, because it seems to me that it should not be done; and I will tell you the thing and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the body, and especially from the throat; and it's a very frequent case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say that it happens through excessive acidity and water, which is spread in the abscesses, or by percussion; and its color is according to the color of the body; and it does not feel pain, but an abscess with a grievous hurt; and sometimes there are grievous abscesses painful and painful, and of a foul color, and on some occasions it comes from another artery, or swells up with inflammation.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by no artery, so it's seen by the disposition of the abscess, when you press on both sides; and it doesn't suit to touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is swollen with vein inflammation is recognized by the disposition of its expression when touched on both sides, and anyone can make good judgment about it, and about similar cases; and you must cut the root of the vein, then separate the head upwards, and pull out the suspender from all parts of the head.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the head is already sore with these swellings, then it's best to treat the head and cut it; and if it's swollen in the sac or within the vessels, it's best to deliver all that vein, and cut it around.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the skin of the nose is near, so that you can copy it all and extract the warts, just as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your wounds are completed, apply the wound of flaxen thread in oil and rose wine, then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses from the tonsils.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess that has broken out wrapped in a membrane similar to the tonsil, with swelling of the tonsils, and the patient dies greatly when it appears; and the cure for this illness is almost as feared as before, and we will tell you about the treatment in the same way as the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	Instruct the patient to sit upright on the elevated bed, then pour the liquor into his vessels until they are full, and hold all the nearby vessels with great care, and stretch them out; then cut at the spatumile trenching wide through the joint in the direction of the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape off from each part, as we have said when extracting the arteries that are in the temples; then put a needle or it has two threads, and tie to the first thread where the vein is arrived, and tied behind to the other head; then cut straight on, according to the length of the body, and take out the corrupting moisture; then cure the wound as with the others, so that no vessel gets blocked while the blood flows; because by this nothing bad happens, and all the vessels come back to their normal state, if it is done for all the vessels; so that the oes do not lose their swelling due to the incision of the vessels.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the surgery of the syphilitic lesion
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The symptoms of this type of fracture are due to the section that occurs because of the syphilitic lesion, or where there is a stretching on the abdomen in the area of the intestines; for it is from this kind of injury that the intestine descends from the same wound onto one of the joints; and these two types of injuries come about by many causes: percussion, bruise, fire, or lifting of pain, and by similar things; and when there are signs that indicate the stretching of the syphilitic lesion, it is that they happen little by little over a long period of time, and do not occur suddenly; and the abscesses become equal in size until reaching the end, because the syphilitic lesion presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when there is a sudden onset of pain at the beginning; and it is that the abscesses have different appearances under the skin close to, and it comes about from the intestine's movement and the body's rejection of the syphilitic lesion.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes from this joint with the intestine, it is retained inside, and it causes great suffering to the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments due to fear, because it is said to be so.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And thus the manner of this operation is that you command the patient to take his intestine inside his hand and put it in the wound if possible; then pinch his neck between your hands, and raise the joints. Then stitch the cut from top to bottom, and put a needle and thread with four threads into the wound according to what you have need for to open the wound, so that they can come out; then clean up the scab that is under the skin of the wounds, as much as it takes to reveal all parts. Then inject your two fingers into that which suits the joint, between the white scab that is under the skin on the shoulder, and between the second scab, and behind the shoulder, and between the second scab; then move with the right hand inside the wound of the joints, and raise the white scab at the top of your left hand, and tie the shoulder to all the scabs towards the belly; and command the minister to extend the shoulder from above, and untie what is behind the binding; and ask if you find any intestine or hard white scab, and if not, inject it into the belly below; then take a needle with which there are four large threads made of six threads, and insert it in the back part of the scab, which is after the skin of the shoulder; behind the belly, then stitch the hairs that appear from the threads, until you have four threads; then assemble them one on top of the other like a cross, and tie the scab with a strong knot of two parts; then tie the strings of the intestines, and tie them tightly enough so that none of the servants who suckle them can enter in you, unless worms come from within; and put the first knot according to the length of two fingers of the second knot, and after that, leave the scab which is under the joint of the skin of the shoulder a long one; and then stitch as we said before it. Then apply moist linen soaked in oil, and put in wounds, and tie up the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white sac is cauterized as we have said after the incision, by suspicion of a continued flow of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and let the cord stay in place until it closes up on its own; and if it lags behind in the bowels, whether it is caused by hot water, or apply what we have said, so that it closes; then cure the wound with another remedy, until he becomes completely healthy.
de hernie carnouse	of a hairy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case I never found anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done just as the knot which holds the vein in place, by a certain manner that you tie the ligatures, after cutting up above them lightly below; then cut into it, and cure the abscess that occurs, until the ligatures stop bleeding; and cure him so as we have said, until he becomes completely healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the hairs, if it muffles and heals the wound, as long as it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilitic is bound and has no appearance in the discharge, and the cauterized area is inflamed and closer to death.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of skin softening from the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the joints is softened in some men, because those that are inside them are mollified, and it can be seen; and it is necessary when treating to make the patient lie on his back, and cut the soft skin over the natural skin; then assemble the two lips onto a seam, and if you see, cut through the seams, and treat the cure as other wounds, until they are healed, and then let the hair grow.
dou chastrement	The afflicted one must let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	We know that cautery is prohibited in our law, and I would prefer not to discuss it in this book; and it is necessary for only two reasons: one is that the physician should answer when asked what cauterization entails, and what cure it involves; and the other is because we often need cauterization of certain animals for our aid, such as a bull and an ass and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that cautery is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	When we perform it by attraction, we seat the patient best on a warm water bath until the congealed blood is softened and then pulled off with your hand, until you no longer feel it.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	In the treatment of circumferencing: it is fitting that you cauterize well, and press the skin around the joints with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and strike on each joint one time, when you have thoroughly scorched them; and let none leave a small spot dry and subtle, which is near the vases; and this manner of circumferencing is milder than that made by attraction, because attraction may sometimes leave something from the skin, by reason of the luxury it desires; then cure the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	On hermaphroditic persons.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphroditic person is in two kinds of houses: one where both testicles are open like the form of a woman, or he has hair, and sometimes even no urination.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another manner is in women, it is so in both men and women, as a finger, they have it above their fingernails.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The cures for fever and hunger are as follows: to bind the tight clothes all around, and treat it like other wounds; in another manner, men whose urine leaks out through their skin around the joints have no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the itching.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Itching is a tight band placed on the natural part, until it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as bad as one finger, and that's the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to dye the superfluous itching on your hand or finger lightly; and do not press too hard, lest there be bleeding, then use another remedy until it is cured; and for another sort that appears in the mouth of the mare, and the nostrils, and sometimes bursts forth, and is like a cow, and so they called it "the old cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must copy it, as we have said the preparation, and the treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.
