des plaies	injuries
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	we have said in the division the remedy for injuries; therefore you will tell me the remedies for hands and fingers according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that injuries are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to their location or where the injury is located, and for what reason they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Things that cause injuries are caused by the impact of a stone, the cutting of a sword and knife, or an arrow, or a club or a chair, or similar things; or what they are made of according to the location of the body, if such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each injury, and I will start with simple wounds to the head, because it is remembered in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I'll translate the text line by line into English.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to let his flesh be mildened if he does not wish to recover, and so let him eat little meat, and do not give him wine, or cheese; and put on a dressing over the wound, should an abscess come, put cotton wool soaked in olive oil alone, or vinegar, into it; and if there is no boiling pus, then apply the dressing, if the wound is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, powder, as I will say something else later, and if the inflammation has moved him, then apply some ointments until he recovers.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	If the wound is great like a splinter of a spear and similar wounds, and the lips cannot be sewn together with stitches, then sew them together, if possible, as I will say about the belly wounds, by suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered of bone, and it is cut, and it clings only to a little, then strike; afterwards cure the wound with medicine, and restore cartilage in place of leather, and command the patient to eat large flesh, such as chicken and bread, just as birds, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or putrefaction of leather, and it clings to the bone, strike it completely, and let it dry, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, choose whichever you prefer, and if you find the artery, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then it is a light cure; and you should put on this powder which also unites the blood as when it has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to take an equal amount of fire cautery and dragon's blood; three parts of white calcined earth and the powder subtly mixed, and apply it to the wound and bind it tightly until it has dried well and is joined with all its blood; then tie it securely but allow it to loosen if it swells, for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes only calcined earth is used alone when there is no fire cautery or dragon's blood, but the powder has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the powder has moved the wound, especially when it is in this state, one does not put on that powder; but puts on some clean ointments or made poultices of wheat flour mixed with water and honey until they dissolve; then the doctor attends to other remedies until he heals.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If a bone fracture comes with an injury and the wound is small, if you pinch it gently; and I will tell you hereafter about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is in the neck and it is small, if there is no difference between the two wounds on the head, but if the vein or artery of the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's the vein, then there is only one thing to do: let the cure take its course, and don't put anything on it that would restrain it, because it will cause the veins to retract; and don't put anything on the wound, because it won't help, for the substance of the veins is cold, and the continuation of the flow so is with the brain, which is in the upper part of the body, but if you have any medicine, such as calomel laved in sweet water, and melted with olive oil, and apply the calomel also in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, then tie with bandages, afterwards cure until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and he is beheaded and full of blood, pierce or lower him; and if the arteries are cut, and there comes blood, tie off, and apply the dressing, because it must be done. And if the spine of the neck is cut, or the throat, and keep the conduit guarded, because the flesh will come, so sew the wound on the collarbone, but not touch the throat, only return to its natural shape, and then immediately tie him up, and let him rest for a few days, afterwards cure with ointments of broken bones until he is healed. And if the wound has left an impression in the bone, pierce; and if there are pieces of bone, so cut them off as soon as possible, and those you cannot get, leave as long as it will not infect and become inflamed, and be discharged and made light of the issue; and if the wound is fresh, so powder on top the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has an abscess, then perform the treatment as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a pierced arrow or sword wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a cut from a lance or sword and the wound is deep, then look at the state of the wound to see if it's going bad: if so, you know that the wound is mortal; but if it's not deep and is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it or tie it shut in the first hour, nor apply a poultice to the wound unless it has been washed away to the bone; and then return to the heart and relieve the patient; but apply an attractive ointment twice a day; if you don't have ointment, put fine cotton in the wound to soak up the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if no pain comes, nor does there come a bad pulse, or any other signs of death; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounded with stitches and other cures, until he is healed; and if she cannot be cured, or heal, then know that there is an abscess; if the treatment is done as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, deep, or on the back, then treat the wound before it; if it is large, suture; and if it is small, powder; and if it has pierced into the bone, and cut out pieces, as it pleases, let the infected parts fall off; and if they do not fall off, leave the wound to fester, so that the extractions will ease the pain; and for other wounds of other members we have already decided.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a stomach drop
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I will translate the text line by line into English.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	In the cold, warm it in this way: moistened with a sponge or one-half of a cloth in water alone, or you cook in water scalding and sulfur and pepper, and remove the swelling as long as the intestine is inflamed; and once done, press wine to restrict it, and make it dry so that it can deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling going away, if you moisten the intestine with water or boil it high and bitter, because this is easy to clog the entry with a little substance; and if it cannot enter, then do a small wound on the instrument with which one strikes the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is dry that it shrinks, so that no one should cut it unless necessary for great need, and this is the cause of tearing: thus penetrate within the nest and avoid not, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines leap out, you must reset it to its natural form in its own place, if you have the power, for this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on his back, with his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should put his head and belly higher than his limbs, so that when there is a rupture of the intestine in one of two parts, you will be in contact with that part which has the navel higher than the other. And thus, according to what I said, this applies to great and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is available to you, then have the poor minister who is skilled in suturing hold one half of the skin with his hand. Then take your needle and thread a strong yarn; and sew through both skin layers until you reach that part, and assemble the two edges together. Then tie a double thread around the needle at one quarter turn; then assemble the wound by sewing again as you did before, until the whole wound is closed. For this type of suture is most convenient for small wounds, because it uses one pair of needles with a medium-sized yarn, which is common. When you have sewn all four layers together, tie the needle at the starting point in the way that one dresses a horse; and put space between each stitch equal to the thickness of half a penny. This suture takes seven stitches, and I used one hundred stitches to close an injury on one person's belly, who had been stabbed with a sword, which was about two palms wide, and it tore through two palms of intestines as well; and it was in the lower part of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I'll translate the text line by line into English:
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physicians had judgment that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointments, because I was in exile where there was no one to be found, nor any medicine; and I applied poultices more on top of the wound two times a day, and washed it with water from honey until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and thread from the part in front of it to that inside; when it has pierced the vein of right into right, so as to cut off or sew with the knife which you have placed the needle, and punctured it on the other side from the part in front of it to that inside; and this is how the suturing should be done, just like how the shoemaker makes his shoes, leaving one side of the skin once, and covering it up with the other, until the suturing is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	In the second manner of sewing, which the Gauls call properly, it is done in this way: whoever does it, joins the two parts together naturally and calls one of the nails on one chief to another chief in this manner: make a needle or nail close by the chief of the hair, and pierce that solely, and leave both joints of the hair; then turn the needle, and pierce from the back side just as close to those bones as before, leaving both joints of the nail; then pierce one and the other from the back side just as close to those bones as before, on two nails on the opposite side; and that is the most common manner of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Gauls say that this is the word, and no one testifies to it, that you must sew the belly with two needles, if there's thread in each; and you must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other side, as those who sew wounds do; and note that when the wound is exposed on the belly, the sewing is more painful than on the other bellies.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgement of the wound is such as that of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound whole to its sinew, so that the art has moved it, then remove the intestine, and the cost; afterwards put on powder in linen cloth, and if the art has moved it, put on any ointment present, until the wound heals; and cut the thread, and sew the suture, and the mirror; then cure the wound as other wounds, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, so put on it, as soon as it comes to grieve with bowels, cotton wool, and move II times a day till it be healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of other medicine besides these dispositions when wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound makes commonality with the principal members, then it is convenient to apply a lightweight linen cloth soaked in hot turpentine oil, or rose oil, between the arms, and under the axles; and if it causes pain or putridity in the bowels, and this often happens, so the clisterize of black wine tedium, and meanwhile when putridity comes just to the intestine, you pierce through it, and see that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "youth" cannot heal when they are injured, and this is because of the plant-like qualities of veins, and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity to its natural state.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the vein bursts from the wound, and you remount it with the intestine, as fresh as possible; and if it becomes old and darkened, and its color has turned black, then it is advisable to cut out the black one, for there will be no more bleeding, because there are veins and arteries; then strike that which is between the ligature, and hang the two heads down from the lower part of the wound until the vein bleeds, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the burn of a fire
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is swollen, and the wound is small, if it can be restored in some people, for this reason I have seen that one man was wounded or pierced in the belly of a lance; and it was the wound on the right side of the stomach, and became inflamed and turned into an abscess, and from there came emission and vomiting; I put him to cure according to what I knew, and did not stop subtilizing until he was healed, and the pain subsided.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the sick person had illness in his belly; and there was no pain, but he recovered in good health, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when a small wound is in the intestine, it must be tied in a certain way: take large strings to great testicles, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the string has bitten over the mouth, put two lips on top of it, so that they strain his mouth shut; and then hit the head, and this stays so that he cannot untie it, and then place another string after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely healed; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, and ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, and se puet on lier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, in this manner: take the head of this thread from intestine that is much descharnez, and then tie to the head of this fine linen thread twisted, then pour the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it back in the rut; and this method of sewing is not fiery than according to the way of faith and expectation; and if the wound is great and wide, the same when it is in one of the intestines' grains, so there is no strength nor health but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or if it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	The hurt or abscess, when it grows old, is called "fistula" universally, and itself when it is swollen and bowed.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is according to the nodulation of the skin that is free from hard and bony growth, or when one does not feel pain, and it looks like a swelled vein of a bird; sometimes it appears clear and swollen, and sometimes thick, sometimes little, and sometimes enough; I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no ulcer, it is caused by fire only for one of the seven causes: namely, because of the smallness of the wound or body; or by malice; or because it has hard flesh inside, and above the lips, which does not allow the flesh to heal; or it has too much swelling; or the juice is poor, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in treatment; or because it is a corruption, which is the manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is delayed in digestion, and late in health, and flees by nature; or it has veins or bones: I have shown all these causes, signs, and remedies for medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you of the treatment for fistula which is made by work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	There are fistulas in all the limbs of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries, and muscles, or to the sac, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and it is known that when they arise in relation to a principal limb and have the same characteristics as them.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas of this kind are of ill health and only have labor and ignorance, and if there is any fistula that does not come from what I said, and you trust in a cure and observe its appearance, if the fistula is straight, tie it with an iron or thread; and if it is bent, find a subtle attempt to pierce, for the pierces are folded under the tortuosity; and if the fistula has lost fingers and cannot be found easily by attempts, pierce it on one of the missing fingers, because the moisture is short in one of the missing fingers, and cleanses; then apply your skill that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressing with your hand, and where they feel it; and when you know truly where it is, and if it is near a joint, nerve, artery, or vein, or any of those things I told you, copy according to what I said, and pierce carefully the source, and remove the rotten flesh and corrupted parts that are inside; and then treat the fistula until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in straight direction, tie it as deeply as possible, whenever you can, and then apply moistened medicine to its head, until the superfluity that was left at the bottom corrodes; and then apply healthy salves on the skin, until it is healed; and if it does not heal by these means, cauterize it as we said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, pierce.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	The patient or surgeon should not cut the vein or nerve if they are swollen and inflamed, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and pus, he should wait until the corruption is all gone, then treat the wound with hot poultices as long as it is clean; and if it's not clean, and the bowels will not come down as before, see that you are not going to make things worse: if you expose and scrape so much that you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb; and if he is thus cleansed, it's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, see that the corruption has gone too far, and you cannot do anything: if there's no other remedy but to put on bandages of nature; and if there's little bone corrupted, and you can treat it with tongs, if the instrument is suitable for that; and if there are many bones, take them all off, don't leave one behind; and if moisture makes against you, and there's no fear or doubt, strike and apply heat and poultice, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	Et if you do not pull them out after an hour, so put on the wound a poultice for purification, and let it remain until the pus is within the bones, and then they will have lighter bones; and if this is one large bone, such as the leg or thigh, then remove only the corruption until the blackness is completely removed from the bone, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corrupted flesh, and it comes close to the bone; so you should clean and cover all around the corruption, and then treat the patient until he is cured; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in one man's leg, so that you take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	It was a young man under thirty years old who had pain in his leg from an inner cause that came out of the body, so much that the materials came to the leg, and he fled from a big abscess, and did not have any other reason to open it; but because of their foolishness they opened it further up so that the abscesses opened, and they corroded a lot of material, and a fistula formed, and many people were suffering from pain and swelling of the body; and after two years no doctor had any cure in the art of hands, until I was called, and came to his leg and the medicines they used to treat him, and what corroded by the abscesses caused great disease; and his skin turned red like the color of citrine.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I made a mistake. This text is not a medieval medical treatise.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I have hastened and cut into one of the wounds so that I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corroded and pierced, and there was corruption coming from within the bone; I knew what appeared to be the corroded bone, and thought there could be no other corruption, except for that which I had taken out; and I began to restore the wound with medicines since for a long time, but it did not heal; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corrosion continuing in the bone, and knew it, and then put it back, and thought of suture it; but I could not do so until I cut into a palm-sized portion of the bone, and pulled it to its full size, then restored it with medicines; and it was healed and sutured quickly, and did not require restarting the work for only the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often happens, but the patient becomes entirely healthy, and an iron cage forms in place of the bone, and he is of good disposition and has no harm or evil at all, neither at rest nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, so that it wishes to be treated in this manner: take a rope, and pull the ligament at the head of the bone which opens, and command that anyone holds it outwards; and take another rope of linen thicker than the first, and tie it above the iron cage that is covering the bone, and extend the head, so that you draw the iron cage downwards, and uncover the charred part underneath, where you see it begin to rot, that it may not be stained with blood; and put a thorn or a tablet below the bone to cover up the corrupted part; and wish it to dry as much as can be seen and felt, and wish for it to dry again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh; then put a tison under, and then sew one part to another the corruption, and so sew over long of the corruption by as much as we have said; and if corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and sew over the bone where it contains from the other side; and if corruption is in the continuity of two joints, then there is no other flesh than in covering; and if corrosion is on the nail of the finger or on the nail of the toe, then this thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must inquire about that corruption, how it opens; and cleanse it with all kinds of methods as much as you can, but without causing harm to the vein or the nerve; and learn what the incisors and the sewings are for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and fineness, and their hardness.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	When the joints are infected either because of something inside them or because of something outside, and when you have treated the inflammation with medicine and it does not help, if necessary cover that part up to where the infection is coming from, so that the patient escapes death by that means, or by the malice, which is greater, the weakness of the limb; and there are signs for this: the limbs become blackened, as if they were burned with fire, and after blackening, it goes through one part of the body to another, and takes by all parts of the body; if you hasten to cover up, and it is because of the impact of some poisonous beasts, such as scorpions from the sea and viper, and similar things, if there is an infection on the head of the two, then hit at it, but do not give any space before coming close to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Et she comes just on the hand, if it strikes the joint, so that no corrosion comes before the arm; and if she comes to the arm, strike at the elbow; and if she passes by the elbow, it is death, and there's no use burning anything else but the quantity of its virtue; and do this in such a way when corruption comes to the bone: if she comes on the first joint, strike after the other joint; and if she comes on the bone, strike all the bone; and if she mounts up on the knee, strike at the joint above the kneecap; and if she comes over the kneecap, there's no other help but to kill the patient with a belt; and the manner of striking or binding the limb is that you tie it over and under, and extend some sashes one below and another above, and serve the cloth which is between the two sashes at an interval of a thumb's breadth, until the bone is exposed; then strike or bind, and put on both sides a strip of linen, so that the bandage does not touch the healthy part, and comes to the patient with another injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the elephant
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that grows under the elephant's foot or hand, or sometimes in other parts; and when it is small, and no care is taken for it, if it becomes a chasm, the patient runs about and makes a geyser, running as long as she can reach the root of the elephant, and by chance, she may run all the way to the bone, causing great pain and stench, and the wounds become wide open, and the color is fastened.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés. Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The fire cautery is a great aid when the bones are healthy, and the joint is healthy; and if the joint presses on the cartilage, and begins to pierce it, so that the blood flows, then it is fitting that you put the plaster under the joint, pointing towards the cartilage, and putting the stick inside, and striking at that subtle and gentle point, and laying down the remainder of the cartilage with medicines hot and corrosive to remove all; then apply ointments until he is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, if you strike and remove it, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be cured; and if you see the corruption spread, strike at it from within, just as was said before, then cure until he is healthy; and if it is inflamed, and ointment, and it feels great pain, it is fitting that you first heal him, then strike the joint with a sharp point, cutting across it on top, and be careful not to let the cut go deep into the cartilage below, because the patient will feel too much pain; and if he has, put something above which will ease his suffering.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from a lump in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The swollen limb of some people is often filled with blood in the hands of men by chance; and sometimes there is an abscess or bones, and not even a single joint swells up, nor does birth occur at the root of any joint.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those that swell in neither joint nor bone do not move, and those that swell at the joint by chance may or may not move. The weight of one who is swollen becomes lighter in this manner: the size of such swelling is proportional to its root in a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that swell at the root of the joint are grievous to cure: if they cling to the copper.

Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The patient who comes to the assembly is either by birth, or by sudden accident of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.

des vils	Old age
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The large veins become swollen and filled with melancholy fluid, which comes out in greater numbers on the limbs of the body; and it is more common in those who go to bed and lie down, who work and carry burdens, rather than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not administer any purging of gallstones, and then apply the basilic.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron remedy is done in two ways: one way is to cut them and treat the black wound; and the other way is to tie a vein and apply it from top to bottom.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting remedy is done in this way: first raise the leg with hot water very strongly until the thick flesh is exposed, then strain the diseased leg from above down to the knee joint; then cut the vein at one, two, or three places, depending on how wide it is, then clean and apply the black wound by hand from head to toe, so that no more of a flow occurs than what the patient's virtues can bear; and then tie it and command him to eat meat containing black gall; and repeat the evacuation and healing whenever the veins are full, and this hurts the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is cut and twisted and gathered together, and it is not straight, as we have said, it is necessary that you break it forcefully, but do not cover it up; and pull it out as we have said before.

de la voinne civile	of the female body.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This female body is tied in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and on dry land where there is no moisture; and by chance it grows somewhere else than in the legs, and this happens because of putrefaction that comes from below the skin, as if the serpent were coming out from inside the body towards the flesh, binding between skin and cartilage.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein surgery are that he comes to the knee a great inflammation, then change his clothes, and begin the vein to force out, like a root of an herb.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the joint is cut open, it is advisable to wrap around a piece of linen from one and a half fingers' width to two and a half fingers' width, up to the knee, and leave the linen on the leg, and at all times when there is no danger, wrap the linen around the knot, and the new flesh; and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cover its root, until it is completely gone; for if you cut it, it will return to the cartilage, and cause abscesses and putrefaction in that place, and a bad disease; therefore, this thing must be treated little by little, until the head, and leave nothing of it inside the body; and sometimes this vein is treated when it is two palms long, or X, and one hand's width away, I came to see someone to whom it emerged from X palm's length, and when you cut it, it spouts I or more, and a piece perforates, and the root reaches the bottom, so that everything comes out; and if there is no material left inside, take the patient medicine daily for putrefaction, and treat him as one with abscesses.

And sometimes this vein is filled with rain, and most of the time when it opens in the joint of the foot, or the foot itself, and a great deal of blood comes out, and from which it often rains; then cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between the leather and the bone
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "bovine sickness" in our land because it has often caused cows to be sick, and it is a small worm that is born between the leather and bone, and moves throughout the entire body, ascending and descending, and causes great pain in every limb until the skin splits or it emerges, and escapes; and it is infested with rotting humors, just like serpents, worms, lice, and other parasites in the belly; and one doubts its malicious nature, because when it moves through the body, it rises to the head, and sometimes enters the eye, and causes destruction there; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you look to cure and treat it, if only fire is used when it is necessary: then it is therefore necessary that you tie the limb both above and below with a strong bond tightly, then strike up and treat it, and if the venom enters deeply into the flesh, and you do not see it, then cauterize with fire on top, until it dies; and the greatest harm that it causes is that it runs oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming near to the head or close by the oil, then tighten down beneath it the sorcery form, then strike up, and treat it; and it is necessary to use the patient with medicinal substances for purifying the flesh, solutes, for bad humors poured out, and to eat inedible food to purge.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and moves from member to member; and I have seen this, which I will tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me one arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of that arm; and after a while, I saw it rise as if a worm had climbed up onto her shoulder, faster than any other thing, like living silver when it cut through the veins into another place; the pain moved away from that place, and settled in her shoulder, and then a little later ran all over the body, until she came to the other arm; and she told me she was turning around inside the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed how she moved from one member to another, because I had never seen this disease in that way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Toutevoie, I have seen that very well that many are not free from pain because of the movement of their body in another place, but I have never seen it myself, as I saw in a woman; and I thought it was for this reason that women have thin bodies, and uncovered breasts, and for this appears the winded constraint; and they do not appear like according to this reason to those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and wounds reopened.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see treating this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens itself as we said, then bind tightly above and below, and then cut on top so that the winded constraint be removed from the body; and cauterize the body; and if you do not see it in your eyes, if the doctor knows how to relieve the winded constraint, such as foul-smelling pills and serpent skins, and similar others.
des saiettes	extraction of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are different, according to their shapes and according to the nature of their bodies or where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their types is that there are those with large points, small ones, pointed tips, and nails; and those with double angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and some pierce in any member according to two ways: or in the principal member it pierces, such as brain, liver, heart, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	So when it pierces in any of these members and the signs of death appear, which I will tell you afterwards: if it suits that you take out this arrow, because the deaths come after in various conditions; and when this sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully inserted, then leave it, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l'os, and the signs that occur when a vein bursts and pierces the bone, and it jumps the space above the brain, is when there is scotomia and pain and swelling and redness of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and commotion of understanding, and vomiting blood; and perhaps it happens without force from the nose, or ears; and perhaps it affects the speech and voice; and it bursts out as if it were a boil on the foot, and as it does so like the sound of breaking charcoal; and when this sign appears, you must take care of the cure, and pull out the vein when it is not filled with blood.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the vein when it bursts or spouts blood is that it is near the left nipple, and feels like it has been pierced in something hard, not swollen; and perhaps the vein stops bleeding like a boil, and comes with cold sweat and cold pain, and fainting; and one must be cautious then, because death may result.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that does not break without swelling of pus from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns, and they gasp loudly and seek relief from the pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow chokes in the covering of the thigh, so it lies in the small ribs, and there is great swelling and great pain, and they gasp; and all their limbs move with the shoulder.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow chokes in the stomach, by chance, it jumps from the wound and eats up some of the indigestible meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow chokes in the belly and does not break up and pass through the intestine by chance, so that there is no hope for the cure or the removal of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow is shot into the bladder, and it flows out in a stream, and comes out of the body, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, just as the flesh and the skin and the throat and the shoulder and the arm and the back of the spine and the rib cage and the chest, and the limbs resembling them, are saved according to various cases.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, just as I told you it happened to me, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened in a house with an arrow shot through the cheek or temple near the nose: I tried to extract it, and drew it out from beneath the fatty tissue of the ear, and he was cured suddenly.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And tie an arrow to the end of a rope that is in the fat of the oil under the paper, and the arrow was tied, and could only be reached at its tip, which was very heavy for one ear, and the arrow was as big as a Turkish bow, weighing all these metals; it was used with great ease before our ears, and did not bring any bad accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And tie an arrow on the neck of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow on his head: I plucked the beards, and I made it so delicate that I could tie it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And tied an arrow on the home that was fallen in or out of his stomach, and I thought he was dying; and then after thirty days, he did not improve at all; I made a cut on the arrow, and put it in, and it worked well, and there were no bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who has an arrow stuck in his chest or in the back, and the wound was closed up; and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not recover from his natural disposition, nor finds any trouble in any of his works by nature.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man who has an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound was closed up; and he suffers for a long time with great pain, and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.
