And there was an arrow stuck in the king's man who had been wounded by an enemy, and he was leaning to the right side; and the arrow was repulsed. I was summoned to the healer after this, three days having passed.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I asked for line by line translation. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I put on the left side of the abdominal stomach, because that’s where the liver swells; and it appeared to me that the liver of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on the hands every day, and solved the wound directly above it, and kept the patient there for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his chest; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put the medicine onto the wound with acid corrosive every day, until it was open, and tried it, and felt the head of the arrow which dried up in the liver; then adjusted the opening of the wound by that medicine, so that the joints of the arrow appeared visibly; and pierced very well the ends for four months, and then saw if the wound I had sewn with tight stitches, from one side and another, would come out; and could not; therefore I did not stop subtlety and ingenuity in making instruments, until I took it one day with perfectly made stitches, according to what came about at the end of this chapter, as I tried, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it then, and the wounds were healed, and the patient was completely recovered.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of extracting arrows, so that you apply your care to what I do not tell you, for the books cannot know everything; but the wise masters understand much better little things, and those who are present and faltering, find new work and new instruments, at the descent of extraneous things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not enter the body through any member where they are pierced except for two kinds: either by the way it enters or by another part; and whichever one is pierced by arrow now, that's an arrow entering the charnel house, and has happened before.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Instruct the patient to let her sleep until the flesh is rotten and putrid, and when she comes out, take the issue; and so if she is fixed in the bone and cannot come out, let her be thus for some days, and every day it moves, and then she will come out, and if she does not come out, pierce through all inside to make her come out, until the swelling subsides, and then take her.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	But if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head and has just come into one of the cavities of the brain, and among the accidents that I have said to the patient: if you do not treat her, but let her sleep until she is even after some days, because if the arrow comes just beneath it, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck only in the bone, and does not reach that far, and the patient stays in bed for a few days without another accident, so it gets stuck there again.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck that way and cannot come out for long, so administer tartarized wine, as I have told you; then treat the patient until they are well.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned to the body in a person who cannot see it, and they are entirely covered by a sheet; and if you feel it, but there is no convenient tool to reach it with; and if you cannot stretch the wound or penetrate deeply enough to find bone or nerve, if you press as hard as possible on the spot where the wound is large; then pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears in the part where it is stuck, if they hold tight, remove the bone that is embedded with two parts per inch as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow so that you can pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, if the law is until the left joint is swollen, then take it out, for extraction removes pain.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the blood of pain is in opposition to this, if you do what we have said about the cure in that chapter; and take care of the incision on the nerve and the vein, and put it in so that you can treat the arrow wound safely, soon or late, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form in which he was when the arrow hit him, because this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do so, then put him according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	When an arrow comes from the other side, or it is blocked with something, or the skin is swollen in that direction if you see or feel it beforehand: take then a bigger size, until the pincers can get hold of it, and then draw it out; if now it has come.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand around completely, until it enters the bone and widens the bone, then pull.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, so leave it alone for now, and then start extracting again until it comes out; and if the arrow is stuck in the wound, then pour it down into the entire shaft; and if it has been shot out, and you see that you must administer ointment, so administer a dressing with an instrument head, so that the tip of the arrow goes into the hair of the instrument; and then pour again, and if the arrow is stuck in the hair, pour the instrument with its pointed end in, to relieve the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, then it is advisable that you copy all the hair on or where the venom is, if you can; and then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	In case the arrow sticks in or near the stomach or bladder or at the ribs, and it is close to the vein and nerve, cover it up if you can; and keep the vein and nerve covered. Then pull it out, then sew the wound, as need be; and cure so long as it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs used to remove arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and it is thus:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they are made in many forms: large, medium-sized, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the nail that clamps hair is also like the feathers of a bird, to push against the tip of the arrow, as it is thus:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of nails for pounding and stitching, if this is so:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins in the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins from which one is cured are XXXI, because it has sixteen heads, that is to say: two fingers that are after the ears, called the "soft herbs"; and two arteries in each temple appearing; and two veins that are in two cheekbones of the two eyes, called "aspirets"; and a vein in the middle of the forehead; and a vein in the head with no nose; and two tendons in the neck; and two veins above the lips of the mouth, which are called "augeherichs"; and two veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that heal commonly are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it is located on the left side of the shoulder, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the middle is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the spleen, and that one heals visibly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the vein is where the auriculaire and anulaire meet, and there are two veins; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the ear pouch on the left side of the shoulder, and the second is at the ankle joint on the right side; and the third vein called "nèse" is in the other ankle joint; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The veins that are behind the ears can help with ancient purgatives and migraines; and the qualities of these veins, as I tell you, are that you raise the patient's head, and rub the leather or the veins with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with one finger, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two levels on the head: whichever appears first, and when you feel your pulse underneath it, signify "enche"; then take the lancet, and push it through below the vein to the bone, then raise your hand all along the vein upwards, strike and remove the skin as much as possible, and make the wound open until you see; then strain and tie, until it is healed; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sickness of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the sickness of the head with diseases of the face ancient, and migraines, and redness; and the qualities are such that the patient strains his neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "surgical", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and pierce upwards from your hand, or with another thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then free the patient's neck, and tie the vein so that it is healthy and never again overflows with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	But it is not good that the flames are too large; and the healthy vein cut across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The injured from two veins that are in two lamellars should be held with the eyes and at the tinge and redness and at the orifice in the oil and for diseases of the face; and those who have this injury so are that the patient strains his neck by twisting any thread, as before; then heal, and if there is a healing through the passage, one small near the long flame one small large, because it has no care.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance it breaks; then make a stitch through the wound, as much as you have need, and then tie up above, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The wound of the vein on the nose is very valuable, and it is a serious source of fever, and diseases of the face, so as emigraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old; and those who have this injury are that the patient strains his neck, then strain his nose with your left hand, and take a subtle long flame, and poke it in the gap between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in which, and now the healing begins; and do not go too far in front, and make a stitch through the wound according to your need, then tie it one night, for it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The sick are helped by the tightening of the vein, and at the beginning of surgery, and with a great deal of diseases, and with empedigine, and with corrosion, and with herpes, and itemones; and the qualities of the sickness are such that the patient strains his neck to one side and to the other, just as we have said; and let the masters be standing above the head of the sick person, and the patient lie on the second seat, then pierce the vein of the long finger slightly wider, then pull out the diseased tissue temperately, until it is necessary; then do it again in the other vein, then release the bandage, and tie around the veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke; and let him just rest in the morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the infection of the fingers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The wounded veins on the lips are aided by applying coal in the mouth and causing corruption of gums, fissures of lips, and discomfort.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the wound are such that you should sit the patient in front of you, and bind his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, where one is on the right lower lip and the other is on the left lower lip, which you can recognize by their color and by the fine black veins inside them. Hit therefore one and the other, and if you do not know them, hit the larger of each part, and similarly do the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the wound below, the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The patient's veins that are below the tongue aid after the treatment of the head, and it is at the constriction of the throat, and with diseases of the eye, and with diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of a good healer if it is such that the patients sit in front of you under the sun, and lift the tongue, and look down at each side one vein black: heal then both, and do not go too far because under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the hand which are commonly cut off are cut according to two manners: either by puncturing at a full-flamed mint leaf large, or olive oil subtle as it cuts the nails, and are called "anesil"; and are large and subtle according to the size and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of fire is well known, and it is widely recognized as being very effective; and its size is like what you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins of the forehead, which contain clear, large blood and trouble; for this is the form of fire olive oil.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is subtler in its application, and is for healing the fine veins, or it has subtle citrus blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basil oil, which is one of these veins, greatly helps with diseases below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and it is fitting that the healer should apply this oil, and that he should draw out the artery that is under.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood comes out as it did; and so you must cauterize, just as I said; and do not be squeezing the flame, but cut it like a donkey.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the ligature does not open clearly, so that you must extract it, and replace another one; or if you want rain on it, or if you heal with a vein in the arm where it was: it opens clearly; and cut it at the flame like we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the vein of the wound, so that you must also extract the arm, where you touch the joint until you know the bones; then mark the vein with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein at the flame like we said; and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the vein swollen, for it is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it rises high like the urine of a child, and is red and subtle, know that it's without an artery: hasten then, and apply your poultice long on it, then take away your poultice when it doesn't bleed, for this happens many times; bind the arm, and leave it so, and don't move the patient's limb; and be cautious, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If it doesn't bleed when you apply pressure, and swells, and the medicine is not present, then cut into the artery if it opens up, because the head of the artery will retract; and press hard.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a scraper of the fistula and make it, and take one of the halves and tie well to the other tomorrow; if it doesn't bleed, it's good; if not, then the healer, as we have said, applies the powders that stop bleeding; and the bleeding is less painful in more difficult dispositions for small wounds, and for the strength of the ligature on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	In the middle of the vein's disease is treated in such a way that it treats wounds on the head above, and under the body, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and to the lord that he should be careful about the nerve below, and if he pierces too close and cuts it, and it swells and the sickness spreads, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person for its subtlety, then it is wise to clean with the instrument aseptic before using it; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, so that it swells longer.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The sickness of the cephalic is treated, so it treats wounds on the head, and aids the eyes; and it is wise to treat with pointed olive oil or pointed myrtle, because it is the most safe of all veins, because there are below neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Everyone seeks to get better quickly, and let nothing trouble you the first time, and start again; and by chance, if it happens that the limbs swell up in some people, but they do not trouble anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that health cannot be preserved except by taking care of it, and by avoiding the diseases that come; and if someone seeks to heal in one of the three veins: head, chest, or liver; because these are the places where health and sickness reside; and should be healed at the beginning of prayers for fasting, in autumn and winter after eating, when they perceive the sign of repletion; and should be healed on the first day or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The sick who are being served do not have a fixed rule for treatment, but rather when they need it by day or night in all hours and at all times; and it is not advisable to heal children up to the age of 12, nor women carrying a full moon only until six months past.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not heal old men who have passed the age of sixty.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	If anyone wishes to be healed in any way, then it is advisable that they first lighten the intestines with a light purgative if he has retained much bile, so that the veins do not carry out waste from the intestines, which are harmful to the principal members; and do not heal those who are too salty of meat, nor those who are suffering from dropsy, whether it is caused by hunger, or vomiting, or constipation of the stomach, and frequent urination with woman, and toil, watching, and lying down; for this is the true virtue, whether through arms or body; then subtle the humors, since they are not large, by food and drink and medicines, and apply them as needed; then take a bath if nothing is forbidden, to subdue the sickness, and get healthy from the vein under the third joint, as we have said; and be careful that day of work, and pain, and luxury, and such similar things; and be quiet and patient, and be more careful than those who are healed, and rub the arm twice or thrice, then loosen the bandage in the middle, because when it is too tight or too loose, he cannot be cured without; and then rub the clean area with hands, until the veins swell, and they can feel it on; then apply a poultice made from the flame of a small amount of old oil, and put his thumb-sized portion of his left hand over that vein below where one wishes to heal, so that the vein does not burst and fail.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, and there are veins that flow just like a string to the healer, and those of such that are filled with windiness, so when one puts on the flame, it retracts again, and cannot open the vein, and thus is done for those; and if you heal the vein, then the wound is too tight, therefore it is wise for the healer to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it is good; but if not, then start again over in a small part below or above where it is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is present, and the patient is afraid, let him stay one day or two, and do not bind his arm: by chance a boil may come up; or he will not enter the bath, then start again with the treatment as it pleases; and if the puncture is small, cut through it subtly and when you doubt that it will not bleed so much as you see, be confident in that same puncture directly; and open it slightly, so that the swelling may come out; for this has happened many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swollen limb, do not resume the treatment again, and apply a small amount of lard oil to it, because it lightens the body with the wound, and is numb in this limb like the oil; and thus administer the oil in each wound that you heal, to soothe the swelling of the wound; and doing the same thing, tie and bow with it when placing it on the limb; but subtlety remove and spare it when it becomes too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess that has happened many times, at the same time as the vein is only open at those times or when opening the vein is small, hasten and apply to the limb a moist sponge in water and with some warm cloth, and bind it for an hour; and it is likely that you will do this after the issue of the wound from the vein, and if it remains on the limb after some days without any harm or benefit, then it does not bother you; and if you see, apply some aloes or mirror remade in juice of camphor, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance at the opening of the basilica: therefore take your hand up, and if you find it soft to the touch with pressure of the hand, that is then a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid putting anything on it that we have said, for by chance you may cut without an artery; but make the wound dry first to harden the limb, then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue and its blood color.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it issue until it becomes red; and if you see a lot of pus, let it issue until it becomes thin; and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for him who is strong and hardy, with a need for bloodletting, to make the wound larger and the incision wider; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it will be better for him and more frequent, and he must be healed in cutting across, not by pricking.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose blood must be given to the healing, it is fitting to give him a moist pain in the juice of quince grapes; if he is hot, then draw off the blood three times or four times. And if his complexion is cold, then make him eat before the healing a moist pain in syrup made from mulberries, or in aromatic syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a most fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If the patient has a hand wound after a lot of bleeding, then it is appropriate for him to drink broth of char, and sweet syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If he wants to separate some limbs and cure again, when it is appropriate, because he is weakened by great bleeding, he will recover little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	Who wants to separate some limbs after the first bleeding and has strong flesh, will recover in 7 hours after the first bleeding, or on the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to cure of another kind, so that he should be cured on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein is opened, then let it be left and do not restrain it more, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If it needs to be treated again after the first treatment, whether with the same hand or in another vein, or on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that is cut in the arm is healthy because of the head, as it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the healing when it is healthy, if the patient pours hot water on their hand, until the swelling subsides; then tie it moderately, so that the vein appears well, and now heal through it, not too thinly nor too thickly; and if it has large punctures, and they are healed near the joint of the hand, if without any complications, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the wound heal in the water, until you have had enough; and if it has been so, do not pour the hand again in hot water, because it is more advantageous to put it in cold than in heat; and healing of this vein is safer than all other veins.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sickness of the salvation of the right hand is worth all the diseases of the belly, and it is thus: strain the hand, and pour in hot water, until the vein opens, if one sees; and if the wound is to cross, and if you tap all over, do not grieve anything; and do not go too far by force, for the nerves are out of order before they get numb, and then put the hand back into hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and will come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have cut into the wound as much as is necessary to it, put on the vein oil and silk to bind tightly, and do so for every wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness of the vein in the left hand is worth the disease of the mouse, and do it exactly as I told you on the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the spleen is worth more than all other illnesses that are outside the body, just as illnesses of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the rain, and of the thighs and old joints, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his spleen are that if the patient drinks some stone in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it dies, and puts above the joint on his foot; and the vein is above the ankle, and from above the foot go a lot of rain; then it is healed, either because the rain has increased or it has come to the ankle.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it above the foot, so as to ward off the ones that are underneath, and the healing through traversing like cutting; and let the inflammation subside.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If he cannot come out on his own, then place his foot in water, and let it well empty the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	If the vein is damaged for the first time, start again on top by a little, because the veins are salty; do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and so make the sponge of the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the scrotum is at the ankle of the foot, and its soreness equals the pain of the haunch, when it is cut.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the quality of his soreness is such that he drinks wine and draws it out above the ankle, and you bend it four times by twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then clean it in all ways as you can, and across; and beware that you copy it, because the veins are swollen, and they are much prone to bleeding with wet hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you don't find it, then look for a man with a rain or wound open on the back of his foot, and towards the little toe, and guard yourself from harm; and do as much bleeding as possible until you see, and then release the bandage, and put cotton on and bind it again; he is now cured.
des sainies de ventouse	from the wounds of suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or of pitch, or of needles; and suction is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing the wound, or by piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction when it is done by piercing and drawing the wound is also in two ways: either by applying fire all over, or by applying heat; suction that is made by piercing and extracting the blood if is made in 13 places of the body, because some are at the top of the head; and others in the neck; and there are two others on each shoulder; and one under the chin; and one on each elbow; and one above the knees; and the suckers on both arms; and the suckers on both legs; and the suckers on both ankles; and it does not treat with wounds, except for small veins scattered throughout the flesh, because thus no harm comes to anyone, as we do with veinletting; and is not advisable at all when made by fire or heat in any disease that comes from overfilling, until the entire body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and myself too, when it is in the middle of my month, we command to ventouse after three hours on the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The pain of the head is aided by the grip of the chief ... when it comes to the eyes, and should not be done except after evacuation of all the body; and this ventousation is in place of the sainie of the cephalic, and should not be used by one who has cold complexion, or who has catarrh, because this causes great harm to them; and for that reason it should not be used by those who have a cold headache.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it, often become blind, and for this reason they must put the ventouse a little more below by the doubt of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wound on the neck is in the place of the vein of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it requires strictness of the arm, and tearing of the channel of the belly, and burning, and filling; and they should not be touched too much, because if she holds it too tightly, it will cause obliquity or stomach pain and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosation has two knots on the neck, and it causes head pain, eye problems, and emigraine, and strangling, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in the place of the basilica vein; and you must command the master that he presses his hand to apply, so as not to cut the artery, and do not be cautious.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventosation under the chin causes mouth illness and gum corruption, and similar illnesses in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of both cheeks.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are worth the disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the sides are worth as much as three veins in the arm, because they bring forth blood from those large veins; and instruct the master not to pierce too deeply, for the veins are bare of flesh, and know beneath the nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The windings that are above the loins are worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for other diseases, and it is necessary to make the woundings large, and made of earth, so as to properly treat them; and by chance, if they are subtle, they will break, and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The windings of the legs heal openly, because they bring forth blood from all the body, and are worth for ancient pains in the rains, in the belly, and in the bladder, and cause to wither; and are in place of two spleens, and two knees, and whatever way they may weaken the body after long use, they bring on fainting in more severe dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Instruct the patient to put on the ventouse first when it is empty and suitable, and then apply it immediately, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the limb red and swollen, and the redness spreading over the wound. Then, remove the ventouses, and take care in the arrangement of corpses, because there are those who have such a strong heart, and sharp teeth: if it is necessary to strike only once, and it is suitable to make large wounds, and deep ones; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is not large, so that you may cut it two times: the first time to open up the large vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very thick, it may be necessary to cut it a third time; and when we try to extract the vein little by little, we should only do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	Instruct the patient that if you want to bleed much, so frequently; and if the blood cannot be drawn quickly, then pierce it again and again until they do flow; and when you see the liver appear suddenly, and are concerned about those who have thick skin and hard pores, that you anoint them with oil of aperitif and dissolving; either with violet oil, or almond oil, or oil from the seed of cucumber; and if it is in the vinegar, then with cresson oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the bleeding is large and cold, then take oil of amber, or balsamite, or oil of anise, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if those who are healthy have thin skin and large pores, do not apply any oil, but rather wash with water from rosewater, cold water, mulberry water, cucumber water, porcelainberry water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, so let him rise from that place, or from water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And he who has large discharges rises from wine vinegar, or water of sycamore, or annet and camomile decoction, or other similar things; and does not wish to be treated with a poultice in front of the bath, nor after the bath for one hour or two hours; and does not sleep afterwards, but must suffer when he should be ventosed, and suffers when he is swollen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware that he who recovers is choleric, and his temper does not become too angry and inflamed; so it is wise for him to take cold things, such as pears, grapes, endives, and lettuce at the beginning, and similar things; and eat pulse foods, and eel of wood, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, and vin odorant moien, which is between old and new, and eaten little, and eaten poutins and small fowl and pigeons; and the day he feels himself ventousera, he must drink more than he eats; and it is fitting to give some men a certain amount of three or mushy food before or after the ventosacion, or afterwards, for comforting the principal members; and be subtlety without, but it is not fitting that only those who are hot drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The ventouses that are applied to hurt are those applied on the liver, and on the mouse, and podagra, and on the belly, the bowels, the veins, and the hunchback, because this member does not suffer from being pierced, and is only done for attracting blood from one part of the body to another, as we apply them to the nipples when they are healing; to reduce the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put ventouses on the belly and bowels to ease the member; and to remove the pain, when there is opilation or stone, it removes by its attractive power by chance the opilation, or clears the stone from its place; and thus does it when you apply it on the liver and on the mouse when there is retained ventosity, and these ventouses are administered empty for sucking alone; and sometimes they are applied together with fire, and sometimes plain water, just as in such painful pleurisy, and in that manner one fills the ventouse with hot water soup, or with whatever it has cooked medicinal herbs suitable to it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered to fire so is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And two fingers of length and a half palm from the edge, so that they cut inward one inch from the middle, as if to pierce an arrow, and are soft enough before that, lest they injure the patient when placing on the member; and there is at the middle one crossbar of iron or wood, to hold a bandage in place, and they are large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the vacuum wounds of children are other than those of adults, and of thin people than of fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus you must put this vacuum on the member: wrap a candle in linen or thread, and place it inside the vacuum through the crossbar that is inside the vacuum, so that the light is at the bottom of the vacuum and does not burn the patient; then put the vacuum on the limb, and make sure your fingers are above the cuts as we said before, so when you take it away, there will be steam, and if you take it off, wrap the linen again as before, often enough if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	When the lung disease is treated with air, it has no benefit if it's not full of blood, and it should only be used when it is full of air, and placed on one member only; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sutures should only be used in members where you cannot put air-filled things, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and if they have a nosebleed, like two or three, and other similar ones; and the qualities of its use are that when you find sutures that are in salty water without causing harm, take them; and put one seed in salty water, until they become familiar, and do not have anything in their stomachs; and then come out to vein and air-filled suture, then rub the member until it is red, and put on sutures; and when they are full and swell, if this can be done, put them, because this is very after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If the skin is not inflamed, then lift the limb with care, and then in water, very well, and then inspect it; and if the limbs become too moist after removing the bandage of linen soaked in cold water, place them again, until they are dry; and if they get wet again, put vitriol broken or opium, and similar things, until they are dry; or you put over the limb a mixture of hot feathers peeled, and leave them until they sweat on the limb, so that it will be healed now; and if you have more need, then take other ointments.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the ointments do not take, then rub the limb with fresh powder, or you prick an arrow so that the wound bleeds, and then place it again, and as soon as they feel the pain, they will stop; and when you see that they shed blood, then sprinkle some powder of aloes and silk broken, or ashes, so that they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This book of fractures begins.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is necessary many times in the art of medicine, and it restores breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know well, dear son, that the art of cutting is found in this chapter, which no one among the ancient books has ever seen, nor have they read any letters about it; and for this reason, the science is lost in our land, because I never found a good one; and nothing else know I, except through the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have handled the science, and by experiment, and by my daily practice; and I have shown you here in this chapter what is contained, and condensed at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments to be used, as I have done in the two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in this prologue of this book the sums of our words and the chapters where the wise men put their understanding, and dwell on the virtue, so that those who have experienced it can learn and acquire this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or splinting comes to anyone, it is necessary to hasten to heal the sick person from one side and the other, if any thing does not hinder them, taking into account weakness of body, illness, or old age; or if the joints are too loose or too cold; and apply heat to colds, that is to say cold poultices, and char of birds and hedgehogs, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not stuff yourself too much with viands that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about pus or swelling in the member; if you revive the sick person according to the previous governance which they used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the broken bones start to heal, it is fitting that one should nourish the patient with foods that produce great swelling, such as wheat, which when cooked in water, becomes soft and sweet, like barley, and rye, and fish, and fowl, and pottage, and fat, and dried meat, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	But with swelling comes the representation of joints and bones being more easily broken.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of old people and those who are decrepit cannot be properly repaired or soldered according to their nature due to dryness of the members, neither those which are too tender, like the bones of small children; but there is no cure. Instead, take great care to reattach the bone with large tenons that secure the joint together, so that it may set as it was before; and do not let them do all their work, and for this reason they must nourish themselves with great foods, just as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or the foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that involve the arm, and others from cutting, just as the thickness of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there are fractures with wounds, and fractures with only a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own method and instrument for restoration, according to what the remembrance comes from; and it is known that fractures of the bone are recognized by the twist of the limb, and the bone opens well through the defect, and sounds with the touch of the hand; but if there is no tortuosity or pain at the toucher, and the patient feels no great pain, unless it has a fracture point; but he can still have some twisting, splitting, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not fitting to move your hand at this moment, but apply the medicines that come here afterwards, and then tighten now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.
