And know that if a fracture is in the arm, and two parts are separated, it must now be put back into place equally, so that the abscesses will come out; and if the abscesses swell, then let it rest for a day, until the swelling subsides; then put it in its proper place with ease and care, and know that restoration of one part is more easy than restoration of another where there are pieces; then tighten it, as is fitting afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if two parts are split, whether it's a large piece or a small one at hand, or both cords, or a cord and one of your hands; then put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the limb that broke are reduced, you remove all additions in their proper place, using the instruments as much as possible, and beware that through your work there does not come to the patient any new injury or pain; and add well the two nails of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the feeling is good in the hand if it seems that it is not well: if you gently draw the bow, and do not stretch it too much, nor press so as those who make it happen through their work cause a hot and contraction to the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is bent, if you tie the patient well so that it does not move, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and take care that the limb be so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not bent, and you should place it in a straight position so that it feels no pain; and take care that it be set correctly, lest tortuousness come to it when restored, and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Broken limbs are of different size and shape and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small limbs, such as arms and forelegs: wrap with soft and thin linen; and for larger ones, like thighs and legs: wrap with a wide and sturdy belt. For the larger belts crush the entire limb, and tightly bind all parts equally, so there is no gap left; then tie light ropes three or four times according to the limb, and hold tight with one hand over the whole rope, then go above the break and gently bind less, as the break will move a little away from it; and loosen the rope slightly, piece by piece, until you gain most of the healthy flesh, then take another belt, and turn around downward under the broken limb; then return to the lower part of the break, and bind moderately, not too hard or too soft, as we have said before; then put linen or cloth ties between the belts, until they are all equal, then tie everything from above with a band, and then set up your needles well, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it has an abscess or an abscess, put a soothing balm over the abscess, and if one cuts the abscess, and leaves it for some days; then strain on those stitches, and make them of a small cleft cane or of wood that makes the saws, or of palm fronds, and so according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the stitch placed on the break be one slightly larger and wider than the others; and so long as is needed for the limb whether small or large; then strain those stitches just as you did at the first application, then tie over with a thread of linen immediately, as in the first application on the break; the tighter it is, the looser, and it should be that the thread is neither too thick nor too thin, and so be made of fine linen, for if the thread is too big, like I have wanted to make works from the foolish ones who make their stitches from cord made of linen twisted, and this is a great error, because the stitch cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it should not be that there are less than two fingers' breadth between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is paralyzed by the bite of a snake after the constriction in its healthy state, so that it stops bleeding when they press on those wounds, then they should put over them cloths of linen or wool.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bones are broken, I shall tell you the treatment as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not wise to constrain the limbs of all broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the members are large, it is not wise to put splints on them for more than 5 days or 7, or longer according to the security of the abscess surrounding; and observe here the way of the ancient physicians to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: and take flour that is kept in the wall of the mill, and mix it with a great amount of milk, and make this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of using the plaster to restore fractures in various situations, and especially for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plasters that restore breaks and dislocations and torsion: take powdered arsenic and lead oxide and antimony and saffron and gum arabic and myrrh, 10 parts; mirror and aloes, 5 parts; ail, VIIII parts; and make a paste, and mix with honey and wheat flour; if the complexion of the skin is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and saves many lives.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is useful for torsion: take myrrh and viscum, 10 parts; mirror and aloes, VIIII parts; caecum, VI parts; boric Armenian, X parts, grind well, and confine with water or honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of splinting is to join and secure the bones with their limbs, and alleviate the following pain, and cut the bone; use a new linen cloth, and apply oil in ease and in oil cooked, and put it on the limb.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These splints do not restore anything, but they are good for alleviating hot abscesses and properly treating pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of splinting that restores broken bones: take dried leaves of fig and earthy leaves, crush them together, and make a splint.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of splinting for the restoration of bone fracture and to alleviate the following of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of vimsalv, camomile, violet flowers, flour of beeswax, from each one take a part; and grind, and mix with wine, and warm the limbs by mixing with wet coriander water or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of applying plaster that is stronger than the first, when an abscessed area comes to be restored on the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vimsalv, and flaxseed, balsam, myrrh, and saffron, and from all take one part; and grind, and mix with warm salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras wrote in his book that one should not put on the broken member a plaster made of wax and oil, except for that, nothing else is to be used, and he said it must be between soft and hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that you should put on the broken member, to restore, dry things with hot air, like glass, and ashes, and incense, similar to what we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of applying poultice is worth the injury and pain: take mutton fat and horse's flesh, or hen's blood, and equal quantities, mix them together, grind them, and then apply it to the wound and let it bind.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that they have moved their bone out of place; if not, loosen by hand every day. If pain comes to the limb, or prurite, with rest, or swell, hasten, and loosen, and now remove the poultice; and put on a lighter cloth, and an sponge soaked in moist water, and plunge into cold water, and lift up the limb, until the itch ceases and the pain is appeased; then let it rest for an hour, put on a dry linen, moistened with warm water or olive oil, and tie above a nut, so that you are sure of the inflammation subsiding; and keep quiet the inflammation in the member, and remove the pain, then resume gentle binding, and add a little poultice, and do not strain it too much as before; and be subtle until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that an abscess has caused redness and swelling and pain, if it has broken out all over, and you have need to draw blood and bind it, as it recurs, just like you did in the first way.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if this does not occur in the member as we have said, and you do not release it after three days or four or five, but rather leave it for twenty days, as is observed, until the fracture heals, and the surrounding area approaches, then tie it tighter than before, and fatten up the flesh, just as I said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than necessary, know that it will not heal; therefore take care of it with hot water, every three days, and let it be dressed in a similar way; by this operation, then cut off the swelling from the member, and make haste to do what the foolish surgeons do, which leaves the member deformed: this is bad, and if it does not have healing power, I see nothing else but to tie and cover it straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of breaks
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of breaks and different shapes, and the causes are predetermined; for there are breaks that are made by striking with a sword, and the collarbone is broken through to the marrow beneath it, just as if one had struck against or with the fist; and thus this kind of break is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword strikes through the bone from above to pierce it, and thus this kind of break is called "absolute"; and there are two kinds of wounds resulting from these two types of breaks: great ones or small ones.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is a penetration or a fracture in the bone of the shoulder, or through the stone, or above the shoulder on the stone, or of other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fracture near the bone, whether it is below or above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is covered with a thin membrane on the bone, just like the feathers of a bird, and the fracture is small, then this fracture is called 'capillary'; and if there is a wound made by striking a stone or by falling, or by some similar thing, which pushes the piece of the bone into the joint, and the tendons are swollen as much as they are when the caulkers burn their fingers on the cauldrons; then the bone enters the joint.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more frequently in those who have moist bones like the head of an infant, and small fragments are lost as if from stones; and I will speak on their behalf.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by pulling back on them, and questioning, and by the corrupted flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of the hair is known by this: when we discover the bone and stroke above it, if we open up the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, take care to watch for any bad accidents in the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, swelling, fainting, fever, red eyes, and other similar dispositions, then it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a most foul accident and yet you expect recovery, as soon as you begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the child comes to you for the first time, and it is in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after birth when you can do so.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	But if it is in this state, then you must hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, otherwise the infection under the bone will spread and accidents like those we have described will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes just to the cloth that covers the brain, it is fitting that you cut the broken part in this way: and be sure to grasp the patient's head tightly, and uncover the bone wherever you can, and make the incision as smooth as possible, and if blood clotting occurs while uncovering the bone or abscess, seek help accordingly, because one should fill the wound with moist cloths soaked in olive oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is calmed down, and be sure of no further bleeding; then start to remove the bone, and it is done according to two ways of work:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he uses a larger cutting than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of different cuts, some are three inches long and others larger, and they should be pointed, and made of iron, and work lightly so as not to strike the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it is advisable to pierce through it, so that you can administer cuts with a rasp, not cutting at all, lest they go through the bone into the flesh, and there must be a margin or circle around the point, so that the point does not go beyond the bone; and it is recommended to have multiple points, so that each one comes out in its place on the edge of the bone, with raspers for every test, and this is the form of the three types of raspers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the bone that breaks are to place it in later on the bone, and turn to your two sides until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the tare (taper) another place a little after, and so do it all around, then strike at the incisive space of the bone which is between the pertu (perforations), and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, just as we have said, until you pull out the bone with your hand, or any of the other instruments that you have, such as pliers, pincers.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and pulled it out, if it seems that there is something left behind on the bone at all other instruments resembling an incisive, but it must be more subtle and finer than the other incisions; and if there are no small bones or scales, pull them gently with one of the instruments; then treat the wound as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other kind of work is this: that the Gauls say, which is more true; and it is very strong, and this is their saying.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, at which or where the break opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, put the upper head of this incision beneath the lens-shaped curve, for it is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and it is the part damaged in two directions, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you cut lightly the bone all around, and be well guarded of the cloth under; if she is rough on the bone, cut the bone lightly, because cutting the bone without harm is better than without danger, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone break is not perforated by a thread, and only hit above, and there are small pieces, so it heals again in relation to that roughness, and remove the scutes at the razor-sharp tool which you must have various quantities for each patient as much as possible according to the work and figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use sharp razors and finer ones afterwards, and do not cease doing so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other type of fine hair cuts and delicate breaks, it is necessary to adapt the treatment according to its direction; and this is a thing that no one has replied to who put their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is uncovered, it is necessary to put a linen cloth soaked in oil rose, according to its quantity, on the wound; then take another cloth doubled twice or three times, and soak it in wine and oil rose, and put it over the first cloth; and do this lighter than you can, so that you do not burden the scab, but rather let it heal by itself. Then administer from above another bandage, and do not tighten it too much until the wound is healed alone; leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed down, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour of vinegar, powder of myrrh, and aromatics, and similar things. And make a powder of these things and put it on the wound, and administer afterwards medicinal medicine under mordicating; be careful that the wound is completely healed, so you do not leave any dressing or tie, for when the bow is tied tightly over the brain cloth, it corrupts and infects, and brings great harm to the patient; for when something is put on a scab, it becomes infected from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Wear your protective clothing then, since no mishaps will happen to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful before doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no mishaps come because of the medicine we have placed on it, which has virtue, then it is fitting that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue a cloth, and apply it to the wound; then do the cures in the manner of cures as it needs, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two bones of the neck are broken, or one alone, because it is two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, it is fitting that you pour your small oil or poultice on the bone, and put this broken piece inside your little finger index, and in a pouch to prevent, until the bone returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, so that the patient does not feel pain by your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and cannot come into place by itself, so that you put equal to the head of a small rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do it again and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; but if not, after the seventh or twelfth day, when the swellings are appeased, then apply a cloth of linen to the head of the nose, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you put the other of another part, if it is a break; and let the swellings be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And the restorers said that we must moisten the swellings in butter and move each one every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they are moist in their preparation of aubun and of powder of mill; then let the tent be, until the bones are hardened, and the cartilage be tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one is not necessary in the presence of ointment of goose fat, and if the wound is wrapped tight around it, and the patient holds still, then blow into him.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes while you are working on it, then apply hot oil or a moist cloth soaked in rose oil or vinegar poultice.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not come, apply a plaster made of flour of sesame, and powder of incense, mixed with aubun of beef, then put on light strips, and do not tie the ointment; and if the fracture is small, and it breaks into little pieces, if you have suitable instruments for that, then cut the wound, and treat the surrounding parts, and sewing, as suitable plasters and ointments are for that; and if there is no wound inside the abscess, then apply a cautery treatment, and put hot poultices on it, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	About the fracture of the jawbone.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured under the teeth, and there is no wound to conceal it, and the fracture occurs without breaking the bones in half, but only curving them within, if this is noticed lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is fitting that if the fracture occurs in the right side, you insert your two fingers into the mouth of the sick person; and if it occurs on the left jawbone, insert your right hand's index finger instead, push the fracture gently inside, and pull with the other hand to make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone occurs in the middle line (II), it is fitting to administer extension to both parts, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	In case of moving the teeth, or breakage, if you strain with a thread of gold or silver, or silk, then set on the broken mandible a sort of cloth, and put upon it a double drap; and put under the double drap a well-made peg, or piece of leather equal in length and width according to the mandible, and bind it above the molar that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve light viands.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, if you cast it away three times, and then put it back on what is changing; and apply plaster upon, with powder of flour from the mill mixed with abundance of egg or sement flour, after you have cut off the sortile; and put upon the plaster a light linen dress, and if the plaster dries, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it thus until he is healed; many are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If an abscessed finger comes, then do what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if it is both a fracture and a wound together, reward with no part of the bone left exposed, but with subtle instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then stretch it to its maximum according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have set all these bones in place and it does not remain for one instant, if the wound is large, then put on some suitable bandages to bind it, in order to heal quickly, until it is cured.
de la forcele	of the lump
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The lump breaks more than once over the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: either it is broken and separated in two parts, with fragments remaining, and this is the lightest to restore; or there is a break together with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Instruct the wounded so that when there is a fracture and an injury, you have two servants, one who holds the shoulder so that the broken limb feels the force of the break; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put equal the break to your fingers, so that the form becomes as it should, and there be no appearance or rough edge.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you have to stretch more, put under the shoulder of the wounded a round spear made of cloth or linen, so large as it suits your need; and stretch and lift the limb, and hold tight the spear in your hand, so that you put equal the break, just as it should.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot treat the head of the fracture due to the swelling, which is coming out from within, it is advisable that the patients lie on their back and place a pillow under the shoulder; and let the servant hold the spear beneath the shoulder, so that the bones of the fracture are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the break to your two sides, and if you find any debris, it is fitting that you cut them up; and take out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join again for any reason, if one of the incisions hits one of those points, but be careful with this instrument, in order to protect the wound.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it resembles a spoon, and is not made of cheese, and so is as large as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two ends, as you see, and one should be wide and the other narrow, just as with the roughness of the wound that you made when you cut the bones; and when you are sure about the location of the abscess, if it is small, or you doubt its size, then apply the dressing of drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms on his foot, so moistens it with rose oil, and ale, and wine, and applies.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is sensitive to pain and swelling, is that you put the bone on top of the plaster made from powder of flour and ale, and apply light bandages, and place a spear under the limb, if necessary; then take a great bandage, one palm in width, and apply double bandages above the plaster, and the plaster; then take a fine awl three fingers wide and long, and put it through the bandage, so that the chief of the bandage is hanging; and place the awl on the break, and turn the bandage up to the neck, and down to the limb, and pull from each part, and when you see that the limb holds the break, and you see clearly that the awl does not move over the broken bone, so apply it every day, and when the ligament is tight, release; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the joint, to lift the plaster upwards; in this way, the swelling of the break by the tension of the shoulder will alleviate itself, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it if any bad accident occurs, for twenty days; then reapply the plaster, if necessary, and tighten and release it thus, until he is restored; and she is restored in twenty-eight days, and less often than with other men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of a broken shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	There is no remedy for a broken shoulder that does not come from its own movement, and does not heal by touch alone; if you align it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways possible; then put powder made from wheat flour with many eggs, and fine needles, on the injured place; next, put a broad needle on top, about half an inch larger than the shoulder, and thread it through the flesh at any point of the shoulder so that the thread is tied in equal parts of stitches; and then bind tightly around a large bandage; so that the needle does not move from its place, and check the tie each day; and every time you loosen it, if necessary, tighten the needle again, and apply pressure to the injured spot; and the shoulder will be healed in twenty or twenty-five days. And when these numbers are completed, he may be sure, for it is not his own bone that has been put together lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of bone protrudes before and the skin over it is not healed, do as we have said in breaking open an abscess with a pointed instrument.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The piece is not broken in the middle but often occurs near it; and it breaks frequently without cause.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it breaks in the middle, it inclines downward and causes the patient great pain, and shortness of breath, and nausea, and sometimes vomiting; and because they open the vessels on the broken bone, and the sensation is much better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient sits up straight on his bed, and he puts a cloth between his shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the two breastbones with his hands, and tries to put them in order in all ways, so that the figure of the bone becomes as it should; then puts on plasters and bandages over the subtle part of salt, or another lighter material, and wraps him up in a sheet, and ties him to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turns the tie around to the back, and tightens it immediately, and rewards each hour with a bandage, and if he swells, tightens it; and if he wants to be untied, because of corrosion or prurite that comes to him, or pain or abscess, so take his leave, and remove the bandage, and shave the plaster, and direct those who have come from ways of treatment; then reapply the plaster, and tighten it until he is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the breast injury
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Which breast injuries occur only in the large afterpart of the back, and at the head within, and are bent only because they are fragile; and it is felt very much by the inquiry on both sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatments are that you put equal the injury, as it is suitable.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply plaster, and bind with a stake, if you have need.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breast injury inclines inward, it causes great pain to the patient, and piercing, like of pleurisy, because the bone pokes the membrane; and there is pain, swelling, vomiting, and great plant-like discharge of blood, and this is a sign of bad health, and the old ones have applied great force.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it should be administered food which fills the belly, to dislodge the fracture at will.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless an abscess has formed inside the flesh.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it is present, remove it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of them said that you should put vents (or poultices) on the limb to suck out pus, because it seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the vents do not attract the superfluities (excess fluids) in the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of them said that you should cover the limb with a moist linen in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the girth even, then treat by plucking, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the pain in the bone causes so much suffering that it cannot be endured by the patient, and doubt is at the patient, then it is advisable to break on the surface of the fractured rib, and it is advisable to insert a certain instrument to protect the abscess; and then one must trench the bone, and treat lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is great, and cure with poultices, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes in the flesh, then put on moist drapes in oil rose, and apply to it; and treat until the swelling of the limb that it is necessary for the abscess, and soaks down on the costal side where it must, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of a broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is no break when the bone of the neck breaks, and soon it happens that he cannot hold up; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens, and you see whether he will be sane or not, if you watch your hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move nor extend, and when you poke them with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Recognize that he is mortal in such other conditions, and if they are silent and feel well when you strain them tightly, recognize that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will recover, if you put him to treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing happens at the spine of the back, and you see whether he will be saved or not, if you watch carefully when his feet are softened, and when accidents occur in his hands, and when he makes movements and excretion with violence, and on your belly, he makes excretion with violence.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is sitting on his back and wants to go ahead, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is fatal if you do not work at his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	But if this happens to him, then it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward him if he has a burning abscess, if he puts on rose oil or oil of myrrh on his spine, until he is relieved; then put on one of the comfortable cloths and tie it with a rope, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not lie on that part where he feels pain, until he is cured.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is split open, it is fitting to cover the wound; and take out the bone, then reassemble the two lips of the wound, if they are large, with a suture, until he is cured; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "chiés de la kowe", put your left handbag pouch onto your right hand, and place it equal to your other hand's power, then put the cloth and nail on, if you have need; then bind it, and if the bone is split open again, take out the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the femur
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the femur bone is fractured, and if it has happened, then if it had occurred for a little while with some swelling at the head; let them lay it long, and incline to the padded side, and it will come to the patient pain in the place, pointing, and swelling as it broke.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you stretch out your hand over it, so much so that you are above the fracture; and search which ones are the fractures and how they look like; and if the fracture is only in the head alone, then set equal to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or declines inward, so that you rest the patient on their belly, until the restoration of that fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have put it in order, then place the plaster on top of it, and then put a stake of wood or bone on top, and hold the break tight so it does not move; and apply the plaster below the ribs, until the limb is ordered.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes on the foot, do not touch it, until the abscess is smoothed out, and put on what we have previously said; and then return to restoration, and hold tight as necessary, if there is no other injury; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The joints are that which is between the arm and the head of the shoulder, and if it is fractured, then one must restore it according to one of two methods: one of them being that you take a straight rod made of thin wood, of that shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Instruct the assistant to tie two strings around each joint, and let them rise up towards the head, and sit the patient on one side; then lay him down with broken arms upon the chest, until it comes to a stop, and has set in an armature of chest, then bend upwards over any heavy thing that the ministers extend downwards; then put the mires on the bruised joint together, so that the bruise returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that they place the patient on his back, and tie one hand to his neck; then instruct the two ministers to have each of them pull in opposite directions - one pulls upwards with the injured hand, and the other pulls downwards at all the joints.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then tie both below and above the joint, and stretch each of the ministers to their limit.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Et if the fracture is close to the shoulder of the arm, then you should put a straight line under the collarbone, and another one downwards towards the wound; and so if the fracture is near the shoulder, it is advisable to put a lighter bandage, without effort, until the fracture is even with its natural position, and with its normal place; then set the fracture as needed, and bind it, since there are no abscesses coming from that side.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come from that side, do not bind it before 7 days have passed, and put a moist linen on it in a warm place with olive oil, until the abscess is subsided; then bind it, and the way of binding it should be such that you put a plaster over the fracture, then assemble the arm to its shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or the chest; put a cloth on, and bind on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless any obstacle prevents it, or if the bones are moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone will move, use this method, and put a larger and stronger nail on the break, one space from each other, so that each nail is as large as it needs to pass through the break three times in each part; then strain on the nails, just like I said at the beginning of this chapter about the break.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the position of the nails and the straining, just as we have said, when restoring the broken limb, and you doubt the location of the abscess, if it is left to form for seven days, just like we have said; then look at each one of those seven days, in which no swelling or inflammation comes up, or any signs of necrosis come to the limb because it is too strained.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If so, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if such an accident does not happen, then do not dislocate it unless after three days or more, and let the patient lie on his back, and put his hands over his stomach; and place the aid beneath the cussion of one plain cloth of wool evenly, and watch each hour of the day or night, that the figure of the broken member does not move, or be loosened in its joints; then straighten the thing by virtue of medicine, and give him the meat which we have put before it, in a manner such that the meat is easily digested; and when he comes to recover, if it is hard.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the aid and the leg should be reset after forty days in all; and therefore he must be dislocated and administered baths and medicine for the joint.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is swollen and blocked, it must stay unbound for three days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fossicle", one small and one large; for the small one is the root of the pouchet; and the other is below, near the small bone; sometimes only the larger fossicle breaks, or the smaller, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, healing is light and easy, and recovery; when the large bone is broken, it is a poor recovery, and more grievous than if both had been broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, it must be extended slightly and put in place.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Instruct the patient to pull with greater force if it is a large ulcer; and stretch out towards the cussin, and lift the pouch of his hand higher than others, and the fingers lower than others, so that the patient crosses himself upon himself, and stretches towards the cussin even higher, lest the patient suffer no pain or labour; then extend one's arm with a swollen hand to the part below his hand, or on its joint, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the joints in equal form according to his best condition.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no surplus that can be grasped to restore it to its place, then make an incision and extract the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with a breakage there is an opening, I have spoken to the singular physician about it; so take the care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration a swelling occurs after an abscess, so that it is wrapped with a cloth made of cerote (or possibly tar) made from oil and white wax, which is not too hard nor too soft; then tie the cloth above subtlety, until the swelling is appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then take away the cerote, and put on the plaster made of powder from the mill with a lot of water, so that it is applied to the arrows, and let one arrow be fixed over the break, somewhat stronger and wider than the others; and know that there should be six arrows or more in such dispositions: either if the breakage is in one bone, or in two; and tighten more above the breakage than elsewhere, and always less when moving, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the drapes that are on top of the break be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the fillets, from which it is strained, be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accidents happen to the limb, so that it itches and hurts as before, you must soak the limb in hot water until the itching is alleviated; and let the limb not be too cramped to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the tightening, and if the joints are loosened and the bones softened, and it seems like that is the case, adjust.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you cannot ward off the swelling from coming to the limb because it is too tightened, then it is advisable to loosen it a little, and let it be so for some days, until the swelling clears up, and then tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If none of these things we have mentioned come to pass for the patient, then it is safe to release them after 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if he requests that his hands be put on his neck, and they are made even, and he is warded off from movement and digitation, and sleeps on his back; then it can be seen that the injury has been restored in thirty days or forty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the nature of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of a hand break
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	It can be seen that the back of the hand has few breaks, and only pain occurs many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And if the finger of the hand is broken or sprained, it is advisable for the patient to sit cross-legged, with his back straight in front of him equally; then he puts his injured hand on a flat surface, and extends the jointed fingers, and sets the broken bones equal, until they are well aligned; and applies the plaster and poultices, unless there is inflammation; then he places an arrow according to the quantity of the wound; and it is covered with one sheet of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	In case of a fracture in the tendons around the belly of the foot, do thus: make a bowstring from cloth and command the patient to bind it to his broken foot; then bind with a long rope, so that the strap is as big as the tendon on the hand, and tie it tightly, just as one should.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the finger, it is fitting that you put a strap above and below the foot, so that the fingers are bent and straight; then tie all around the hand, and tighten the chain between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of us on the fingers, and it is swollen, so that you make it even, then tie it as seems fitting; and bind with the foot, and if you see, put a straight little strap to lift the fracture, and not move; and if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or any others, make it even, and bind with the good finger that is next; or tie all the fingers at once, as seems valuable, or put a strap on it, as you have said; be careful in restoration and placement of the abscess, and cure those who come to you, just as I have told.
de la cuixe brisie	The body breaks
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the body is often broken, and one can see it when she turns before and behind; and the restoration is thus as one ties above the break, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients swell on their face, then stretch out each of these ministers equal to his part; and it is thus when the break meets the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the body, so it is one of the ligaments near the finger, and the others near the break.
