Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, and thus one of the ligaments near the knee or the other below the break; then put the splints the bone equal to its two hands, so long as it be in accordance with its natural figure, and then apply plaster, and the bandage, so that abscess does not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess on his body, so let him calm it down then return to his work and his treatment; the remedy is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap a strip of cloth around the fracture with two fingers or more doubled, and keep superfluous fluid, then turn the leg so that the toes reach to the root of the nail, and pour one long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and veer upwards the head of the thread to above; then turn up the leg and above the thigh the strip, then put a splint on the fracture, and put an anchor on the bone of the leg; then use soft drapes between the leg and the thigh to tighten the binding, then start to tie in form III or four above the fracture; and as you go higher on the fracture, and less will bind it; then take out the two heads of the thread that have been poured between the leg and the thigh, and put three anchors above, then return below to the head of the thread, until you see beneath the foot; and if the binding does not move from its place, then let it be so, then when there will come no abscess or inflammation or other signs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, if the joint dislocates, and addresses itself in that way, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of bone that grasp, let them be cut off, if possible; and if it cannot be, then break the limb and apply force; and do the cure as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the chest broken in such a way that we insert nails, as in the arm or shoulder joint; all the time, after this restoration, the patient does not recover.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it has been observed that the chest is restored in three days, or a little more or less, according to the diversity of the patient's complexion.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin ditch
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	The thing to cut with fire commands the sick man to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, but only to an opening or a split, and the pain is felt in all the wound and the pain, and so much is felt inside.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by placing equal on those who are blind to their right and left, until they are assembled and can be; then apply plaster, and put a rounded bell if you have need, and bind it as it should be done, then follow all the dispositions that we have said about other breaks, similar to abscesses and other appearances; for each accident apply what is necessary, until he is cured.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Knowing that in the leg there are two bones, namely the "right" one called "mustelz", and the other called "foscile"; and just like any other fracture it comes to the arm, therefore the restoration is done equally as with the arm, and the treatment is all the same. And if both two bones are broken together, then turn the leg in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bones are broken, they turn towards.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen clearly; and turn below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And therefore apply extension, and set it equal, and tie the stitches equally; but be careful, if the break is crooked, and there are more pieces, that the extension may not be too little and very light; but apply according to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et when you have completed all of your work, take two handfuls of fustian threads that color the leg from one side and the other, and are as long as the length of the leg from the groin to the knee; then sew them in both above and below, and tie it at the middle, so that the leg will not bend to the right or left, and thus is good; and none should administer this to both hands of the leg, and if it's made of fustian, and it puts on the leg to prevent movement, then properly done it in the break where there was a wound; and move each one every day the leg, to see if it has an abscess or other accident; so that the healer should continue until he is sane.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no breakage, but sometimes at the two feet bone comes a breakage and does so little, and it has only once more severe condition.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If it has a breakage at the two feet bone and you see these bones protruding one on top of the other, so put this patient's foot on the ground, just like when he would walk, and then put your foot on his, where they are lifted up, then press them together until they align in their own place; then apply a plaster and bandages over, and put an iron staple under the foot joint, afterwards tie around it tightly, and other things that you may have need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four will have passed, if you release the bandage, because you will find that the bones are aligned, whether they are broken, or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any broken bones, then set them straight again, as I have said about the broken bones of the hand; then put a pin into each broken bone according to its length, and make it slightly larger, then place on top of that the foot that is flat and square as I said; and in the end, strain them.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things I have said about other breaks, from now on; and heal each accident as it is fitting.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone at the finger joint
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, if it enlarges, then incline it to the back of the spine, and hold it there behind; then fill the pit with wool of the patient's countenance, and put as much into it as into my own; then bind the woman, and lift her back little by little, and when she begins to come out, the bone comes with it too; and when she wants to urinate, if the cotton comes out, and when she has urinated, return to it, and do this for seven days or more: then the break will be restored, and if you see, take a container of wool, and tie the perforated one a cord, and pour all the vessel into the nature; then blow into the cord until the vessel is emptied inside: the nature will come back to the break; then fill with cotton, and let it stay like this for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the arm or the hand is broken, as in the case of the shinbone; and these near fractures are not hidden from him who applies his study and use, and has read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaking signifies more deaths on the straight path of restoration; then therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the phallus, when it is broken, take a goose gourd and pour the phallus into it; then envelop it in cloth, and let it be three days or four days, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaking with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has a breaking with wound, especially if it is great, such as the bone of the shoulder or arm, or similar, that he be healed now, if the remedies we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the wound is clean, and you have no other option, then restart the breaking of the fracture in the same hour, or on the following day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess does come, then wait until the next day to restart the restoration, as long as the abscess is relieved, and do not touch it or on the second day or the fourth, for you would do a bad and unfortunate accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the broken bone appears on the surface of the uncovered wound, it is advisable to put it at an angle slightly towards your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the extension is not suitable to put at an equal angle to your hands, if there is this instrument of iron, which has seven or eight fingers long, and the width varies according to the size of the wound; and so it is a matter for the surgeon to apply three or four, according to what he needs in each case of fracture; and be thin and not very thick, that it does not bend under compression on the limb at your work, and be thick at the front, and one finger thick from the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the curved knife must be placed on top of the bent bone of the skull; and let him swallow once, until he returns to normal, and they must be even in front and back.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the splinters cannot well take hold of the bone, it is advisable to copy the skull bone, so that the splinters may have a chance.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone as we have said, then, with the available instrument, whether it is cutting or needle-like or superior, try your best; and take out what is left stuck in the bone, rough and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it indicates that he is not in his natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Si fai tant qu'il soit en son leu,
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is severe or great and you doubt that more accidents will happen as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, if it cannot be put on a splint; but wrap tightly around it, in its place, tight bandages, and tie.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two days to come the bowels have been at the wound, if that which you have put on top of it is vinegar, and ointment for healing wounds, just as ointment has four virtues and is similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary that you move the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it becomes warm and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary to bind the limb in a certain way so that the bowel moves down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they touch the fire cautery every day, and it cannot be stitched but repeatedly torn apart by bowstring, see how small pieces of bone there are, because it is necessary to want to treat the wound with care, and remove all these useless pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess comes to the limb, or another kind of corruption, it is advisable that you treat it, according to what he has said in his previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and opens on the limb, just as the bone of the elbow or shoulder, and other similar bones in the great members, do not neglect it, because many times death comes from it, but let it be for a while until it can cause him to lose weight; by chance he will die after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if you can, and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of those who come from the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the health of an injury, especially when it is near a joint, and a terrible thing to see the shape of the member; and by chance it cannot make the members their natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care that it is fresh: if you administer medicinal remedies such as aloes, incense, and mirror, and saffron, and other similar things, just as you pick up any of these or all together, and mix with vinegar or wine or asafoetida; and put on a poultice and tie well, and do not release it in your hands for days; then remove the poultice, and repeat another one until the nodules are removed; or apply to a piece of pounce well made: for the property of pounce is that it removes all swellings from members; and if the nodulation has become hardened like stone, just as hard as bone, and it is necessary to remove it, so take off half above, and make the swelling apparent; or you can take it to anyone who will shave it, until it is removed, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A limb that is weak after the battle.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and stays in place after the weak limb and subtle movement, there may be for many reasons: because one is due to being too tightly tied, and was not tied as he wanted it; or because there are too many ties, and cannot come to the member's proper movement; or because of multiple arrow shootings; or because of excessive movements, neither in its hour nor in its rest; or because it has little blood in his body, so weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you will make the patient eat, and make his body soft, until there are no more multiplicities in him; and administer bath, and give joy and delight to the sick man; then apply poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great movement, and the arrow shoots frequently from watered-down blood, until the movement reaches the limb; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A dislocated limb after recovery.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after recovery, and the bones are broken apart, and the form of the limb is ugly, all things should be returned to their natural state: do not believe fools who say one must break the limb anew; for many fools have done this in our land, and these wounds are blamed, and from them come great harm, and sometimes death. Therefore, if the nodulations and tortures are fresh, it is advisable to treat them with hot water or herbs cooked in a way similar to that of willow bark, and roots, and mallow, and similar things; and apply the mollifying poultice as one does with aqua-vitae well done, and take the muscillaige of willow bark, and mix it with lard or sesame oil, and apply the poultice on it; or take fatty figs, grind them with fine flour of millet, and similar medicines that alleviate the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes is removed the nodulation due to continuous and prolonged friction with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And so move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted part is hardened and aged, like stones, and it needs to be heated with iron, then if they want to cover just on top of the bone, at the subtle incision slightly; and put a cushion and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in anyone, if they want to now bring back into place carefully.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the cauteries of dislocations on the lower joints just below the knee.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	And it happens that the jaws are displaced upwards, and the dislocations of both jaws occur in two ways: either they are a little osteedematous from their own joints, and softened a little; or they are completely displaced, hanging towards the chin, and causing difficulty to swallow saliva so that he can neither hold his mouth closed nor close his lips, and is overcome by his words with his tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns in multiple ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and completed, then you must immediately reset it, and do not hesitate; and in such a manner that the ministrants take hold of the chief of the sick person, and give him some medicine in one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other two fingers are held back to make it even; and instruct the patient to release his jaws, and move them from all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	The doctor puts an equal amount of medicine, as long as it regains its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	But if the joint is still swollen, especially when it's the two lower mandibles joined together, apply cold water and oil so that it settles lightly; do not force it to return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned to their place and the swollen mouth is freed with malleafier [likely a malleable material], apply moist cloths in rose oil and beeswax, then lightly bind them with soft linen; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his shoulders between two cushions, so that he does not move or lift his arm or his shoulder, nor try to straighten it, but take gentle food until the pains are gone and the mandibles are freed; and then gently take what he wants to eat, and do not struggle to open his mouth to swallow, until the mandible is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not converted to their normal position, then fever, sweating, and accustomed vomiting will occur, and by chance, stomach troubles and nausea may happen, and by chance, one might vomit blood.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it's a sign of bad omen; and many die within seven days.
de la forcelle	of the wrist.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The wrist cannot dislocate towards the chest and inside the forearm and towards the fingers, and is not able to return to its normal position at all, and it's clearly felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient must lie on his back, and extend his arms; then press the wrist to his palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it; and the joint that was displaced towards the shoulder cannot dislocate again; if not, and if it does dislocate at all, so it is reset in its place, just as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus, the joints of the spine are also brought back into place when they are displaced.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways the shoulder dislocation can occur: when it happens below the joint at the bottom of the arm; or when it occurs near the knee; and by chance, sometimes it also happens above, which is rare; and this does not happen behind the shoulder or within the body; and more frequently, it dislocates downwards towards the joint, in exactly those who have little strength, because at that instant they will suffer an immediate fall; whereas those who have sufficient strength will stumble upon a stone.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance this happens to some men, who percuss or break it, and swell the shoulder with an inflamed abscess, and think that it is a dislocation.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary therefore that you examine it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they are fallen towards the socket, and you will find a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among their diversity manifest signs; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the socket in the neck the head of the shoulder, just as it would be in either case; and the patient cannot bring back his hand to its normal position, nor move from any movement; and similarly, if she is fallen above, then she is not hidden, because you will find manifestly at the neck; and this kind of dislocation is not hard to correct when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	Instruct the patient to lift his arm upwards with the hand, then put his fists downwards on the wound, and lift the joint at force in the upper part of the limb; and the minister lifts the hand, and extends it upwards, because he puts it downwards; so if there is an immediate result.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we said four days later, it is advisable to bathe the patient in hot water; and minister him a gentle purgative and soothing, like a decoction of alum and fenugreek and millet in hot water, and administer it; then sit the patient on his back, and put a cloth downwards on the wound with an equal thickness, neither too soft nor too hard, then place his mire ( perhaps a poultice?) on the cloth, and lift the shoulder joint gently, and treat the patient's arm; and another minister lifts the patient's head, so that it does not move after; this shoulder will return to its normal state, and if you see it, make sure it is reduced according to this manner: and do that a man be present who is greater than the patient; and stand upright towards the cost (shoulder), and pour water out of the wound on the patient's shoulder, and lift the joint up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister treats the patient's arm downwards towards the ventre (belly).
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then lift with him any heavy thing, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also done in another way: and it's as if you throw a long iron bar into the ground, so that the shoulder joint is made like a piston, neither too big nor too small; then put it under the patient, but when they have soft skin above, and the patient has their arm straight on the long wooden stick; then extend their hand downwards from another side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to come back for all these things that we have said, do this cure: take an iron bar of two arms' length and four fingers wide, which has the head turned in towards the middle, going under the bone, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Instruct the patient to lie under the head of the broken fist, so that it does not strike the face of the sick one; then place the arm below the bone of the sick one. And stretch out some fingers on the fist of long hair, and tie the assistant on the fist, and the arm to the shoulder of the hand, then place the arm under a pinched wheel of an enlarged side, and let the hands down, and let the body hang from another part: the joint will be straight now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in that state, whatever manner it may be, it is advisable to put under the bone an iron spear of wool equal, then place the plaster applied with powdered mill on flax, with incense and with salt of bees, on all the shoulder and around; then strip from under the bone immediately, and turn the tie on the plaster, and tie the hand to its neck, and so let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is fitting that you apply poultice often, until the limbs are comforted, because he will heal faster; and then apply more after five days or seven, and move him; and if he is firm and not softened, then he is cured.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is broken due to moisture that has occurred, or for another reason, it is fitting that you administer cauterization at three punctures, as he is placed in front of the cauterizing instrument.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and the joint dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot lift any arm up, then you should know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder has been bruised or stretched out or softened; and you should know that the joint was never properly fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs near the elbow and knees, or behind, is done by impulse and stretching of hands, and one must provide another binding; and care until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes to grief in the limb, and slow movement, then the patient takes many baths, until that grief is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder cut.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	It is known that the shoulder joint is often displaced at points, and returns to its original state; and if it has been displaced from all parts, and also in front of and behind, and the dislocations are not easily replaced, because one can see them well and feel them well; and displacement according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick limb to the healthy one, so it is clearly visible.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor press against the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And therefore it must be set straight again, so that an abscess forms there, for if an abscess forms there, then the setting will cause grief; and by chance it cannot be set straight at all, especially when it is in the back part; this one is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance death may come.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is done when it can be returned to its former state, so that you extend your two hands; and his arms are stretched out, and his hands soft as possible according to the wound on both sides, and pull the joint into its sockets or to the root of his palm, until it revives in its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if there is a dislocation before it, so that when he doubles his hand to his hand, and proud of the palm's root which is displaced.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not return to his normal state, so that one minister extends the arm and tightens both wrists, and two ministers extend the other arm and tighten both wrists, so that it will not move with extension; then turn the arm from each side, when you have wrapped a double-length rope around it, and when the joint touches a joint in its hand, push against any oil to smooth out the joint, then bind the joint tightly until it becomes normal again; and when it is returned to normal, place a plaster of flour with water on top of the collarbone with the patient's neck, and let it remain for some days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the ligament and let it go; and if you see that the joint does not hold tight well, then reapply the plaster and the ligament, and let it go like so for some days, until it is firmly fixed; then let it go.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the return of the joint, and it is quiet, then bathe him well and rub him gently, and press until he becomes calm; or place on the joint a piece of fatty mutton fat, then let it be for one day and one night, then remove, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, then rub the joint temperately, then put back the fat, and then enter the bath again; and thus do two or three times, until he is healed; and if you see that, put on a warm moist poultice with butter and stretch it on; if he returns to his former condition.
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and if it returns lightly, it is better than other joints. To return it to its place immediately in the same spot where it was dislocated, so that the swelling subsides or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And if the return is that you put the diseased hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the other hand, and straighten the wrist, so that he puts his palm over the appearance of the joint, and press it down until it returns to its place. Then, observe whether it is well in its place; afterwards, have the sick man put his back against a table at extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, he puts the sick person's back against his own hand on the table, and stretches out his other hand to touch the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, that is good. If not, if the strain of apothecaries soothes the abscesses and he lets him do so again in this manner.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it and you can't put him back after some days, the joint will be twisted; and there's no remedy for the patient other than so much that his hands are numb, and he can't strain anything more: then see that the nerves have been cut, or the arteries; since there is nothing else to do except to strain with cautery on the case, and perhaps it's worth nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when his hands are put back, then put on the poultice that we have said, apply the strain and let him rest for a day, then remove it and let him do so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no pain, apply the damp cold water, and rub him so that he becomes healthy.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the joint of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	They are dislocated at either joint of the hand, or sometimes on the back of the palm or the belly; therefore it is necessary to identify and reset the joint. Then hold the head of the joint tightly until it comes into place, and direct it towards the part where it is dislocated; and let it stay there for two days, then set it equal again that day; and tie up the wound as we have said, and release it every day, and make it move again, and tie it back. Do this repeatedly until it tightens, and do so also if it is dislocated on the other part of the hand, and do it just like before, until he becomes healthy; and do the same thing when it is dislocated in another joint.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	When dislocation of the shoulder occurs from a fall
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or the neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, if there is no treatment, because death quickly takes the patient.

And the signs are that the dislocation cannot be held in place, nor can it be sustained, and many times a member becomes soft or both knees or both arms become weak; and often the dislocated limb remains four parts: one who falls to the back is called "gilbositez", the cure believes if gilbositz has come from birth: if there is no treatment or healing.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of cures were spoken in great words, with no particular gain; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I dis that in the goutiness that comes to the toe in front, no remedy is found; and similarly when it comes directly in two places, and cannot be cured with fire only those that come properly to the back, as I said; and it is because the patient lies on his face in one place and has a strain below him, so he does not bleed; then strike one beam at the head in the ground, and another at the pie, and tie one rope behind the ankles of the sick person, and another behind the knees and groins, and the two servants will know how to tie the ropes, one at the head and the other at the pie, among the two beams; and they should be well closed, like we have said, and the mires should put his palms on the point of the spear in form, until it returns.

And when she does not return by this cure, take a table of three long arms, and place it beneath her in that way, and let the patient lie on his side, and pour the chief of the table under her belly; then put the middle of the table on the spine; and put your mires on the other chief of the table, and press well, until she returns to the right; and if you see it, do so at the turnet which turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And place two thorns on the chief of one arm of the patient, and between each pair of thorns, over and under, an open palm width of long wood; and have in each thorn a small puncture or the turnet moves, so that it is firmly rooted in the earth, not moving; and between each two thorns have one thorn turning, because they turn together, and have in each pair two thorns of an open palm width to turn the turnet; and then tie the turnet which is between the joints to the chief, and the other tie to the feet to the other turnet, and each minister turns its turnet along the entire joint, and the masters will put the spine straight as we have said.

des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the thigh
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Things that happen only to the thigh and shoulder joints are dislocations alone, not in other joints; and the joint of the thigh is displaced in four parts: inside and outside, before and behind; and more so inside them, and less so before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And if a person with dislocation of the joint inside is known by this: when you join the sick leg to the healthy one, they are longer and more open in the joints of the sick than those of the healthy person; and the sick cannot double their knee on fire; and it is the ones who are nearest the groin that come from the abscess hot, because the head of the shoulder comes loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who suffers from this disease is such that this injury is contrary to the front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who suffers from this when they come to the front are such that he stands well on his leg according to the completion; all his joints ache, not doubleing the knees in pain, and if it is made to walk, he cannot, retains his urine, and swells his groin, and when he urinates, passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who suffers from this when it happens behind are such that he cannot expand his knees, nor double them, and that leg is crooked more than the other, and his groin is softened, and there are pain in the heel bones below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this similar appearance of dislocation are such that if you repair the injury when the dislocation is old and it lingers according to its nature, without any cure; and it should not be presumed that he has the condition.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this where the dislocation is fresh, and it's of four kinds of dislocation, so hasten that you return to the joint, and put it inside and outside, and it will move on both hands and on the left hand; by chance if it returns, and there needs no other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, so you should apply strong force, and put the leg strongly on both hands, or tie it to the knee; and some other ministers do stretch one hand above in such a way that they pour their hands under their seats, then tighten them with a strong thread over the flank; and some others tie the head to the ligature; and all extend up and down once, until the patient is lifted out of the ground once, and stays.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of stretching is common with four signs, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is true.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	But if this is not the case, it is best to apply treatment to its appearance When dislocations are at the shoulder, it is best that you lift the patient on their side so that they rest comfortably, then put a bandage on the base of the scapula, and the one that is under the angle, then tighten the bandage towards the angle, and towards the armpit; then take other assistants to hold the large bandage of the sick arm, and stretch it away from the fault: if it returns to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	But if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, it is best to tie the two feet and two knees of the sick person together with a strong bandage above the two ankles, and above the two knees; then let the leg be stretched twice as much as the other limbs; then hang them from the top of a beam, and higher than the ground, two arms of wood; then command to one minister that he takes hold of the scapula, and let another ministers stand with the sick person, who take hold together, forming the scapula, because the joint returns soon.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when dislocations are beyond repair, the patient is given medicine, as we have said in the case of gout, and the artery is strained above the diseased leg, and on the flesh as well; then two stakes are placed, one at the head and one at the other joint, then a stake is driven between the knee bones of the sick man, according to his form; and wet cloths are applied around, that he may not bleed, then each of these attendants stretches towards him, and ties the dislocation with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it comes back, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on a bed, and press as we have said in the case of gout, and give medicine to the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocations occur before, you must stretch the diseased leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and place the patient's pain above the angina of the diseased joint, then press with the other hand, and extend all the way down to the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocations are outside, you must not stretch the diseased leg down, nor lift it up from the ground, but rather it should be so that the joint is as if it had been displaced outside, as we have said when lying on the two joints; and its face should be above, and the ligament extended as we have said before, and one must press firmly on the joint at the table; and will be at point when the diseased person extends their legs, and they are even; then add the splints, and apply the plaster, and tie with a bandage, so that the joint does not move; and if it rests for three days or four, then take off the splint, and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, apply the strain as before, and let it rest for three days; then take off the splint, and have the person walk well, until their limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the shoulder joint dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The groin is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; but not before.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg to his groin, and if it does not return to its place, know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back under his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take hold of his groin in your hands, and press between your two, then bend both sides of the groin form; and another minister extends his foot, until the groin returns to its place, and the sign is that he can easily return his leg to its place; and apply plaster to it, and make the leg warm against the groin for three days or four, and then release him; and do not work on the patient while he walks, until his limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	If the limbs are not at all, then extend a great force, as we have said in the treatment of the hemlock, until they become sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	of foot dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The feet are sometimes swollen and sometimes completely dislocated, and within and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and tight, and pressing against the part where it is dislocated: the remedies if so are lighter, and one must extend lightly to their hands when only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, it is best to sit the patient upright, and press firmly by the leg, above the ankle; then take hold of the foot in your right hand, and then in your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and pour the foot upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, pouring and taking out the foot; if it returns, it is well; if not, if it recurs, because it will return; and if it cannot return so, sit the patient on his back on the ground, and firmly fasten the splint between his knees, and tie cloths tightly around him, so that he does not bleed; then press the tendons of the knee, and other tendons extend the foot to his hands or to its binding, as it is bound above the neck of the foot; then extend each tendon equally, and the splints should be stuck between the knees of the patient to hold him when one tends; then put equal mires on the dislocation at his hands, and other tendons press the healthy leg down, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it happens to be set in place, so he puts the plaster and poultices on top of it, and the strain forms, and ties the foot to the leg, and guards the tendons that are above the ankle, so that the ligament is not too tight; then he leaves him for two days or three days, and if the straining continues, he applies the poultice; then he frees him on the fourth day or a quarter, and waits for four days before sending the patient again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to a head, so it must be calmed, as we have said elsewhere, until he is safe.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two bones are dislocated, they must be stretched out in due course, and it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient if the dislocation is in neither of the joints on the back of the foot or on the ankle, you should seat him on a level surface either on the plain floor or on the table straight, and put your foot upon that which opens from these joints; then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is equalized and there is nothing open, place under the plant of the foot a table for two fingers, then form an arch, and leave him three days, then take away the bandage; and make him rest, until he be healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you try to restore it, many patients die; do not be presumptuous in the treatment, unless you are wise in the art and have used it long, and if you are not kind, merciful, and slow to act, do not be harsh; use soothing measures at the beginning of things, to clean out abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands, unless you see no chance of recovery; and when you see hope, now straighten the member as soon as possible, so that the abscesses heal; and when the limb is straightened, administer soothing measures again, and treat the wound as it requires, using dry bandages; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are broken, set them, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will be your reward, according to your Creator, and for the skill with which you are armed and your body.
Amen	Amen
